What Is Mantiq?
beginner
5 min
The Scope of Theory of Knowledge
Author defines theory of knowledge and summarizes scholarly views on its scope.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key components of theory of knowledge as described by the author and summarize the differing scholarly views on its scope.

Core Idea
Theory of knowledge covers all aspects of human knowing, from source to limits to subject-object relation.

This passage sets out to clarify what theory of knowledge (nazariyyat al-ma'rifa) actually studies. You will encounter multiple scholarly opinions—some narrow, some broad. The passage argues for a comprehensive, unified view. By working through this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the different elements that make up this field and see how they fit together.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial comprehensive definition
Locate the first sentence where the author lists all aspects: principles, nature, source, methods, value, limits, subject-object relation, and correspondence to reality.
This is the author's starting point for the discussion.
2
Find the first alternate view
Some scholars restrict theory of knowledge to just the relationship between the knowing subject and the known object. Identify this view.
This view narrows the scope significantly.
3
Find the second alternate view and the critique of each
Some argue that the first definition (focus on source, value, limits) should be called 'critique of knowledge' instead of 'theory of knowledge'. Others consider the second definition (subject-object only) as an imaginary inquiry. Locate these.
These critiques challenge the naming and scope of the field.
4
Note the added view about means of knowledge
Some scholars add the investigation of means of knowledge—whether innate or acquired. Identify this addition.
This expands the scope further.
5
Synthesize the author's conclusion
The author concludes that all these aspects are properly part of theory of knowledge and should be treated as a unified system, even if terms vary. Understand why the author argues for this comprehensive view.
The author emphasizes unity over terminological disputes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا كانت تلك هي معاني النظرية، فإن نظرية المعرفة تبحث في مبادئ المعرفة الإنسانية وطبيعتها ومصدرها ،وطرائقها وقيمتها وحدودها، وفي الصلة الذات المدركة والموضوع المدرك، وبيان إلى أي مدى تكون فيه تصوراتنا مطابقة لما يؤخذ فعلاً، مستقلاً عن الذهن)) (4) .
و حصرها البعض في إطار البحث في العلاقة بين الذات العارفة والموضوع المعروف (۱). وهناك من يرى أن تعريفها على الوجه الأول، بمعنى أنها البحث في مصدرها وقيمتها وحدودها.... إلخ يستدعي تسميتها بـ ((نقد المعرفة) لا ((نظرية المعرفة))(۲).
وأما تعريفها على الوجه الثاني فقد دعا بعض الفلاسفة إلى اعتبار ذلك مبحثاً وهمياً (۳). وثمة من يضيف إلى ذلك كله أن من مهامها أيضاً البحث في وسائل المعرفة من حيث فطريتها واكتسابها ( ٤ ) .
والحق أن جميع ذلك مما تتناوله نظرية المعرفة في مباحثها، والأولى أن يؤخذ نسقاً واحداً للنظرية وإن ترادفت بعض المصطلحات، أو عبر عنها بصيغ مختلفة.
If those are the meanings of theory, then theory of knowledge examines the principles of human knowledge, its nature, its source, its methods, its value, and its limits, and the relationship between the perceiving subject and the perceived object, and the statement of to what extent our conceptions correspond to what is actually taken, independent of the mind. And some confined it to the framework of investigating the relationship between the knowing subject and the known object. And there are those who see that defining it in the first sense, meaning that it is the investigation of its source, value, and limits... etc., necessitates calling it 'critique of knowledge' not 'theory of knowledge'. As for defining it in the second sense, some philosophers have considered it an imaginary investigation. And some add to all that that among its tasks is also the investigation of the means of knowledge in terms of their innateness and acquisition. And the truth is that all of that is covered by theory of knowledge in its investigations, and it is better to take it as a single system for the theory, even if some terms are synonymous or expressed in different forms.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage defines the scope of theory of knowledge (nazariyyat al-ma'rifa). It begins by establishing that theory of knowledge studies the principles, nature, source, methods, value, and limits of human knowledge, as well as the relationship between the knowing subject and the object known, and the correspondence of our conceptions to reality independent of the mind. The author then presents different scholarly views: some restrict it to the relationship between subject and object; others argue that if it focuses only on source, value, and limits, it should be called 'critique of knowledge' rather than 'theory of knowledge'; some philosophers consider the second definition (focus on subject-object relation) to be an imaginary inquiry. Another view adds the investigation of means of knowledge (innate vs. acquired). The author concludes that all these aspects are properly part of theory of knowledge, and it is best to treat them as a unified system, even if terms vary.

Key Terms
نظرية المعرفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT part of the scope of theory of knowledge as the author concludes?
A) Principles of human knowledge
B) Relationship between subject and object
C) Derivation of legal rulings
D) Means of knowledge (innate vs. acquired)

Key Takeaway
Theory of knowledge is a comprehensive discipline covering principles, source, methods, value, limits, subject-object relation, and means of knowledge; scholars differ on its exact scope, but the author advocates a unified view.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
List the components of theory of knowledge as given in the first definition. For each component, provide an example from Islamic sciences (e.g., source: revelation and reason; method: ijtihad).
?
Compare the two main definitions (comprehensive vs. subject-object only). Which definition better suits the needs of usul al-fiqh? Justify your answer in one paragraph.

What Is Mantiq?
intermediate

The Integrated Scope of Nazariyya al-Ma'rifa
Defines nazariyya al-ma'rifa and argues for an integrated approach.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the core components of nazariyya al-ma'rifa and explain why the author treats them as a unified field.

Core Idea
Nazariyya al-ma'rifa is a unified field covering source, value, limits, means, and subject-object relation.

This lesson examines various definitions proposed for nazariyya al-ma'rifa and shows why the author insists on a single comprehensive framework. By understanding these definitions, you will see how Islamic epistemology integrates multiple aspects of knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Extract the four definitions
Read the passage and list the four different ways scholars have defined nazariyya al-ma'rifa: (1) limited to subject-object relation, (2) focused on source/value/limits (calling it critique of knowledge), (3) considered an imaginary subject, (4) includes means of knowledge (innate vs acquired).
The definitions are marked with footnote numbers.
2
Identify the author's preferred view
Find the sentence beginning with 'والحق أن جميع ذلك...' and summarize why the author argues for a unified framework rather than adopting any single definition.
3
Reflect on the implications
Consider why a unified approach might be important in Islamic epistemology. How does it prevent fragmentation of knowledge discussions?
Think about how this applies to fields like usul al-fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الأول: الفصل الثاني- التعريفات
و حصرها البعض في إطار البحث في العلاقة بين الذات العارفة والموضوع المعروف (۱). وهناك من يرى أن تعريفها على الوجه الأول، بمعنى أنها البحث في مصدرها وقيمتها وحدودها.... إلخ يستدعي تسميتها بـ ((نقد المعرفة) لا ((نظرية المعرفة))(۲).
وأما تعريفها على الوجه الثاني فقد دعا بعض الفلاسفة إلى اعتبار ذلك مبحثاً وهمياً (۳). وثمة من يضيف إلى ذلك كله أن من مهامها أيضاً البحث في وسائل المعرفة من حيث فطريتها واكتسابها ( ٤ ) .
والحق أن جميع ذلك مما تتناوله نظرية المعرفة في مباحثها، والأولى أن يؤخذ نسقاً واحداً للنظرية وإن ترادفت بعض المصطلحات، أو عبر عنها بصيغ مختلفة.
نظرية المعرفة والإبستمولوجيا (Epistemology)
وإذا تقرر أن نظرية المعرفة تتناول كل ما سبق فإلى أي مدى تلتقي مع الإبستمولوجيا الغربية؟
تجدر الإشارة ابتداء إلى أن الدراسات الإبستمولوجية إذ تتناول بالتحليل والنقد نتائج العلوم الطبيعية منها ،والإنسانية كإحدى اهتماماتها الرئيسة، فإنها تعني بذلك نوعاً من (فلسفة العلوم (). وبمعنى أوسع فإن من الممكن اعتبار الإبستمولوجيا نوعاً من الفلسفة العامة بوصفها إحدى المباحث الثلاثة للفلسفة: الوجود (ontology) والقيم (Axiology) وكذلك المعرفة (Epistemology). ولكن ذلك لا يعني جواز استخدام مصطلح فلسفة المعرفة باعتباره مرادفاً لنظرية المعرفة كما ذهب إلى ذلك بعض الباحثين (۱) ، وحيث إن الأولى تبحث قضية المعرفة بصورة عامة، في حين أن الثانية تبحث في طبيعتها ومصادرها وإمكان الحصول عليها أو حدودها فحسب وعليه فإن استخدام المصطلحين على نحو من الترادف مجانبة للصواب، وتوسع في غير مقامه.
أما معنى الإبستمولوجيا (Epistemology) تحديداً فقد عرفها قاموس وبستر الجديد (Webster's New Collegiate Dictionary) على أنها إدراك المعرفة والحصول عليها كمعرفة، ودراسة، مرجعيتها، وحدودها، ومدى مصداقيتها). وهي بهذا المعنى امتداد لنظرية المعرفة في العربية إلى أقصى حد. بيد أن معجم الفلسفة والدين (Dictionary of Philosophy and Religion) أرجعها إلى أصلها اليوناني. إذ هي مقطعين يونانيين هما (Episteme) وتعني المعرفة أو العلم، و(logos) وتعني المعرفة أو المعلومات، ومن ثم فإن محتوياتها تعطي نظاماً يتعلق بالمعرفة عن المعرفة. وهذا المجال من يسمى أحياناً بـ(نظرية المعرفة)(۳)، أو (علم المعرفة)، حسب اصطلاح أحد الفلاسفة المعاصرين(4). ولعل ذلك من وراء اشتقاقها اللغوي الذي يعني ( علم العلوم) أو (الدراسة النقدية للعلوم)). وإذن فإن السؤال المنطقي هنا : هل تطابق الإبستمولوجيا نظرية المعرفة تماماً؟ أم ثمة اختلاف كلّي أو جزئي؟
ولتحديد الإجابة بدقة يمكن تحديد الآراء إزاء هذا المشكل بالقول: إنها تنبثق متابعة أي منهما لأي من اللغتين الإنكليزية أو الفرنسية. فالإنكليزية ترى من
Chapter One: Section Two - Definitions. Some limit it to the study of the relationship between the knowing self and the known object (1). There are those who see that defining it in the first way, meaning it is the study of its source, value, and limits... etc., requires calling it 'Critique of Knowledge' not 'Theory of Knowledge' (2). As for defining it in the second way, it led some philosophers to consider it an imaginary subject (3). And some add to all that that among its tasks is also the study of the means of knowledge in terms of their innateness and acquisition (4). The truth is that all of that is what the theory of knowledge deals with in its investigations, and it is better to take it as a single framework for the theory even if some terms are synonymous or expressed in different formulations. Theory of Knowledge and Epistemology. If it is established that the theory of knowledge includes all the above, to what extent does it meet Western epistemology? It is worth noting at the outset that epistemological studies, when they analyze and critique the results of natural and human sciences as one of their main concerns, thereby mean a kind of 'philosophy of science'. In a broader sense, it is possible to consider epistemology as a kind of general philosophy as one of the three branches of philosophy: existence (ontology), values (axiology), and also knowledge (epistemology). But that does not justify using the term philosophy of knowledge as synonymous with theory of knowledge as some researchers have claimed (1), because the former (philosophy of knowledge) investigates the issue of knowledge in general, while the latter (theory of knowledge) investigates its nature, sources, possibility of obtaining it, or limits only. Therefore, using the two terms synonymously is a mistake and an expansion out of place. As for the precise meaning of epistemology (Epistemology), Webster's New Collegiate Dictionary defines it as 'the perception and acquisition of knowledge as knowledge, and the study of its reference, limits, and degree of credibility.' In this sense, it is an extension of the Arabic theory of knowledge to the utmost extent. However, the Dictionary of Philosophy and Religion traces it back to its Greek origin. It consists of two Greek parts: 'Episteme' meaning knowledge or science, and 'logos' meaning knowledge or information. Hence, its contents give a system related to knowledge about knowledge. This field is sometimes called 'theory of knowledge' (3) or 'science of knowledge' according to the terminology of a contemporary philosopher (4). Perhaps that is due to its linguistic derivation which means 'science of sciences' or 'critical study of sciences'. Thus, the logical question here: does epistemology completely correspond to the theory of knowledge? Or is there a total or partial difference? To determine the answer precisely, one can define the opinions regarding this problem by saying: it arises from following either the English or French language. The English sees from
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage defines the scope of 'nazariyya al-ma'rifa' (theory of knowledge) and contrasts it with Western epistemology. The author first presents various definitions: some restrict it to the relationship between subject and object, others call it 'critique of knowledge' if focused on source and limits, and some even consider it imaginary. The author asserts that all these aspects are included in a unified concept of epistemology. Then, the question of correspondence with Western epistemology is raised. Epistemology is described as a branch of philosophy dealing with science, but the author warns against equating 'falsafat al-ma'rifa' (philosophy of knowledge) with 'nazariyya al-ma'rifa' (theory of knowledge), because the former is broader. The passage explains the etymology of 'epistemology' from Greek, and notes that it is sometimes synonymous with 'theory of knowledge' in certain contexts, but ultimately leaves the question open, noting that English and French usage differ.

Key Terms
نظرية المعرفة
نقد المعرفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the author's main argument regarding the various definitions of nazariyya al-ma'rifa?
A) They should be kept separate to avoid confusion.
B) Each definition is valid but the best is the one focusing on source and limits.
C) They should all be integrated into a single framework.
D) The theory of knowledge should be renamed as critique of knowledge.

Key Takeaway
Nazariyya al-ma'rifa is an integrated field covering multiple aspects of knowledge, and fragmenting it would undermine its comprehensiveness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

What Is Mantiq?

Nazariyya al-Ma'rifa and Western Epistemology
Compares nazariyya al-ma'rifa with Western epistemology, emphasizing differences in scope.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish nazariyya al-ma'rifa from Western epistemology (al-ibistimulujiya) based on the author's analysis of their scopes and terminologies.

Core Idea
Nazariyya al-ma'rifa is broader than Western epistemology, and confusing it with 'falsafat al-ma'rifa' is a mistake.

This lesson explores the relationship between the Islamic theory of knowledge and Western epistemology, highlighting the author's caution against equating falsafat al-ma'rifa with nazariyya al-ma'rifa. You will learn how the author uses lexical and conceptual distinctions to clarify the boundaries.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key components of Western epistemology
From the passage, note how epistemology is described: as a branch of philosophy (alongside ontology and axiology) and as a philosophy of science that analyzes natural and human sciences.
Look for the phrases 'فلسفة العلوم' and 'المباحث الثلاثة للفلسفة'.
2
Understand the warning against synonymy
Find where the author says using 'falsafat al-ma'rifa' as a synonym for 'nazariyya al-ma'rifa' is wrong. Note the reason: the former is general, the latter is specific (nature, sources, possibility, limits).
The passage states: 'فالأولى تبحث قضية المعرفة بصورة عامة، في حين أن الثانية تبحث في طبيعتها ومصادرها...'
3
Examine the etymology and definitions
Read the dictionary definitions from Webster and the Greek etymology. Consider why the author leaves the question of correspondence open, noting the difference between English and French usage.
The logical question at the end is: 'هل تطابق الإبستمولوجيا نظرية المعرفة تماماً؟'

وأما تعريفها على الوجه الثاني فقد دعا بعض الفلاسفة إلى اعتبار ذلك مبحثاً وهمياً (۳). وثمة من يضيف إلى ذلك كله أن من مهامها أيضاً البحث في وسائل المعرفة من حيث فطريتها واكتسابها ( ٤ ) .

Chapter One: Section Two - Definitions. Some limit it to the study of the relationship between the knowing self and the known object (1). There are those who see that defining it in the first way, meaning it is the study of its source, value, and limits... etc., requires calling it 'Critique of Knowledge' not 'Theory of Knowledge' (2). As for defining it in the second way, it led some philosophers to consider it an imaginary subject (3). And some add to all that that among its tasks is also the study of the means of knowledge in terms of their innateness and acquisition (4). The truth is that all of that is what the theory of knowledge deals with in its investigations, and it is better to take it as a single framework for the theory even if some terms are synonymous or expressed in different formulations. Theory of Knowledge and Epistemology. If it is established that the theory of knowledge includes all the above, to what extent does it meet Western epistemology? It is worth noting at the outset that epistemological studies, when they analyze and critique the results of natural and human sciences as one of their main concerns, thereby mean a kind of 'philosophy of science'. In a broader sense, it is possible to consider epistemology as a kind of general philosophy as one of the three branches of philosophy: existence (ontology), values (axiology), and also knowledge (epistemology). But that does not justify using the term philosophy of knowledge as synonymous with theory of knowledge as some researchers have claimed (1), because the former (philosophy of knowledge) investigates the issue of knowledge in general, while the latter (theory of knowledge) investigates its nature, sources, possibility of obtaining it, or limits only. Therefore, using the two terms synonymously is a mistake and an expansion out of place. As for the precise meaning of epistemology (Epistemology), Webster's New Collegiate Dictionary defines it as 'the perception and acquisition of knowledge as knowledge, and the study of its reference, limits, and degree of credibility.' In this sense, it is an extension of the Arabic theory of knowledge to the utmost extent. However, the Dictionary of Philosophy and Religion traces it back to its Greek origin. It consists of two Greek parts: 'Episteme' meaning knowledge or science, and 'logos' meaning knowledge or information. Hence, its contents give a system related to knowledge about knowledge. This field is sometimes called 'theory of knowledge' (3) or 'science of knowledge' according to the terminology of a contemporary philosopher (4). Perhaps that is due to its linguistic derivation which means 'science of sciences' or 'critical study of sciences'. Thus, the logical question here: does epistemology completely correspond to the theory of knowledge? Or is there a total or partial difference? To determine the answer precisely, one can define the opinions regarding this problem by saying: it arises from following either the English or French language. The English sees from

Commentary
This passage defines the scope of 'nazariyya al-ma'rifa' (theory of knowledge) and contrasts it with Western epistemology. The author first presents various definitions: some restrict it to the relationship between subject and object, others call it 'critique of knowledge' if focused on source and limits, and some even consider it imaginary. The author asserts that all these aspects are included in a unified concept of epistemology. Then, the question of correspondence with Western epistemology is raised. Epistemology and Theory of Knowledge: A Terminological Distinction
Author defines epistemology and compares it to theory of knowledge across English and French traditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to differentiate between the English and French conceptualizations of epistemology (إبستمولوجيا) and theory of knowledge (نظرية المعرفة) as presented in modern philosophical discourse.

Core Idea
Epistemology and theory of knowledge are not identical; their relationship depends on linguistic tradition.

In contemporary Arabic philosophical texts, the terms 'إبستمولوجيا' and 'نظرية المعرفة' are often used, but their precise relationship varies. This passage from a modern work on Quranic theory of knowledge clarifies the distinction by contrasting English and French academic traditions. Mastering this distinction will help you read modern epistemological discussions with precision.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main terms
Locate the Arabic terms 'إبستمولوجيا' and 'نظرية المعرفة' in the passage. Note that the author considers them not fully synonymous.
2
Extract the dictionary definitions
Find the definitions provided from Webster's Dictionary and the Dictionary of Philosophy and Religion. What does each source say about epistemology?
Pay attention to the Greek etymology.
3
Compare English vs. French perspectives
The passage states that in English, the terms are synonymous, while in French they are distinct. Identify the key differences according to Lalande.
Epistemology in French is the critical study of scientific principles, not methodology.
4
Identify the third term: المعلومية
The passage introduces 'المعلومية' as a synonym for epistemology in the French sense. What does it mean?
It is the critical study of principles and results of sciences.
5
Synthesize the author's conclusion
Based on the passage, does the author lean toward the English or French view? What is the overall relationship between epistemology and theory of knowledge?

الباب الأول: الفصل الثاني- التعريفات
لنظرية المعرفة كما ذهب إلى ذلك بعض الباحثين (۱) ، وحيث إن الأولى تبحث قضية المعرفة بصورة عامة، في حين أن الثانية تبحث في طبيعتها ومصادرها وإمكان الحصول عليها أو حدودها فحسب وعليه فإن استخدام المصطلحين على نحو من الترادف مجانبة للصواب، وتوسع في غير مقامه.
أما معنى الإبستمولوجيا (Epistemlogyo) تحديداً فقد عرفها قاموس وبستر الجديد (Webster's New) على أنها إدراك المعرفة والحصول عليها كمعرفة سيبها، ودراسة، مرجعيتها، وحدودها، ومدى مصداقيتها). وهي بهذا المعنى امتداد لنظرية المعرفة في العربية إلى أقصى حد. بيد أن معجم الفلسفة والدين (Philosophy and Religion) أرجعها إلى أصلها اليوناني. إذ هي مقطعين يونانيين هما (Episteme) وتعني المعرفة أو العلم، و(logos) وتعني المعرفة أو المعلومات، ومن ثم فإن محتوياتها تعطي نظاماً يتعلق بالمعرفـة عـن المعرفة. وهذا المجال من يسمى أحياناً بـ(نظرية المعرفة)(۳)، أو (علم المعرفة، حسب اصطلاح أحد الفلاسفة المعاصرين(4). ولعل ذلك من وراء اشتقاقها اللغوي الذي يعني ( علم العلوم) أو (الدراسة النقدية للعلوم)). وإذن فإن السؤال المنطقي هنا : هل تطابق الإبستمولوجيا نظرية المعرفة تماماً؟ أم ثمة اختلاف كلّي أو جزئي؟
الفلسفة هو ما ولتحديد الإجابة بدقة يمكن تحديد الآراء إزاء هذا المشكل بالقول: إنها تنبثق متابعة أي منهما لأي من اللغتين الإنكليزية أو الفرنسية. فالإنكليزية ترى من التطابق بينهما حيث تصدير الإبستمولوجيا (Epistemolgyo) مرادفة لمصطلح نظرية المعرفة تماماً (۱). ويبدو أن جميع الذين رأوا التطابق قائمـاً بين المعنيين، إنمـا تابعوا المصطلح الإنجليزي وحده (۲) ، في حين تختلف الإبستمولوجيا عن نظرية المعرفة في الفرنسية. فالإبستمولوجيا في الفرنسية Epistemologie) لا تجعل من المعنيين معنى واحداً، بل تميز بينهما، وتجعل من الإبستمولوجيا مرادفاً لفلسفة العلوم دون أن تكون طريقته (Methodology)، كما يقول (لالاند) (ت: ١٩٦٣م): إنها تدل على فلسفة العلوم، لكن بمعنى أدق فهي ليست حقاً دراسة المناهج العلمية والتي هي الطرائقية، وتنتمي إلى المنطق. كما أنها ليست توليفاً أو إرهاصاً ظنياً بالقوانين العلمية على منوال المذهب الوضعي والنشوئي). جوهرياً المعلومية هي الدرس النقدي لمبادئ مختلف العلوم وفرضيتها ونتائجها، الرامي إلى تحديد أصلها المنطقي قيمتها ومداها الموضوعي علينا إذن التفريق بين المعلومية ونظرية المعرفة، على الرغم من كون المعلومية مدخلاً لها، ومساعدها اللازب فهي تمتاز عن نظرية المعرفة بأنها تدرس المعرفة بالتفصيل، وبشكل بعدي، في مختلف العلوم والأغراض، أكثر منها تدرسها على صعيد وحدة الفكر (۳).
وعلى هذا فإذا شايع بعض الباحثين التفريق بين الإبستمولوجيا وبين نظرية المعرفة، فهم إنما تابعوا المعنى الفرنسي، و(لالاند) على وجه الخصوص (٤). إذن فإنها تبدو وفق هذا المعنى متعارضة مع نظرية المعرفة السائدة اليوم نسبياً، حيث تمثل الإبستمولوجيا مدخلاً لنظرية المعرفة فقط دون أن تعنى
Chapter One: Second Section – Definitions. For the theory of knowledge, as some researchers have argued (1), and since the first [term] investigates the issue of knowledge in general, while the second investigates its nature, sources, possibility of obtaining it, or its limits only, therefore using the two terms synonymously is a departure from correctness and an expansion out of place. As for the specific meaning of epistemology (Epistemology), the New Webster's Dictionary defined it as: 'the perception and acquisition of knowledge as knowledge of its cause, and the study of its reference, limits, and extent of credibility.' In this sense it is an extension of the Arabic theory of knowledge to the utmost. However, the Dictionary of Philosophy and Religion traced it back to its Greek origin. It consists of two Greek parts: 'Episteme' meaning knowledge or science, and 'logos' meaning knowledge or information; thus its contents give a system related to knowledge about knowledge. This field is sometimes called 'theory of knowledge' (3), or 'science of knowledge', according to one contemporary philosopher (4). Perhaps that is due to its linguistic derivation which means 'science of sciences' or 'the critical study of sciences'. Then the logical question here: Does epistemology completely match the theory of knowledge? Or is there a total or partial difference? Philosophy is what... To determine the answer precisely, one can identify the opinions regarding this problem by saying: It stems from following either the English or French language. The English sees a correspondence between them, where epistemology (Epistemology) is used as a synonym for the term 'theory of knowledge' completely (1). It seems that all who saw the correspondence between the two meanings followed the English term alone (2), while epistemology differs from theory of knowledge in French. In French, epistemology (Epistémologie) does not make the two meanings one, but distinguishes between them, and makes epistemology synonymous with philosophy of science without being its methodology, as Lalande (d. 1963) says: 'It indicates the philosophy of science, but in a more precise sense it is not really the study of scientific methods which is methodology, and belongs to logic. Nor is it a synthesis or a conjectural anticipation of scientific laws on the model of positivism and evolutionism.' Essentially, epistemology is the critical study of the principles of various sciences, their hypotheses, and their results, aiming to determine their logical origin, their value, and their objective scope. We must therefore distinguish between epistemology and theory of knowledge, despite the fact that epistemology is an introduction to it and an indispensable aid; it is distinguished from theory of knowledge in that it studies knowledge in detail and in a posteriori manner in various sciences and purposes, more than it studies it at the level of the unity of thought (3). Accordingly, if some researchers have favored distinguishing between epistemology and theory of knowledge, they have followed the French meaning, and Lalande in particular (4). Thus, according to this meaning, it appears contradictory to the prevailing theory of knowledge today relatively, where epistemology represents only an introduction to theory of knowledge without concerning itself with
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage is a definitional and comparative analysis of two key terms in epistemology: 'إبستمولوجيا' (epistemology) and 'نظرية المعرفة' (theory of knowledge). The author begins by noting that some researchers use these terms interchangeably, but argues that this is incorrect because the first term (theory of knowledge) generally investigates the issue of knowledge, while the second (epistemology) focuses specifically on its nature, sources, possibility, and limits. The author then provides a detailed definition of 'إبستمولوجيا' from the New Webster's Dictionary, describing it as the perception and acquisition of knowledge, including its cause, reference, limits, and credibility. This makes it an extension of the Arabic theory of knowledge. The Dictionary of Philosophy and Religion traces epistemology to Greek roots: 'Episteme' (knowledge/science) and 'logos' (knowledge/information), resulting in a system about knowledge of knowledge. This field is sometimes called 'theory of knowledge' or 'science of knowledge', and its linguistic derivation means 'science of sciences' or 'critical study of sciences'. The logical question posed is whether epistemology and theory of knowledge are fully equivalent. To answer, the author explains that the relationship depends on linguistic tradition. In English, epistemology is synonymous with theory of knowledge, and scholars who see correspondence follow English usage. In French, however, epistemology (Epistémologie) is distinct; it is synonymous with philosophy of science, not methodology. The author quotes Lalande, who states that epistemology is the critical study of scientific principles, hypotheses, and results, determining their logical origin, value, and objective scope. Therefore, epistemology is an introduction and aid to theory of knowledge, but differs by studying knowledge in detail and a posteriori across sciences, rather than at the level of unified thought. Finally, the author notes that researchers who distinguish between the two follow the French meaning, particularly Lalande, and that this view contrasts with the prevailing theory of knowledge, where epistemology is merely an introduction.

Key Terms
إبستمولوجيا
نظرية المعرفة
المعلومية

Key Takeaway
Epistemology, in the French tradition, is a critical study of scientific principles and serves as an introduction to theory of knowledge, not a synonym.

Critique of Using 'Theory' for the Quran
Author introduces the controversy over using 'theory' for the Quran, citing Sayyid Qutb's rejection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Sayyid Qutb's objection to calling the Islamic creed a 'theory' and explain the epistemological danger he identifies.

Core Idea
The Quran is a living reality, not a theoretical construct.

This lesson examines a critical challenge to applying the term 'theory' (nazariyya) to the Quran. Sayyid Qutb argues that the Islamic creed is a dynamic, lived reality, and reducing it to an abstract theory distorts its nature. Understanding this objection is essential for properly framing the Quran's epistemological role.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target of the critique
What is being rejected? The use of the term 'theory' (nazariyya) to describe the Quran or the Islamic creed ('aqida).
2
Extract Qutb's reasoning
What reasons does he give? He says the creed should not crystallize into an abstract theory for intellectual study; it is a living, moving reality.
3
Recognize the binary
Notice the contrast: 'abstract theory' vs. 'living, moving reality'. Qutb sees them as incompatible.
4
Assess the implication
If Qutb is right, what does that mean for academic study of the Quran? It challenges the use of modern academic categories like 'theory' for sacred texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نظراً للخلاف القائم بين المصطلحات سواء مصطلح النظرية أم نظرية المعرفة فضلا عن الإبستمولوجيا الغربية - فقد دفع ذلك ببعض الباحثين لاتخاذ موقف ظاهره الرفض القاطع لاستخدام مصطلح (نظرية) لوصف القرآن الكريم. ومن هؤلاء سيد قطب - رحمه الله تعالى - الذي يقول في هذا الصدد: وخطأ - بالقياس إلى الإسلام - أن تتبلور العقيدة في صورة نظرية مجردة للدراسة الذهنية المعرفية الثقافية، بل خطر أي خطر كذلك. وقال: «يجب أن ندرك خطأ المحاولة وخطرها معاً، في تحويل العقيدة الإسلامية الحية التي يجب أن تتمثل في واقع تام حي متحرك، إلى (نظرية)
Due to the existing conflict between the terms, whether the term 'theory' or 'theory of knowledge' in addition to Western epistemology - this has driven some researchers to take a position that appears to be an outright rejection of using the term 'theory' to describe the Holy Quran. Among them is Sayyid Qutb - may Allah have mercy on him - who says in this regard: 'It is a mistake - by analogy to Islam - for the creed to crystallize into an abstract theory for intellectual, cognitive, cultural study; rather it is a danger, any danger.' And he said: 'We must realize the mistake and the danger together in converting the living Islamic creed, which must be embodied in a complete, living, moving reality, into a theory.'
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage introduces the controversy surrounding the use of the term 'theory' (nazariyya) for the Quran. The author notes that due to terminological confusion, some scholars completely reject applying the word 'theory' to describe the Quran. Sayyid Qutb is cited as an example. He argues that reducing the Islamic creed to an abstract theory for intellectual study is erroneous and dangerous. The creed is meant to be a living reality, not a theoretical construct. This critique is important for understanding the methodological approach of the book, which likely aims to define 'theory' in a Quranic context while addressing such objections.

Key Terms
نظرية (nazariyya): An abstract theoretical construct used for intellectual analysis; the author is critiquing its application to the Quran. [Note: In classical Islamic sciences, 'nazariyya' often means speculative or theoretical knowledge; here it is used in a modern academic sense.]
العقيدة (al-'aqida): The Islamic creed, which is a lived reality according to Sayyid Qutb, not a theoretical system. [Note: Standard term for Islamic doctrine; Qutb's usage emphasizes its practical, dynamic nature.]

Defining Ma'rifa: Recognition and Prior Ignorance
Author presents and critiques definitions of ma'rifa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish ma'rifa from 'ilm based on the criterion of prior ignorance.

Core Idea
Ma'rifa is recognition preceded by ignorance; 'ilm is not necessarily preceded by ignorance.

This lesson explores the definition of ma'rifa as presented by classical scholars like al-Razi and al-Jurjani. You will learn the key feature that sets ma'rifa apart from 'ilm: the requirement of prior ignorance. This distinction matters in Islamic theology because God is described as 'alim but not 'arif, as He is never ignorant.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum
Find the Arabic term المعرفة (al-ma'rifa) in the passage. Note the various definitions offered by al-Razi and al-Jurjani.
Al-Razi gives multiple definitions; al-Jurjani gives a concise summary.
2
Extract the genus and differentia
The genus is 'perception of a thing as it is' (إدراك الشيء على ما هو عليه). The differentia is 'preceded by ignorance' (مسبوقة بجهل) and sometimes includes recognition of a previously perceived object.
Al-Jurjani's definition explicitly includes the differentia.
3
Compare definitions
Compare al-Razi's definitions with al-Jurjani's. All include the element of prior ignorance. Note that God is not described as 'arif because He is never ignorant.
4
Distinguish from 'ilm
Al-Jurjani explicitly contrasts ma'rifa with 'ilm: ma'rifa is preceded by ignorance, unlike 'ilm. This is the key distinction.
This distinction is used in Kalam to predicate 'ilm of God but not ma'rifa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما الإمام الرازي فقد أورد عدة تعريفات لها منها: حصول العلم بعد الالتباس، ولهذا يقال: ما كنت أعرف فلاناً والآن عرفته. سبق الجهل، ولهذا يوصف الله تعالى بأنه عالم لا عارف إذ الجهل محال على الله تعالى. تطلق على من أدرك شيئاً، وانحفظ أثره في نفسه، ثم أراك ذلك الشيء ثانياً، وعرف أن هذا المدرك ثانياً هو المدرك أولاً، فهذا هو المعرفة. تقول: عرفت هذا الرجل، وهو فلان الذي كنت رأيته وقت كذا. ويلخص الجرجاني (ت: 816هـ) معناها فيقول: «إنها إدراك الشيء على ما هو عليه، وهي مسبوقة بجهل بخلاف العلم». وأما تعريفها من قبل الباحثين المعاصرين فعلى الرغم من الاختلاف اللفظي بين تقديم وتأخير، وإضافة وحذف لكنها في المحصلة النهائية لا تخرج عن معنى: أنها عملية إدراك للأشياء على حقيقتها، عن طريق مصادر ووسائل المعرفة على خلاف في تحديدها. أما في استخدام القرآن الكريم فيرى بعض الباحثين في هذا الموضوع أنها عبارة عن: المعلومات والمفاهيم اليقينية أو الأكيدة، والأحكام والمدركات والتصورات الجازمة التي نكونها أو نتوصل إليها عن شيء ما نتيجة ما نتلقاه عن طريق الوحي، أو عن طريق الحس والعقل والحدس، أو عن طريقها جميعاً. ولعل هذا لا يتعارض مع ما خرج به باحث آخر من أن القرآن الكريم يطلق اسم القراءة على المعرفة استيجاء من قوله تعالى ﴿اقْرَأْ بِاسْمِ رَبِّكَ الَّذِي خَلَق﴾ [العلق: 1/96]، على اعتبار أن القراءة مفتاح المعرفة، وبها يمكن إدراك الأشياء على حقيقتها، وفق رؤية علمية مستندة إلى المصادر والوسائل المعتبرة. تعريف العلم: علمه كسمعه عِلماً بالكسر، عرفه وعلم به كسمع شعر، وهذا صريح في أن العلم والمعرفة والشعور بمعنى واحد، وأنه يتعدى بنفسه في المعنى الأول بالباء، إذا استعمل بمعنى شعر. ومع أن رأي أكثر أهل اللغة قريب من هذا، إلا أن أكثر المحققين يفرقون بينها جميعاً. وفي بعض المصادر أيضاً: علمه يعلمه علماً: عرفه حق المعرفة، والعلم نقيض الجهل. ويعرف العلم بأنه إدراك الشيء على حقيقته، وذلك ضربان: أحدهما إدراك ذات الشيء، والثاني: هو الحكم على الشيء بوجود شيء هو موجود له، أو نفي شيء هو منفي عنه. فالأول يتعدى إلى مفعول واحد نحو قوله تعالى: ﴿ولا تَعْلَمُونَهُمُ اللهُ يَعْلَمُهُمْ﴾ [الأنفال: 60/8].
As for Imam al-Razi, he presented several definitions for it (ma'rifa), among them: 'The occurrence of knowledge after confusion, and for this it is said: I did not know so-and-so and now I have known him.' 'It is preceded by ignorance, and for this God is described as 'alim (knower) not 'arif (recognizer) because ignorance is impossible for God.' 'It is applied to one who perceives something, and its trace is preserved in his soul, then he shows you that thing a second time, and he knows that this perceived second time is the perceived first time; this is ma'rifa. You say: I recognized this man, and he is so-and-so whom I saw at such-and-such time.' And al-Jurjani (d. 816 AH) summarizes its meaning saying: 'It is perception of a thing as it is, and it is preceded by ignorance, unlike knowledge ('ilm).' As for its definition by contemporary researchers, despite the verbal difference between precedence and delay, addition and deletion, in the final analysis they do not go beyond the meaning: that it is a process of perceiving things as they really are, through the sources and means of knowledge, with disagreement in specifying them. As for its use in the Noble Quran, some researchers in this subject see that it is: 'The certain or assured information and concepts, and the definitive judgments, perceptions, and conceptions that we form or reach about something as a result of what we receive through revelation, or through the senses, reason, and intuition, or through all of them together.' And perhaps this does not contradict what another researcher concluded, that the Noble Quran uses the term 'reading' (qira'a) for knowledge, deriving from His saying, 'Read in the name of your Lord who created' (Al-'Alaq 96:1), on the basis that reading is the key to knowledge, and through it one can perceive things as they really are, according to a scientific view based on reputable sources and means. Definition of 'ilm: 'He taught him' like 'he heard him' with kasra, 'he recognized him' and 'he knew by it' like 'he heard poetry,' and this is explicit that 'ilm, ma'rifa, and shu'ur (awareness) have one meaning, and that it is transitive by itself in the first meaning with the letter ba, if used in the sense of 'felt.' And although the opinion of most philologists is close to this, most investigators distinguish between all of them. And in some sources also: 'He knew it, he knows it, as knowledge: he recognized it truly,' and that knowledge is the opposite of ignorance. And knowledge is defined as perception of a thing as it is, and that is of two types: one is perception of the essence of a thing, and the second is the judgment about a thing of the existence of something that exists for it, or the denial of something that is denied from it. The first is transitive to one object, as in His saying: 'And you do not know them; God knows them' (Al-Anfal 8:60).
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage is a definitional survey of two key terms: ma'rifa (knowledge/recognition) and 'ilm (science/knowledge). The author begins by presenting definitions of ma'rifa from classical scholars, starting with al-Razi. Al-Razi offers multiple definitions: (1) knowledge after confusion, (2) preceded by ignorance (hence God is called 'alim not 'arif), (3) a recognition of something previously perceived with a preserved trace. Then al-Jurjani's concise definition: perception of a thing as it is, preceded by ignorance, unlike 'ilm which is not necessarily preceded by ignorance. The author then notes that contemporary definitions, despite verbal differences, converge on the idea of perceiving things as they are through various sources. A Quran-based definition describes ma'rifa as certain information and definitive judgments obtained through revelation, senses, reason, and intuition. Another researcher connects ma'rifa to 'reading' (iqra') as the key to knowledge. The author then turns to 'ilm, starting from lexicography: 'ilm is synonymous with ma'rifa and shu'ur, but most investigators distinguish them. 'Ilm is defined as perception of a thing as it is, divided into two types: (a) perception of the essence (tasawwur) and (b) judgment (tasdiq) affirming or denying something. An example from the Quran illustrates the first type. The passage thus provides a comprehensive overview of definitions, showing the nuanced relationship between ma'rifa and 'ilm in Islamic thought.

Defining 'Ilm: Perception of Essence and Judgment
Author defines 'ilm and distinguishes its two types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any given piece of knowledge as either perception of essence (tasawwur) or judgment (tasdiq) using the definition of 'ilm.

Core Idea
'Ilm is perception of a thing as it is, divided into perception of essence and judgment.

This lesson unpacks the definition of 'ilm as given in the passage. 'Ilm is defined as perception of a thing as it is, and it has two types: one is perception of the essence (tasawwur), and the other is judgment (tasdiq) that affirms or denies something. You will learn to apply this distinction to Islamic sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum
Locate the definition of العلم ('ilm) in the passage: 'إدراك الشيء على حقيقته' (perception of a thing as it is).
This is the core definition.
2
Extract the two types
The passage divides 'ilm into two types: (a) perception of the essence (إدراك ذات الشيء), and (b) judgment (الحكم) affirming or denying something about the thing.
These correspond to tasawwur and tasdiq in Islamic logic.
3
Understand the transitive structure
The first type is transitive to one object (e.g., 'you do not know them'). The second type involves a relation. Notice the Quranic example: 'ولا تعلمونهم' illustrates the first type.
4
Apply to Quranic example
The verse 'ولا تعلمونهم الله يعلمهم' is an example of perception of the essence: the knowledge is about the people themselves, not a judgment about them.
This helps distinguish the two types in practice.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما الإمام الرازي فقد أورد عدة تعريفات لها منها: حصول العلم بعد الالتباس، ولهذا يقال: ما كنت أعرف فلاناً والآن عرفته. سبق الجهل، ولهذا يوصف الله تعالى بأنه عالم لا عارف إذ الجهل محال على الله تعالى. تطلق على من أدرك شيئاً، وانحفظ أثره في نفسه، ثم أراك ذلك الشيء ثانياً، وعرف أن هذا المدرك ثانياً هو المدرك أولاً، فهذا هو المعرفة. تقول: عرفت هذا الرجل، وهو فلان الذي كنت رأيته وقت كذا. ويلخص الجرجاني (ت: 816هـ) معناها فيقول: «إنها إدراك الشيء على ما هو عليه، وهي مسبوقة بجهل بخلاف العلم». وأما تعريفها من قبل الباحثين المعاصرين فعلى الرغم من الاختلاف اللفظي بين تقديم وتأخير، وإضافة وحذف لكنها في المحصلة النهائية لا تخرج عن معنى: أنها عملية إدراك للأشياء على حقيقتها، عن طريق مصادر ووسائل المعرفة على خلاف في تحديدها. أما في استخدام القرآن الكريم فيرى بعض الباحثين في هذا الموضوع أنها عبارة عن: المعلومات والمفاهيم اليقينية أو الأكيدة، والأحكام والمدركات والتصورات الجازمة التي نكونها أو نتوصل إليها عن شيء ما نتيجة ما نتلقاه عن طريق الوحي، أو عن طريق الحس والعقل والحدس، أو عن طريقها جميعاً. ولعل هذا لا يتعارض مع ما خرج به باحث آخر من أن القرآن الكريم يطلق اسم القراءة على المعرفة استيجاء من قوله تعالى ﴿اقْرَأْ بِاسْمِ رَبِّكَ الَّذِي خَلَق﴾ [العلق: 1/96]، على اعتبار أن القراءة مفتاح المعرفة، وبها يمكن إدراك الأشياء على حقيقتها، وفق رؤية علمية مستندة إلى المصادر والوسائل المعتبرة. تعريف العلم: علمه كسمعه عِلماً بالكسر، عرفه وعلم به كسمع شعر، وهذا صريح في أن العلم والمعرفة والشعور بمعنى واحد، وأنه يتعدى بنفسه في المعنى الأول بالباء، إذا استعمل بمعنى شعر. ومع أن رأي أكثر أهل اللغة قريب من هذا، إلا أن أكثر المحققين يفرقون بينها جميعاً. وفي بعض المصادر أيضاً: علمه يعلمه علماً: عرفه حق المعرفة، والعلم نقيض الجهل. ويعرف العلم بأنه إدراك الشيء على حقيقته، وذلك ضربان: أحدهما إدراك ذات الشيء، والثاني: هو الحكم على الشيء بوجود شيء هو موجود له، أو نفي شيء هو منفي عنه. فالأول يتعدى إلى مفعول واحد نحو قوله تعالى: ﴿ولا تَعْلَمُونَهُمُ اللهُ يَعْلَمُهُمْ﴾ [الأنفال: 60/8].
As for Imam al-Razi, he presented several definitions for it (ma'rifa), among them: 'The occurrence of knowledge after confusion, and for this it is said: I did not know so-and-so and now I have known him.' 'It is preceded by ignorance, and for this God is described as 'alim (knower) not 'arif (recognizer) because ignorance is impossible for God.' 'It is applied to one who perceives something, and its trace is preserved in his soul, then he shows you that thing a second time, and he knows that this perceived second time is the perceived first time; this is ma'rifa. You say: I recognized this man, and he is so-and-so whom I saw at such-and-such time.' And al-Jurjani (d. 816 AH) summarizes its meaning saying: 'It is perception of a thing as it is, and it is preceded by ignorance, unlike knowledge ('ilm).' As for its definition by contemporary researchers, despite the verbal difference between precedence and delay, addition and deletion, in the final analysis they do not go beyond the meaning: that it is a process of perceiving things as they really are, through the sources and means of knowledge, with disagreement in specifying them. As for its use in the Noble Quran, some researchers in this subject see that it is: 'The certain or assured information and concepts, and the definitive judgments, perceptions, and conceptions that we form or reach about something as a result of what we receive through revelation, or through the senses, reason, and intuition, or through all of them together.' And perhaps this does not contradict what another researcher concluded, that the Noble Quran uses the term 'reading' (qira'a) for knowledge, deriving from His saying, 'Read in the name of your Lord who created' (Al-'Alaq 96:1), on the basis that reading is the key to knowledge, and through it one can perceive things as they really are, according to a scientific view based on reputable sources and means. Definition of 'ilm: 'He taught him' like 'he heard him' with kasra, 'he recognized him' and 'he knew by it' like 'he heard poetry,' and this is explicit that 'ilm, ma'rifa, and shu'ur (awareness) have one meaning, and that it is transitive by itself in the first meaning with the letter ba, if used in the sense of 'felt.' And although the opinion of most philologists is close to this, most investigators distinguish between all of them. And in some sources also: 'He knew it, he knows it, as knowledge: he recognized it truly,' and that knowledge is the opposite of ignorance. And knowledge is defined as perception of a thing as it is, and that is of two types: one is perception of the essence of a thing, and the second is the judgment about a thing of the existence of something that exists for it, or the denial of something that is denied from it. The first is transitive to one object, as in His saying: 'And you do not know them; God knows them' (Al-Anfal 8:60).

Commentary
This passage is a definitional survey of two key terms: ma'rifa (knowledge/recognition) and 'ilm (science/knowledge). The author begins by presenting definitions of ma'rifa from classical scholars, starting with al-Razi. Al-Razi offers multiple definitions: (1) knowledge after confusion, (2) preceded by ignorance (hence God is called 'alim not 'arif), (3) a recognition of something previously perceived with a preserved trace. Then al-Jurjani's concise definition: perception of a thing as it is, preceded by ignorance, unlike 'ilm which is not necessarily preceded by ignorance. The author then notes that contemporary definitions, despite verbal differences, converge on the idea of perceiving things as they are through various sources. A Quran-based definition describes ma'rifa as certain information and definitive judgments obtained through revelation, senses, reason, and intuition. The author then turns to 'ilm, starting from lexicography: 'ilm is synonymous with ma'rifa and shu'ur, but most investigators distinguish them. 'Ilm is defined as perception of a thing as it is, divided into two types: (a) perception of the essence (tasawwur) and (b) judgment (tasdiq) affirming or denying something. An example from the Quran illustrates the first type. The passage thus provides a comprehensive overview of definitions, showing the nuanced relationship between ma'rifa and 'ilm in Islamic thought.

Defining Ma'rifa and 'Ilm: Essence vs Attributes
Author defines ma'rifa and 'ilm with Quranic evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between ma'rifa and 'ilm based on their objects (essence vs attributes) and map them to tasawwur and tasdiq.

Core Idea
Ma'rifa grasps the essence; 'ilm grasps the attributes.

In this passage, the author clarifies two key epistemological terms: ma'rifa (recognition/knowledge) and 'ilm (knowledge/science). He explains that ma'rifa concerns the essence of a thing, while 'ilm concerns its states and attributes. This foundational distinction parallels the division of knowledge into conception (tasawwur) and assent (tasdiq). Understanding this difference is essential for precise discourse in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the terms being defined
Locate the definitions of ma'rifa and 'ilm in the Arabic. Note that ma'rifa is defined as the presence of the image and scientific likeness of a thing in the soul, while 'ilm is the presence of its states, attributes, and relations.
2
Extract the objects of each
For ma'rifa, the object is the essence/thing itself; for 'ilm, the object is the states/attributes. Observe how the Quranic verses given for 'ilm all pertain to knowledge of divine attributes (tawhid, punishment, revelation).
3
Map them to tasawwur and tasdiq
The author directly says ma'rifa resembles tasawwur (conception) and 'ilm resembles tasdiq (assent). Understand that tasawwur is the simple grasping of a concept, while tasdiq involves a judgment about a state of affairs.
Ma'rifa is like a concept, 'ilm is like a proposition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الأول: الفصل الثاني- التعريفات
ثانياً من حيث المعنى
١ - المعرفة تتعلق بذات الشيء، والعلم يتعلق بأحواله، فقال سبحانه: ﴿فَاعْلَمْ أَنَّهُ لا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللهُ ﴾ [محمد: ١٩/٤٧]، وقال: ﴿اعْلَمُوا أَنَّ اللَّهَ شَدِيدُ الْعِقَابِ﴾ [المائدة: ٩٨/٥]، وقال: ﴿فَاعْلَمُوا أَنما أُنْزِلَ بِعِلْمِ اللهِ ﴾ [هود: ١٤/١١].
فالمعرفة إذن حضور صورة الشيء ومثاله العلمي في النفس، أما العلم فحضور أحواله وصفاته، ونسبتها إليه فالمعرفة تشبه التصور، والعلم يشبه التصديق. -٢- تأتي المعرفة غالباً لما غاب عن القلب بعد إدراكه، فإذا أدركه قيل عرفه، أو تكون لما وصف له بصفات قامت في نفسه. فإذا رآه وعلم أنه الموصوف بها قيل عرفه، قال تعالى: ﴿وَيَوْمَ يَحْشُرُهُمْ كَأَن لَمْ يَلْبَثُوا إلا ساعَةً مِنَ النهار يَتَعارَفُونَ بَيْنَهُمْ﴾ [يونس: ٤٥/١٠]، وقال: ﴿وَجَاءَ إِخْوَةُ يُوسُفَ فَدَخَلُوا عَلَيْهِ فَعَرَفَهُمْ وَهُمْ لَهُ مُنْكِرُونَ﴾ [يوسف: ٥٨/١٢]، وقال: ﴿الَّذِينَ آتَيْنَاهُمُ الْكِتَابَ يَعْرِفُونَهُ كَما يَعْرِفُونَ أَبْناءَهُم﴾ [البقرة: ١٤٦/٢، الأنعام: ٢٠/٦]، ذلك أن صفاته كانت معلومة لديهم، فرأوه أي عرفوه بتلك الصفات. ومن هذا يتضح أن المعرفة تشبه الذكر للشيء، وهو حضور ما كان غائباً عن الذكر. ولهذا كان ضد المعرفة الإنكار، وضدّ العلم الجهل، قال تعالى: ﴿يَعْرِفُونَ نِعْمَةَ اللهِ ثُمَّ يُنْكِرُونَها﴾ [النحل: ٨٣/١٦]، ويقال عرف الحق فأقر به، وعرفه فأنكره. تفيد المعرفة تمييز المعروف عن غيره، أما العلم فيفيد تمييز ما يوصف به غيره. والفرق بين هذا الفرق والذي سبقه أن الأول يرجع إلى إدراك عن صفاتها. أما هذا فيرجع إلى تخليص الذات من غيرها وتخليص صفات غيرها. إننا حين نقول: علمت زيداً لا نفيد المخاطب شيئاً فهو ينظر الحال التي عرفناه عليها، ولذلك فكان ينبغي القول علمت زيداً كريماً أو شجاعاً، كي تحصل الفائدة. ولكن قولنا: عرفت زيداً يفيد الإثبات والتمييز له عن غيره.
٤ - المعرفة هي العلم بعين الشيء مفصلاً عما سواه، بخلاف العلم فإنـه قـد يتعلق بالشيء مجملاً. وهذا الفرق نقله ابن القيم عن العسكري في فروقه وفروق غيره. أ. هـ. (۱)
Chapter One: Section Two – Definitions. Secondly, with respect to meaning. 1 – Ma'rifa pertains to the essence of a thing, and 'ilm pertains to its states. So He, exalted, said: 'Know that there is no god but Allah' [Muhammad 47:19], and said: 'Know that Allah is severe in punishment' [al-Ma'idah 5:98], and said: 'Know that it was sent down with the knowledge of Allah' [Hud 11:14]. Ma'rifa, therefore, is the presence of the image of a thing and its scientific likeness in the soul; as for 'ilm, it is the presence of its states and attributes and their relation to it. So ma'rifa resembles conception (tasawwur), and 'ilm resembles assent (tasdiq). 2 – Ma'rifa often comes for what was absent from the heart after its perception: when he perceives it, it is said 'he knows it', or it is for that which has been described to him with attributes that have been established in his soul. When he sees it and knows that it is the described one, it is said 'he knows it'. The Most High said: 'And on the Day when He will gather them, as if they had not tarried but an hour of the day, they will recognize one another' [Yunus 10:45], and said: 'And the brothers of Joseph came and entered upon him, and he recognized them while they were unaware of him' [Yusuf 12:58], and said: 'Those to whom We have given the Book recognize him as they recognize their own sons' [al-Baqarah 2:146, al-An'am 6:20]. That is because his attributes were known to them, so they saw him, i.e., they recognized him by those attributes. From this it becomes clear that ma'rifa resembles remembrance of a thing, which is the presence of what was absent from remembrance. For this reason, the opposite of ma'rifa is denial, and the opposite of 'ilm is ignorance. The Most High said: 'They recognize the favor of Allah, then they deny it' [al-Nahl 16:83], and it is said: he recognized the truth and affirmed it, and he recognized it and denied it. Ma'rifa gives the distinction of the known from others, while 'ilm gives the distinction of what is described by others. The difference between this distinction and the preceding one is that the former refers to perception of attributes, while this refers to isolating the essence from others and isolating its attributes from those of others. When we say 'I knew Zayd' (in the sense of 'ilm), we do not inform the addressee of anything; he looks at the condition in which we knew him. Therefore, one should say 'I knew Zayd as generous or brave' to obtain benefit. But our saying 'I recognized Zayd' (with ma'rifa) gives confirmation and distinction of him from others. 4 – Ma'rifa is knowledge of the very thing in detail as distinct from others, unlike 'ilm which may pertain to a thing in summary. This difference was transmitted by Ibn Qayyim from al-Askari in his 'Differences' and the differences of others. End.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage defines two key epistemological terms: ma'rifa (knowledge/cognition) and 'ilm (knowledge/science), distinguishing them through Quranic evidence and cognitive processes. The author begins by stating that ma'rifa relates to the essence of a thing, while 'ilm relates to its states. Three Quranic verses are cited to illustrate 'ilm as knowledge of matters like tawhid, punishment, and revelation. Ma'rifa is defined as the presence of the form or mental image of a thing in the soul, whereas 'ilm is the presence of its states, attributes, and relationships. This leads to the observation that ma'rifa resembles conception (tasawwur) and 'ilm resembles assent (tasdiq). The second point discusses the usage of ma'rifa: it often applies to something that was absent from the heart after having been perceived, or is based on prior description. The Quranic examples of mutual recognition on the Day of Judgment, Joseph recognizing his brothers, and the People of the Book recognizing the Prophet (like their own sons) show that recognition occurs through prior knowledge of attributes. Ma'rifa is thus likened to remembrance, bringing back what was absent. Its opposite is denial (inkar), while the opposite of 'ilm is ignorance (jahl), as in the verse about recognizing Allah's favor then denying it. Ma'rifa serves to distinguish the known from others, while 'ilm serves to distinguish what is described from others. The first difference (between the two distinctions) is that the former goes back to perception of attributes, while the latter is to isolate the essence from others and its attributes from others' attributes. An example: saying 'I knew Zayd' (with 'ilm) without specifying quality gives no benefit; one should say 'I knew Zayd as generous or brave'. But saying 'I recognized Zayd' (with ma'rifa) gives affirmation and distinction. The fourth point adds another definition from Ibn al-Qayyim and al-Askari: ma'rifa is knowledge of the thing in detail, distinguishing it from others, whereas 'ilm can be summary. This reinforces the idea that ma'rifa is more specific and detailed.

العلم
التصديق
التصور

Key Takeaway

Distinguishing Ma'rifa from 'Ilm: Detail, Opposition, and Usage
Author elaborates differences between ma'rifa and 'ilm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the opposite of each term, explain the difference between detailed (ma'rifa) and summary ('ilm) knowledge, and apply the correct term in sentences.

Core Idea
Ma'rifa is detailed distinction; 'ilm can be summary. Their opposites are denial and ignorance.

The author further elaborates the distinction between ma'rifa and 'ilm by examining their opposites, their cognitive functions, and the level of detail. He notes that ma'rifa often involves recognizing something previously known but absent, while 'ilm can be a general knowledge. Moreover, ma'rifa gives detailed distinction of the known from others, whereas 'ilm gives distinction of attributes. These nuances are vital for precise expression in Islamic discourse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opposites
Find where the passage states the opposite of ma'rifa is denial (inkar) and the opposite of 'ilm is ignorance (jahl). Note the Quranic verse that pairs recognition with denial.
2
Understand the usage of ma'rifa
The passage explains that ma'rifa is used for something that was absent from the heart after perception, or for something recognized by prior attributes. The examples include mutual recognition on Judgment Day, Joseph recognizing his brothers, and the People of the Book recognizing the Prophet.
Ma'rifa is likened to remembrance.
3
Differentiate the functions: distinction of essence vs distinction of attributes
Ma'rifa distinguishes the known from others; 'ilm distinguishes what is described from others. The author says the first (ma'rifa) perceives attributes, the second ('ilm) isolates essence and attributes from others.
4
Apply the distinction using the given example
The author gives: 'I knew Zayd' (with 'ilm) without quality is uninformative, but 'I recognized Zayd' (ma'rifa) is informative. Practise this by constructing sentences that would require 'ilm vs ma'rifa.
For 'ilm, specify the attribute; for ma'rifa, the bare term suffices.

الباب الأول: الفصل الثاني- التعريفات
ثانياً من حيث المعنى
١ - المعرفة تتعلق بذات الشيء، والعلم يتعلق بأحواله، فقال سبحانه: ﴿فَاعْلَمْ أَنَّهُ لا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللهُ ﴾ [محمد: ١٩/٤٧]، وقال: ﴿اعْلَمُوا أَنَّ اللَّهَ شَدِيدُ الْعِقَابِ﴾ [المائدة: ٩٨/٥]، وقال: ﴿فَاعْلَمُوا أَنما أُنْزِلَ بِعِلْمِ اللهِ ﴾ [هود: ١٤/١١].
فالمعرفة إذن حضور صورة الشيء ومثاله العلمي في النفس، أما العلم فحضور أحواله وصفاته، ونسبتها إليه فالمعرفة تشبه التصور، والعلم يشبه التصديق. -٢- تأتي المعرفة غالباً لما غاب عن القلب بعد إدراكه، فإذا أدركه قيل عرفه، أو تكون لما وصف له بصفات قامت في نفسه. فإذا رآه وعلم أنه الموصوف بها قيل عرفه، قال تعالى: ﴿وَيَوْمَ يَحْشُرُهُمْ كَأَن لَمْ يَلْبَثُوا إلا ساعَةً مِنَ النهار يَتَعارَفُونَ بَيْنَهُمْ﴾ [يونس: ٤٥/١٠]، وقال: ﴿وَجَاءَ إِخْوَةُ يُوسُفَ فَدَخَلُوا عَلَيْهِ فَعَرَفَهُمْ وَهُمْ لَهُ مُنْكِرُونَ﴾ [يوسف: ٥٨/١٢]، وقال: ﴿الَّذِينَ آتَيْنَاهُمُ الْكِتَابَ يَعْرِفُونَهُ كَما يَعْرِفُونَ أَبْناءَهُم﴾ [البقرة: ١٤٦/٢، الأنعام: ٢٠/٦]، ذلك أن صفاته كانت معلومة لديهم، فرأوه أي عرفوه بتلك الصفات. ومن هذا يتضح أن المعرفة تشبه الذكر للشيء، وهو حضور ما كان غائباً عن الذكر. ولهذا كان ضد المعرفة الإنكار، وضدّ العلم الجهل، قال تعالى: ﴿يَعْرِفُونَ نِعْمَةَ اللهِ ثُمَّ يُنْكِرُونَها﴾ [النحل: ٨٣/١٦]، ويقال عرف الحق فأقر به، وعرفه فأنكره. تفيد المعرفة تمييز المعروف عن غيره، أما العلم فيفيد تمييز ما يوصف به غيره. والفرق بين هذا الفرق والذي سبقه أن الأول يرجع إلى إدراك عن صفاتها. أما هذا فيرجع إلى تخليص الذات من غيرها وتخليص صفات غيرها. إننا حين نقول: علمت زيداً لا نفيد المخاطب شيئاً فهو ينظر الحال التي عرفناه عليها، ولذلك فكان ينبغي القول علمت زيداً كريماً أو شجاعاً، كي تحصل الفائدة. ولكن قولنا: عرفت زيداً يفيد الإثبات والتمييز له عن غيره.
٤ - المعرفة هي العلم بعين الشيء مفصلاً عما سواه، بخلاف العلم فإنـه قـد يتعلق بالشيء مجملاً. وهذا الفرق نقله ابن القيم عن العسكري في فروقه وفروق غيره. أ. هـ. (۱)
Chapter One: Section Two – Definitions. Secondly, with respect to meaning. 1 – Ma'rifa pertains to the essence of a thing, and 'ilm pertains to its states. So He, exalted, said: 'Know that there is no god but Allah' [Muhammad 47:19], and said: 'Know that Allah is severe in punishment' [al-Ma'idah 5:98], and said: 'Know that it was sent down with the knowledge of Allah' [Hud 11:14]. Ma'rifa, therefore, is the presence of the image of a thing and its scientific likeness in the soul; as for 'ilm, it is the presence of its states and attributes and their relation to it. So ma'rifa resembles conception (tasawwur), and 'ilm resembles assent (tasdiq). 2 – Ma'rifa often comes for what was absent from the heart after its perception: when he perceives it, it is said 'he knows it', or it is for that which has been described to him with attributes that have been established in his soul. When he sees it and knows that it is the described one, it is said 'he knows it'. The Most High said: 'And on the Day when He will gather them, as if they had not tarried but an hour of the day, they will recognize one another' [Yunus 10:45], and said: 'And the brothers of Joseph came and entered upon him, and he recognized them while they were unaware of him' [Yusuf 12:58], and said: 'Those to whom We have given the Book recognize him as they recognize their own sons' [al-Baqarah 2:146, al-An'am 6:20]. That is because his attributes were known to them, so they saw him, i.e., they recognized him by those attributes. From this it becomes clear that ma'rifa resembles remembrance of a thing, which is the presence of what was absent from remembrance. For this reason, the opposite of ma'rifa is denial, and the opposite of 'ilm is ignorance. The Most High said: 'They recognize the favor of Allah, then they deny it' [al-Nahl 16:83], and it is said: he recognized the truth and affirmed it, and he recognized it and denied it. Ma'rifa gives the distinction of the known from others, while 'ilm gives the distinction of what is described by others. The difference between this distinction and the preceding one is that the former refers to perception of attributes, while this refers to isolating the essence from others and isolating its attributes from those of others. When we say 'I knew Zayd' (in the sense of 'ilm), we do not inform the addressee of anything; he looks at the condition in which we knew him. Therefore, one should say 'I knew Zayd as generous or brave' to obtain benefit. But our saying 'I recognized Zayd' (with ma'rifa) gives confirmation and distinction of him from others. 4 – Ma'rifa is knowledge of the very thing in detail as distinct from others, unlike 'ilm which may pertain to a thing in summary. This difference was transmitted by Ibn Qayyim from al-Askari in his 'Differences' and the differences of others. End.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage defines two key epistemological terms: ma'rifa (knowledge/cognition) and 'ilm (knowledge/science), distinguishing them through Quranic evidence and cognitive processes. The author begins by stating that ma'rifa relates to the essence of a thing, while 'ilm relates to its states. Three Quranic verses are cited to illustrate 'ilm as knowledge of matters like tawhid, punishment, and revelation. Ma'rifa is defined as the presence of the form or mental image of a thing in the soul, whereas 'ilm is the presence of its states, attributes, and relationships. This leads to the observation that ma'rifa resembles conception (tasawwur) and 'ilm resembles assent (tasdiq). The second point discusses the usage of ma'rifa: it often applies to something that was absent from the heart after having been perceived, or is based on prior description. The Quranic examples of mutual recognition on the Day of Judgment, Joseph recognizing his brothers, and the People of the Book recognizing the Prophet (like their own sons) show that recognition occurs through prior knowledge of attributes. Ma'rifa is thus likened to remembrance, bringing back what was absent. Its opposite is denial (inkar), while the opposite of 'ilm is ignorance (jahl), as in the verse about recognizing Allah's favor then denying it. Ma'rifa serves to distinguish the known from others, while 'ilm serves to distinguish what is described from others. The first difference (between the two distinctions) is that the former goes back to perception of attributes, while the latter is to isolate the essence from others and its attributes from others' attributes. An example: saying 'I knew Zayd' (with 'ilm) without specifying quality gives no benefit; one should say 'I knew Zayd as generous or brave'. But saying 'I recognized Zayd' (with ma'rifa) gives affirmation and distinction. The fourth point adds another definition from Ibn al-Qayyim and al-Askari: ma'rifa is knowledge of the thing in detail, distinguishing it from others, whereas 'ilm can be summary. This reinforces the idea that ma'rifa is more specific and detailed.

العلم
الإنكار
الجهل

Key Takeaway
Ma'rifa is detailed recognition that distinguishes the known, with denial as its opposite; 'ilm can be summary knowledge of attributes, with ignorance as its opposite.

The Logical Structure of Defining Tarbiyah
Analyzing linguistic roots to build a definition of tarbiyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the genus and differentia in any definition of tarbiyah and evaluate its completeness as a jami' mani' definition.

Core Idea
A jami' mani' definition of tarbiyah must include all dimensions of human growth and exclude non-Islamic paradigms.

This passage grounds tarbiyah in three linguistic roots, then traces how classical scholars derived a concept of gradual nurturing. Modern definitions add differentiae like physical, intellectual, and spiritual development. The author ultimately calls for a jami' mani' definition that distinguishes Islamic education from others. You will learn to dissect this definitional process and apply it to other Islamic concepts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three linguistic roots
Extract the three meanings of the root 'ر ب ب': increase/growth, being reared, and setting right/taking charge. Each supports a dimension of nurturing.
The Quranic verse and poetry illustrate each root.
2
Analyze classical conceptualization
See how al-Raghib al-Asfahani and al-Baydawi synthesize the roots into 'bringing a thing step by step to completion'. This is the genus of tarbiyah: a gradual process of perfection.
They define 'rabb' as tarbiyah itself.
3
Dissect the modern definitions
In the researcher's definition and the conference definition, identify the process (genus) and the specific aspects being developed (differentiae): physical, psychological, intellectual, spiritual, social, religious.
These definitions are rasm taam (descriptive) but not yet hadd.
4
Evaluate the call for jami' mani'
Understand why the author finds the previous definitions insufficient: they may not exclude non-Islamic educational concepts. A proper hadd must be exclusive (mani').
The author proposes a definition that 'distinguishes this education more from other types'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تعريف التربية
من استقراء أحد الباحثين التربويين لمادة (رب)، توصل إلى أصول لغوية ثلاثة لها: الأصل الأول: ربَّ . معنى زاد ونما وأتم . وفي هذا المعنى جاء قول الله تعالى: وَمَا آتَيْتُمْ مِنْ رِبَا لِيَرْبُوَ فِي أَمْوالِ النَّاسِ فَلَا يَرْبُو عِنْدَ اللَّهِ ﴾ [الروم: ٣٩/٣٠]. الأصل الثاني: ربي يربى على وزن خفي، ومعناها: نشأ وترعرع، وعليه قول ابن الأعرابي: فمن يك سائلاً عني فإني بمكة منزلي وبها ربيت الأصل الثالث: ربَّ يرُبُّ بوزن مدَّ ، بمعنى أصلحه وتولى أمره، وفي هذا قول حسان ابن ثابت: ولأنت أحسنُ إذ برزت لنا يوم الخروج بساحة القصر من دُرَّةٍ بيضاء صافية مما تربب حائر البحر أي الدرة التي يربيها الصدف في قعر الماء، والحائر مجتمع الماء.
وفي ضوء هذه الأصول اللغوية فسر الراغب الأصفهاني: (ت: ٥٠٢هـ) (الرب) بمعنى التربية فقال: الرب في الأصل التربية، وهو إنشاء الشيء حالاً فحالاً إلى حد التمام).
كما ذهب البيضاوي: (ت: ٦٨٥هـ) نحو هذا، إذ قال عند تفسيره لقول الله تعالى: ﴿ورَبِّ الْعالَمِينَ ﴾ [الفاتحة: ٢/١) الرب في الأصل بمعنى التربية: وهي تبليغ الشيء إلى كماله شيئاً فشيئاً).
وعلى أساس هذا المفهوم اللغوي والاصطلاحي عرّف أحد الباحثين التربية قائلاً: فالتربية عملية مقصودة تهدف إلى تربية الإنسان الصالح بتنمية طاقاته الجسمية والنفسية والعقلية والروحية وتتجه بها نحو الأفضل والأكمل، وتهدف كذلك إلى تنمية المجتمع والنهوض به بتلبية حاجاته المختلفة).
وكان المؤتمر العالمي الأول للتعليم الإسلامي المنعقد بمكة المكرمة (١٣٩٧هـ - ۱۹۷۷م) عرف التربية قريباً من هذا المعنى فقال إنهـا: رعاية الإنسان في جوانبه الجسمية والعقلية والعلمية واللغوية والوجدانية والاجتماعية والدينية وتوجيهها نحو الصلاح، والوصول بها إلى الكمال).
ومع أن هذه التعريفات مختارة من بين تعريفات كثيرة للتربية الإسلامية لكنها قد لا تقتصر عليها بضرورة منطوق هذه التعريفات، إلا أن يستصحب المرء شخصيات أصحابها بوصفهم مسلمين يؤمنون بوجود (التربية الإسلامية) وقدرتها وفاعليتها على تحقيق أهدافها وتجسيد مفردات العملية التربوية في فلسفة التربية الإسلامية بيد أن طبيعة هذه الدراسة تفرض على صاحبها الإفصاح أكثر عن مقصوده بالتربية الإسلامية. ولذلك فإن أنسب تعريف جامع مانع للتربية الإسلامية تفرضه طبيعة هذه الدراسة، وينسجم مع التعريفات السالفة في مجملها بيد أنه يميز أكثر هذه التربية عما عداهـا مـن أنـواع التربيات
Definition of Tarbiyah. From the investigation of one educational researcher into the root (رب), he concluded that it has three linguistic origins: The first origin: rabba, meaning increased, grew, and completed. In this meaning came the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'And whatever you give of usury [riba] to increase within the wealth of people will not increase with Allah' [Quran 30:39]. The second origin: rabiya yarbā on the pattern of khafiya, meaning grew up and was reared. Upon this is the saying of Ibn al-A'rabi: 'Whoever asks about me, then indeed I am in Makkah, my home, and in it I was reared.' The third origin: rabba yarubbu on the pattern of madda, meaning he set it right and took charge of it. In this is the saying of Hassan ibn Thabit: 'And you are more beautiful when you appeared to us on the day of departure in the courtyard of the palace, than a white pure pearl, from what the oyster of the sea nourishes.' That is, the pearl that the shell nurtures at the bottom of the water, and al-ha'ir is the gathering of water. In light of these linguistic origins, al-Raghib al-Asfahani (d. 502 AH) interpreted (al-Rabb) as meaning tarbiyah, saying: 'Al-Rabb originally means tarbiyah, which is bringing a thing into existence stage by stage until it reaches completion.' Likewise, al-Baydawi (d. 685 AH) went towards this, as he said in his interpretation of the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'Lord of the worlds' [Quran 1:2]: 'Al-Rabb originally means tarbiyah, which is bringing a thing to its perfection little by little.' And on the basis of this linguistic and technical concept, one researcher defined tarbiyah saying: 'So tarbiyah is a purposeful process aiming to nurture the righteous human by developing his physical, psychological, intellectual, and spiritual potentialities and directing them towards the best and most complete, and also aiming to develop society and advance it by fulfilling its various needs.' And the First World Conference on Islamic Education held in Makkah al-Mukarramah (1397 AH - 1977 CE) defined tarbiyah close to this meaning, saying it is: 'The care of the human in his physical, intellectual, scientific, linguistic, emotional, social, and religious aspects and directing them towards righteousness, and reaching with them perfection.' And although these definitions are chosen from among many definitions of Islamic education, they may not be confined to them by necessity of the wording of these definitions, unless one considers the personalities of their authors as Muslims who believe in the existence of (Islamic education) and its ability and effectiveness to achieve its goals and embody the elements of the educational process in the philosophy of Islamic education. However, the nature of this study imposes on its author to disclose more about his intended meaning of Islamic education. Therefore, the most suitable comprehensive and exclusive (jami' mani') definition of Islamic education which the nature of this study requires, and which is consistent with the previous definitions in their entirety, but distinguishes this education more from other types of education.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage defines 'tarbiyah' (education/upbringing) by first analyzing its linguistic roots and then presenting technical definitions from classical and modern scholars. It begins by citing a researcher who identified three Arabic verbal roots for the triliteral root (رب): (1) 'rabba' (to increase, grow), (2) 'rabiya' (to be reared), and (3) 'rabba' (to set right, take charge). Each root is illustrated with a Quranic verse or line of poetry. The passage then shows how classical exegetes like al-Raghib al-Asfahani and al-Baydawi derived the concept of tarbiyah from these roots, defining it as the gradual bringing of something to completion. Modern definitions are then provided: one from a researcher describing tarbiyah as a purposeful process developing all human faculties, and another from the First World Conference on Islamic Education emphasizing comprehensive care and guidance towards perfection. Finally, the author notes that these definitions, while selected, do not exhaust the concept; the study's nature requires a more precise 'jami' mani'' (comprehensive and exclusive) definition that distinguishes Islamic education from other types. This passage exemplifies the logical process of definition: starting from linguistic origins (the basis for genus), moving to technical definitions (adding differentiae), and refining to ensure exclusivity.

Key Takeaway
A rigorous definition of tarbiyah must be both comprehensive (jami') covering all developmental dimensions and exclusive (mani') distinguishing Islamic education from other paradigms.

The Comprehensive Definition of Islamic Education
Author defines Islamic education as a comprehensive process.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the author's definition of Islamic education and identify its distinguishing feature (governance by the Islamic vision).

Core Idea
Islamic education integrates spirit, mind, psyche, and body under an Islamic worldview.

The author presents a multi-dimensional definition that goes beyond school subjects. This definition emphasizes holistic preparation for both this world and the Hereafter, governed by the comprehensive Islamic system. Understanding this definition is key to grasping the full scope of Islamic education.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum
Find the term being defined: التربية الإسلامية (Islamic education). The author provides a full sentence definition.
The definition appears near the beginning of the passage.
2
List the four aspects covered
The definition mentions spiritual, mental, psychological, and physical aspects. Note these as the dimensions of preparation.
These correspond to الروحية والعقلية والنفسية والجسمية.
3
Identify the purpose
The definition states it aims to enhance desired behavior and modify undesired behavior, for the life of this world and the Hereafter.
The purpose spans both worldly and afterlife success.
4
Extract the distinguishing element
The author emphasizes that this definition is governed by the Islamic vision (التصور الإسلامي). This is unique and separates it from other definitions.
The phrase 'محكومة بالتصور الإسلامي' is key.
