الباب الأول: الفصل الثاني- التعريفات

الأخرى، يمكن صياغته على النحو التالي: التربية الإسلامية عبارة عن عملية إعداد منظم شامل متكامل للفرد والمجتمع من جميع الجوانب الروحية والعقلية والنفسية والجسمية للحياة الدنيا والآخرة عبر جميع مراحل النمو، بهدف تعزيز السلوك المرغوب وتعديل غير المرغوب، وذلك في إطار النظام الإسلامي الشامل.

وثمة تأكيدان يحسن الإشارة إليهما

الأول: لعلَّ هذا التعريف يحدّد المراد أكثر بمقصود التربية الإسلامية من خلال التأكيد على جوانب الروح والنفس والعقل والجسم وذلك ما يشاطر بـه هذا التعريف جملة التعريفات المختارة المشار إليها سابقاً، بيد أن التنصيص على كونها محكومة بالتصور الإسلامي هو المميز له تماماً.

الثاني: يبدو أن تعريف التربية الإسلامية المتبنى في هذه الدراسة، قد ألمح بصورة ضمنية إلى أن التعريف المدرسي للتربية الإسلامية، حين يطلق على جملة المواد المتصلة بعلوم الشريعة المقررة على الطلبة في المدارس لا يعني سوى المعنى الخاص للتربية الإسلامية، أما المعنى العام لها فهو التعريف المشار إليه آنفاً. مـع ملاحظة أن ليس ثمة اختلاف بينهما إلا من حيث العموم والخصوص، من غير أن يُشعر ذلك بوجود فصل للخاص عن العام، ولكن حصر المعنى في الخاص فحسب، هو التضييق للواسع، ولذلك كان لا بد من هذا التأكيد أيضاً.
Chapter One: Section Two - Definitions

[...] it can be formulated as follows: Islamic education is a process of organized, comprehensive, integrated preparation of the individual and society from all spiritual, mental, psychological, and physical aspects for the life of this world and the hereafter, through all stages of growth, with the aim of enhancing desired behavior and modifying undesired behavior, within the framework of the comprehensive Islamic system.

There are two emphases worth noting:

First: This definition perhaps specifies more what is meant by Islamic education by emphasizing the aspects of spirit, psyche, mind, and body. This is what this definition shares with the set of selected definitions previously referred to, but the stipulation that it is governed by the Islamic vision is what distinguishes it completely.

Second: It seems that the definition of Islamic education adopted in this study has implicitly hinted that the school definition of Islamic education, when applied to the set of subjects related to the religious sciences prescribed for students in schools, means only the specific meaning of Islamic education. As for the general meaning, it is the definition referred to above. Noting that there is no difference between them except in terms of generality and specificity, without that indicating a separation of the specific from the general. But restricting meaning solely to the specific is a narrowing of the broad, and therefore this emphasis was also necessary.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage is a definitional exposition from a modern work on Islamic education. It begins by presenting a comprehensive definition of Islamic education as an organized process covering spiritual, mental, psychological, and physical dimensions, aimed at the life of this world and the hereafter, within an Islamic framework. The author then highlights two key emphases. The first emphasis is that this definition, while sharing elements with other definitions, is distinct because it explicitly states that it is governed by the Islamic worldview. The second emphasis draws a crucial distinction: the school-level meaning of 'Islamic education' (referring to religious subjects) is only the specific sense, whereas the general sense is the broader process described. The author clarifies that these two are not separate; rather, the specific is a narrower application of the general. Confining the term only to the specific would be an unjustified restriction. This distinction is important for avoiding confusion in discourse about Islamic education.

General vs Specific Meaning of Islamic Education
Author distinguishes general and specific meanings of Islamic education.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the general and specific meanings of Islamic education and explain why restricting to the specific is problematic.

Core Idea
The school definition is just the specific branch, not the whole tree.

The author addresses a common misunderstanding: when people say 'Islamic education' in schools, they usually mean only the religious subjects. But this is only the specific meaning. The general meaning is the broader holistic process. The two are not separate; the specific is a part of the general. Restricting the term to only the specific meaning distorts the concept.

Guided Path
1
Identify the specific meaning
Find where the author describes the specific meaning: it refers to the set of subjects related to religious sciences (shari'a sciences) taught in schools.
The phrase 'جملة المواد المتصلة بعلوم الشريعة' indicates this.
2
Identify the general meaning
The general meaning is the comprehensive definition given earlier in the passage: the holistic process of preparation covering all aspects.
This is the primary definition in the first part.
3
Analyze the relationship
The author states there is no difference except in generality and specificity; the specific is not separate from the general. They are related as part to whole.
The phrase 'ليس ثمة اختلاف بينهما إلا من حيث العموم والخصوص' is key.
4
Understand the consequence of restriction
If one uses only the specific meaning, it narrows the broad concept ('تضييق للواسع'). The author warns against this.
This is why the second emphasis is necessary.

الباب الأول: الفصل الثاني- التعريفات

الأخرى، يمكن صياغته على النحو التالي: التربية الإسلامية عبارة عن عملية إعداد منظم شامل متكامل للفرد والمجتمع من جميع الجوانب الروحية والعقلية والنفسية والجسمية للحياة الدنيا والآخرة عبر جميع مراحل النمو، بهدف تعزيز السلوك المرغوب وتعديل غير المرغوب، وذلك في إطار النظام الإسلامي الشامل.

وثمة تأكيدان يحسن الإشارة إليهما

الأول: لعلَّ هذا التعريف يحدّد المراد أكثر بمقصود التربية الإسلامية من خلال التأكيد على جوانب الروح والنفس والعقل والجسم وذلك ما يشاطر بـه هذا التعريف جملة التعريفات المختارة المشار إليها سابقاً، بيد أن التنصيص على كونها محكومة بالتصور الإسلامي هو المميز له تماماً.

الثاني: يبدو أن تعريف التربية الإسلامية المتبنى في هذه الدراسة، قد ألمح بصورة ضمنية إلى أن التعريف المدرسي للتربية الإسلامية، حين يطلق على جملة المواد المتصلة بعلوم الشريعة المقررة على الطلبة في المدارس لا يعني سوى المعنى الخاص للتربية الإسلامية، أما المعنى العام لها فهو التعريف المشار إليه آنفاً. مـع ملاحظة أن ليس ثمة اختلاف بينهما إلا من حيث العموم والخصوص، من غير أن يُشعر ذلك بوجود فصل للخاص عن العام، ولكن حصر المعنى في الخاص فحسب، هو التضييق للواسع، ولذلك كان لا بد من هذا التأكيد أيضاً.

Three Definitions of the Unseen World
Author presents three definitions of the unseen world

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the three definitions of the unseen (al-ghayb) presented in the passage and identify their key features.

Core Idea
Definitions of the unseen range from transcendent reality to sensory absence; each determines the role of revelation.

This passage introduces the first field of knowledge: the unseen (al-ghayb). Different researchers have proposed three definitions, each with distinct implications for how we access knowledge of the unseen. Understanding these definitions is essential for evaluating their epistemological foundations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first definition
Locate the first definition in the Arabic: it describes the unseen as a world of rational, spiritual nature transcendent of matter, not subject to human witnessing.
This definition emphasizes transcendence and limits human perception to effects only.
2
Identify the second definition
Find the second definition: it restricts knowledge of the unseen to God alone, who reveals it to chosen servants via revelation.
This definition centers on divine exclusivity and prophecy.
3
Identify the third definition
Find the third definition: it defines the unseen as every matter absent from customary sensory perception.
This definition is based on human sensory ability rather than inherent nature.
4
Compare the roles of revelation and sensory perception
Notice that the first two definitions ground the unseen in its essence (transcendence) or divine will, while the third ties it to human sensory capacity.
This difference is the basis for the author's later critique.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثاني: الفصل الثاني- ميدان المعرفة - الغيب والشهادة الميدان الأول الغيب

التعريف: سبقت الإشارة إلى أن عالم الغيب يمثل ما وراء المحسوس إجمالاً، ولكن سعى بعض الباحثين لمحاولة وضع تعريفات جامعة ومنها: - عالم الغيب عالم ذو طبيعة عقلية معنوية متعالية عن المادة، ولذلك فإنه ليس بعالم قابل للشهود الإنساني، بل يدرك الإنسان ثبوته وآثاره فحسب كالوجود الإلهي، ووجود الملائكة والجن والجنة والنار، وغيرها من الموجودات الغيبية، والله تعالى وحده الذي يحيط علمه بعالمي الغيب والشهادة جميعاً) (۱). عالم الغيب عالم يخص به علم الله وحده، يوحي ما يشاء من أمره على من يشاء من عباده، ويرسلهم بالرسالات إلى الأمم هداية وتبصيراً لمعنى وجودهم، وغاية هذا الوجود، وعلاقته ومآله))(۲). - عالم الغيب كل أمر غائب عن مجال إدراكنا الحسي العادة (۳).

ونجد أن صاحب هذا التعريف الأخير يعود ليقرر أن مناط عالم الغيب قائم على عدم قدرتنا على مشاهدة ما غاب عن حواسنا، وعليه فإن أموراً كانت غيباً يوماً ما، ثم غدت مشاهدة لا تعدّ من عالم الغيب، بل من عالم الشهادة. ومثال ذلك أمر الجنّ إذ لو تمكن البحث العلمي عن طريق التجربة والاختبار، واستخدام بعض القوى الكونية - أن يتصل بالجنّ مثلاً اتصالاً عادياً لأصبح أمر الجن ضمن عالم الشهادة، والتي كانت فيما سبق في إطار عالم الغيب الذي سبيله الوحيد الوحي. وكذلك الحال في مثل قدرة الأبحاث الجنينية التنبؤ بما في بطن الحامل من جنس المولود، فإن هذا لم يعد غيباً، بل غدا جزءاً
Chapter Two: Section Two - Field of Knowledge – The Unseen and the Witnessed. The First Field: The Unseen. Definition: It was previously indicated that the world of the unseen represents what is beyond the sensory in general, but some researchers have attempted to formulate comprehensive definitions, including: - The world of the unseen is a world of a rational, spiritual nature transcendent of matter, and therefore it is not a world subject to human witnessing, rather man perceives only its existence and effects, such as the divine existence, the existence of angels, jinn, paradise, hellfire, and other unseen beings, and God Almighty alone encompasses with His knowledge both worlds of the unseen and the witnessed (1). - The world of the unseen is a world that God's knowledge alone specializes in; He reveals what He wills of His command to whomever He wills of His servants, and sends them with messages to nations as guidance and insight into the meaning of their existence, the purpose of this existence, its relationship and ultimate outcome (2). - The world of the unseen is every matter absent from the scope of our customary sensory perception (3). We find that the author of this last definition goes on to assert that the basis of the world of the unseen rests on our inability to observe what is absent from our senses, and accordingly, matters that were unseen one day and then became observed are not counted as part of the world of the unseen, but rather of the world of the witnessed. An example of that is the matter of jinn: if scientific research through experiment and testing, and the use of some cosmic powers, were able to contact jinn in an ordinary manner, then the matter of jinn would become part of the world of the witnessed, whereas previously it was within the framework of the world of the unseen whose only path is revelation. Similarly, the case of the ability of embryonic research to predict the sex of the fetus in the pregnant woman's womb: this is no longer unseen, but has become a part...
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage begins a new section focusing on the first field: the unseen (al-ghayb). The author provides definitions from various researchers. The first definition characterizes the unseen world as rational, spiritual, transcendent of matter, not subject to human witnessing; humans perceive only its existence and effects, like God, angels, jinn, paradise, hellfire. Only God encompasses knowledge of both worlds. The second definition restricts knowledge of the unseen to God alone; He reveals what He wills to chosen servants via revelation. The third definition defines the unseen as anything absent from our customary sensory perception. The author then critiques this third definition, noting that its proponent bases the unseen on our inability to observe with our senses. Consequently, things that were once unseen but become observable are no longer unseen but part of the witnessed realm. The author gives examples: jinn, if science could contact them, would become witnessed; similarly, prenatal sex determination via embryonic research was once unseen but is now known. This critique highlights the instability of defining the unseen purely relative to human sensory capacity, as it may change with scientific progress.

Key Terms
عالم الغيب
الشهود
المحسوس
الوحي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the first definition in the passage, what is the nature of the world of the unseen?
A) It is material and observable.
B) It is rational and spiritual, transcendent of matter.
C) It is known only through prophecy.
D) It is whatever is absent from our senses.

Key Takeaway
The unseen is defined either as a transcendent reality known through revelation or as whatever lies beyond current human sensory reach.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Compare the first and second definitions: what is the role of human reason in each? Why might a theologian prefer the first over the second?

Critique of Sensory-Based Definition of the Unseen
Author critiques the third definition's reliance on sensory perception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the author's critique of the third definition of the unseen and reconstruct the argument's logical form.

Core Idea
Defining the unseen by sensory absence makes it unstable; scientific progress can turn the unseen into the witnessed.

The author critiques the third definition because it ties the unseen to human sensory ability. Using examples of jinn and fetal sex determination, he shows that what is unseen today may become seen tomorrow. This challenges the exclusive role of revelation in knowledge of the unseen.

Guided Path
1
Restate the third definition
The third definition says the unseen is every matter absent from customary sensory perception.
2
Identify the author's objection
The author argues that if something becomes observable, it ceases to be unseen, making the definition contingent on human capability.
He gives examples: jinn if contacted by science, fetal sex determined by embryology.
3
Reconstruct the logical argument
The argument is conditional: If X becomes observable, then X is no longer unseen. Therefore, the definition is unstable because it depends on human progress.
We can formalize it as: P → Q, where P = 'science observes X' and Q = 'X is not unseen'.
4
Assess the strength of the critique
The critique is logically valid; it shows that a sensory-based definition cannot provide a fixed category for the unseen.
The author implies that a proper definition should be based on the thing's essence, not our ability to perceive it.

Source Text

Critiquing the Division of Ghayb
Author presents and critiques a proposed division of the unseen.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two-part division of ghayb proposed by some researchers and evaluate the author's two critiques of that division.

Core Idea
The unseen is epistemologically unified; dividing it is problematic.

In this lesson, we examine a proposed division of the unseen (ghayb) into two categories: one that might become observable under certain conditions, and another that remains exclusively known to Allah. The author presents two key observations that challenge this division, reinforcing the unity of ghayb as a holistic concept. Understanding this critique is essential for grasping the epistemological foundations of Quranic narratives.

Guided Path
1
Identify the proposed division
Locate in the text the two parts of ghayb as described by some researchers: one that can become observable (shahada) if conditions are prepared, and another that remains exclusive to Allah's knowledge.
The division is based on potential observability by creatures.
2
Understand the proponent's motivation
Why do researchers think ghayb can be divided? They imagine that what is unseen for humans might be witnessed by jinn or angels, so ghayb is relative to the observer.
3
Analyze the first critique
The author previously defined ghayb as 'what is definitively absent from the senses' (qat’iyyan). This excludes conjectural matters. The first category of the division (potentially observable) is problematic because it relies on hypothetical conditions, not definitive absence.
The definition is key: ghayb is not about what could be seen, but what cannot be seen at all.
4
Analyze the second critique
The division improperly brings in non-human creatures (jinn, angels) into the discussion of knowledge. The author's focus is specifically on human epistemology; other creatures have different capacities.
Thus the division is irrelevant to the study of human knowledge of the unseen.
5
Synthesize the conclusion
The author emphasizes the unity and totality of ghayb: though its types and manifestations are diverse, they all fall under one holistic concept. The proposed division is rejected.

تِلْكَ مِنْ أَنباء الْغَيْبِ نُوحِيها إلَيْكَ ما كُنتَ تَعْلَمُها أَنْتَ وَلَا قَوْمُكَ مِنْ قَبْلِ هَذَا فَاصْبِرْ إِنَّ الْعَاقِبَةَ لِلْمُتَّقِينَ﴾ [هود: ٤٩/١١]. وعن يوسف - عليه السلام: وَذَلِكَ مِنْ أَنْبَاءِ الْغَيْبِ نُوحِيهِ إِلَيْكَ وَمَا كُنتَ لَدَيْهِمْ إِذْ أَجْمَعُوا أَمْرَهُمْ وَهُمْ يَمْكُرُونَ﴾ [يوسف: ۱۰۲/۱۲]. والمحتوى الدراسي معني باعتماد أخبار القرآن وقصصه، وجعلها في أعلى مراتب الصحة رواية ودراية وأساليب المنهج معنية بدورها في جعل أسلوب القصة أحد الأساليب المرعية عند تقديمها للمحتوى. هل يُجَزا الغيب؟ يذهب بعض الباحثين إلى تجزئة الغيب بوضعه في قسمين: أحدهما: قسم قابل لأن يكون من عالم الشهادة إذا تهيأت للمخلوقات شروط مشاهدته. الآخر: قسم غير قابل لأن يكون من عالم الشهادة لأنه مما استأثر الله تعالى - بعلمه لنفسه. ولعلّ دافع صاحب هذا التقسيم هو مفهومه لمعنى الغيب - وقد مر معنا - ثم تصوره لإمكان أن تكون هناك أشياء من عالم الغيب بالنسبة إلى الإنسان، لكنها قد تكون من عالم الشهادة بالنسبة إلى الجن أو الملائكة أو مخلوقات أخرى. بيد أن ثمة ملحوظتين على هذا التقسيم: الأولى: سبق أن تم تبني تعريف الغيب بما غاب عن الحواس على نحو قاطع خروجاً من الوقوع في أمور ظنية تحسب من الغيب، وماهي من الغيب عند التحقيق في أمرها. الثانية: إن الباحث صاحب هذا التقسيم يُدخل مخلوقات غير الإنسان في مسألة المعرفة مع أن مدار بحثنا هنا هو المعرفة لدى الإنسان، لما يمتاز به عن سائر الكائنات، وعليه فإن هذا التقسيم غير ذي موضوع بالنسبة إلى هذه الدراسة على الأقل. ويبقى التأكيد على وحدة عالم الغيب وكليته، وعدم تجزئته على تلك الصورة، فالغيب وإن تعددت أنواعه و تشعبت مظاهره، فإن هذا التنوع وذلك التشعب يدور في إطار المفهوم الكلّي للغيب، ليس أكثر.
These are from the news of the unseen; We reveal them to you; you did not know them, nor your people, before this. So be patient; indeed, the [best] outcome is for the righteous. [Hud 11:49]. And about Yusuf - peace be upon him: And that is from the news of the unseen which We reveal to you; and you were not with them when they agreed upon their plan while they conspired. [Yusuf 12:102]. The study content is concerned with adopting the Quranic news and stories, and placing them at the highest level of authenticity in narration and knowledge, and the methods of the approach are concerned with their role in making the story style one of the approved methods when presenting the content. Can the unseen be divided? Some researchers go to dividing the unseen by placing it into two parts: One: a part that can be from the world of the witnessed if conditions for its observation are prepared for creatures. The other: a part that cannot be from the world of the witnessed because it is what Allah Almighty has kept exclusive to Himself in knowledge. Perhaps the motive of the proponent of this division is his concept of the meaning of the unseen - which has passed with us - then his imagining that there could be things from the world of the unseen for humans, but they might be from the world of the witnessed for jinn or angels or other creatures. However, there are two observations on this division: The first: the definition of the unseen has previously been adopted as what is definitively absent from the senses, to avoid falling into conjectural matters that are considered unseen, but are not from the unseen when investigated. The second: the researcher proponent of this division brings in creatures other than humans into the issue of knowledge, whereas our focus here is knowledge in humans, due to what distinguishes humans from other beings. Accordingly, this division is irrelevant to this study at least. And the emphasis remains on the unity of the unseen world and its totality, and not dividing it in that manner; for the unseen, even if its types are numerous and its manifestations diverse, this diversity and ramification revolve within the framework of the holistic concept of the unseen, nothing more.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage discusses the concept of the unseen (ghayb) and critiques a proposed division of it. The author begins by quoting two Quranic verses that emphasize that certain knowledge comes only from divine revelation, establishing the authority of the Quran in matters of the unseen. Then the author notes that the study content relies on Quranic narratives as authentic and methodologically sound. The key question is whether ghayb can be divided. Some researchers propose a division into two categories: one that can potentially become observable (shahada) under certain conditions, and another that remains exclusively known to Allah. The author suggests that the proponent's motivation stems from a previous understanding of ghayb and the idea that what is unseen for humans might be witnessed by other beings like jinn or angels. However, the author presents two critiques. First, the earlier definition of ghayb as what is definitively (qat'iyyan) absent from the senses excludes conjectural matters, so the first category of the division is problematic because it relies on hypothetical observability. Second, the division improperly includes non-human creatures in the epistemological discussion, which is focused on human knowledge. Therefore, the division is irrelevant to this study. The author concludes by reaffirming the unity and totality of the unseen: although its manifestations may be diverse, they all fall under one holistic concept.

Key Takeaway
The division of ghayb based on potential observability by other creatures is invalid for human epistemology; ghayb remains a unified concept defined by definitive absence from the senses.

Parsing the Definition of the Witnessed World
Author defines the witnessed world and contrasts it with the unseen.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to parse the definition of 'alam al-shahada and identify its components: sensory means, custom, and the contrast with the unseen.

Core Idea
The witnessed world is defined by sensory accessibility, not by physical existence alone.

How do Islamic scholars define the realm of empirical knowledge? In this lesson, we analyse the definition of 'alam al-shahada provided by al-Maydani and cited by the author. Understanding this definition is crucial for distinguishing between what can be known through observation and what remains in the unseen (ghayb), a distinction that underpins Islamic epistemology and sciences like usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum
The term being defined is 'alam al-shahada (عالم الشهادة). Locate it in the Arabic passage. Note that it is introduced as 'The Other Field' before the definition.
The definiendum is the subject of definition.
2
Extract the genus and differentia
The definition states: 'everything that we can attain its witnessing through the sensory means within us according to custom.' The genus is 'everything' (كل أمر), a universal category. The differentia is 'we can witness it through sensory means customarily.'
The differentia consists of two parts: sensory means and the customary condition.
3
Analyze the qualifier 'according to custom'
The phrase 'حسب العادة' limits witnessing to what is normally perceptible by humans. This excludes extraordinary sensory abilities or temporary impairments. Consider why this qualifier is important for a stable epistemological framework.
Custom here refers to the normal functioning of human senses.
4
Contrast with the unseen
The passage earlier contrasted the witnessed world with the unseen (غيب). How does this definition exclude the unseen? The unseen is precisely what cannot be sensed. Understanding this contrast helps define the scope of empirical inquiry in Islam.
The unseen includes things like the afterlife, angels, or divine essence.

الميدان الآخر: الشهادة
إذا كان عالم الغيب ميداناً للمعرفة الغيبية؛ فإن عالم الشهادة ميدان للمعرفة المشاهدة والتي يمكن تعقلها بالتعاون مع الحواس. ولأن الكون هــو مـيـدان عـالـم الشهادة ذاته فإن مذهبية الإسلام تقوم في نظرتها إليه على أساس التكامل والتوازن، لأنها قائمة في الأساس على مواجهته والتعامل معه بحسبانه ميدانـاً للإنجازات العظيمة، عن طريق تسخير القوانين المودعة فيه، من خلال عقلانية حاسمة قائمة على أساس السببية والتوافقية و التعامل المباشر مع أجزائه. ولهذا فلا مجال فيه للغيبية ولا للتأمل الاستغراقي الغنوصي ) .

The Other Field: The Witnessed
If the world of the unseen is a field for unseen knowledge, then the world of the witnessed is a field for witnessed knowledge which can be apprehended with the cooperation of the senses. And because the universe itself is the field of the witnessed world, the Islamic doctrinal stance regarding it is based on integration and balance, because it is fundamentally built on confronting and dealing with it as a field for great achievements, by harnessing the laws deposited in it, through a decisive rationality based on causality, compatibility, and direct interaction with its parts. Hence, there is no room in it for occultism nor for immersive gnostic contemplation.
The Definition
(2)
The world of the witnessed can be defined as: everything that we can attain its witnessing through the sensory means within us according to custom. (3)
(1) Abdul Hamid Abu Sulayman, Crisis of the Muslim Mind, 110.
(2) Muhsin Abdul Hamid, Renewal of Islamic Thought, 118. Gnosticism is a syncretic doctrine combining philosophy and religion based on the idea of emanation and mixing knowledges. Academy of the Arabic Language, Philosophical Dictionary, 133. See also: Philosophical Dictionary by Murad Wahba, 298, and Dictionary of Arabic Terms by Majdi Wahba and Kamil al-Muhandis, 267.
(3) al-Maydani, Islamic Creed, 28.
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage begins a new subsection titled 'The Other Field: The Witnessed,' establishing a clear counterpart to the earlier discussion of the unseen. The author first characterizes the witnessed world as the realm of knowledge obtained through sensory cooperation. Unlike the unseen, this field is open to empirical investigation. The Islamic approach to the witnessed world is described as one of integration and balance, rejecting both occultism (ghaybiyya) and gnostic immersion. The universe is seen as a field for harnessing laws through rationality based on causality and compatibility. The passage then provides a formal definition of the witnessed world, quoting al-Maydani: it is everything that can be witnessed through the sensory means inherent in us, according to custom. This definition highlights the empirical and customary nature of witnessing—it is not absolute but relative to normal human faculties. The footnotes clarify the term 'gnosticism' and provide sources. This definition is crucial for understanding the scope of empirical knowledge in Islamic thought.

Definition and Properties of Al-Shahada
Defines the realm of the witnessed and explains its properties and epistemological tools.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the nature of al-shahada and distinguish the roles of sense, intellect, and revelation in studying it.

Core Idea
Al-shahada is the sensed universe, comprehensible by intellect, but neither tool works without revelation's guidance.

In classical Islamic epistemology, the realm of 'al-shahada' (the witnessed) contrasts with 'al-ghayb' (the unseen). This passage defines al-shahada's essence and explains how we come to know it. You will see how sense perception is primary, yet intellect and revelation are indispensable partners.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum and definition
Find the term being defined and the exact wording of the definition. The passage begins with 'ويعرفه آخر بـ' – it presents a definition from another source.
The definition: 'هذا الوجود المادي الواقع تحت الإدراك الحسي للإنسان'
2
Extract genus and differentia
The genus (jins) is 'material existence' (الوجود المادي). The differentia (fasl) is 'that falls under human sensory perception' (الواقع تحت الإدراك الحسي للإنسان). Also note the property: 'معقول الذات' (intellectually comprehensible).
The definition is a hadd haqiqi (real definition) with an added property.
3
List the epistemological tools
The passage mentions three tools: sense (الحس), intellect (العقل), and revelation (الوحي).
Sense is primary; intellect follows senses; revelation guides both.
4
Explain the relationship between tools
Sense is the main tool of inquiry in shahada. The intellect operates but depends on senses as perceptual channels. Neither can function independently; revelation guides and supports them.
The passage says: 'لا يمكن الاستقلال بأي من الأداتين' (independence from either tool is not possible).
5
Apply to educational goal
The learner's cognitive act should stay within the sensed universe, using sensory tools primarily, then employing intellect for vicegerency, all within revelation's framework.
This ensures knowledge is grounded and guided.

ويعرفه آخر بـ ((هذا الوجود المادي الواقع تحت الإدراك الحسي للإنسان، أو الذي يمكن أن يقع تحته. ومن خصائصه أنه معقول الذات قابل للوجود الإنساني، إذا توفرت أسباب الشهود) (۱). إن هذين التعريفين يتفقان من حيث المضمون على طبيعة عالم الشهادة وخصائصه وأداة البحث فيه. فطبيعة هذا العالم هو الكون المحسوس وخصيصته إمكان تعقله، وأداة البحث فيه هي الحس، وإن كان العقل أداة عاملة فيه لكنها تتبع الحواس، باعتبار هذه الحواس منافذ إدراكية للعقل. وفي كلا الحالين لا يمكن الاستقلال بأي من الأداتين، فثمة مصدرية الوحي وطريقته الذي يعمل على توجيه مسار البحث في ميدان الشهادة. والمضمون التربوي لميدان الشهادة من هذه الزاوية متوجه نحو جعل الفعل المعرفي للمتعلم لا يخرج عن إطار الكون المحسوس، بحيث يتمكن من التعامل معه بأدوات حسية بالدرجة الأساس، ثم إعمال قوى العقل فيه بهدف استثماره لتحقيق هدف الاستخلاف، ولكن دون أن يتعارض ذلك وتوجيهات الوحي، بل هو المسند لكل من الحس والعقل.
And another defines it as: 'This material existence that falls under the sensory perception of humans, or that which can fall under it. And among its characteristics is that it is intellectually comprehensible in essence, susceptible to human existence, if the causes of witnessing are present.' These two definitions agree in content on the nature of the world of testimony, its characteristics, and the tool of inquiry in it. The nature of this world is the sensed universe, and its distinctive feature is the possibility of its intellectual comprehension, and the tool of inquiry in it is sense, although the intellect is an operative tool in it, but it follows the senses, considering these senses as perceptual channels for the intellect. In both cases, independence from either tool is not possible; rather there is the source of revelation and its method, which works to guide the course of inquiry in the realm of testimony. The educational content of the realm of testimony from this perspective is directed towards making the learner's cognitive act not exceed the framework of the sensed universe, so that they can deal with it primarily with sensory tools, then employ the powers of the intellect in it for the purpose of investing it to achieve the goal of vicegerency, but without contradicting the directives of revelation; rather, it is the support for both sense and intellect.
Source pages p. 159

Commentary
This passage defines the realm of al-shahada (the witnessed) and discusses its nature, characteristics, and epistemological tools. It begins with a definition from another source, describing it as material existence that falls under human sensory perception or can potentially do so. A key property is that it is 'ma'qul al-dhat' (intellectually comprehensible in essence) and susceptible to human existence given appropriate conditions of witnessing. The author then notes that the two definitions agree on the nature of this realm, its characteristics, and the primary tool of inquiry. The nature is the sensed universe; its distinctive feature is the possibility of intellectual comprehension. The primary tool of inquiry is sense perception, though the intellect operates but follows the senses, which serve as perceptual channels for the intellect. Neither tool can operate independently; revelation also guides the inquiry. Finally, the educational implication is that the learner should not exceed the framework of the sensed universe, using sensory tools primarily, then employing the intellect for vicegerency, all while being supported and guided by revelation.

Key Terms
الشهادة (al-shahada): The realm of the witnessed, i.e., the material universe accessible to sensory perception. [Note: No significant shift — consistent across Islamic epistemology.]
الوجود المادي (al-wujud al-madi): Material existence, the observable physical world. [Note: No significant shift.]

Evaluating Definitions Using Jami' Mani'
Author lists and evaluates definitions of mankind

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate a definition of a species using the criteria of comprehensiveness (jami') and exclusiveness (mani'), and identify its genus and differentia.

Core Idea
A proper definition must include all members and exclude all non-members: the jami' mani' test.

In Islamic logic, a sound definition (hadd) must satisfy two key conditions: comprehensiveness (jami') and exclusiveness (mani'). This passage applies those criteria to various definitions of the human being from different schools. By examining these definitions, we will learn how to critically assess any definition in the Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum
Find the term being defined in the passage. It is 'insan' (the human being). All definitions aim to capture this species.
2
List the alternative definitions
Note each definition and its source: (1) Greek philosophers: rational/speaking/thinking animal; (2) Early Muslim philosophers: follow the Greeks; (3) Religious scholars: religious creature; (4) Sociologists/economists: social animal; (5) Linguists: symbolic animal.
The author also mentions that these are complementary, not contradictory.
3
Apply the jami' criterion
Check if each definition includes all humans. For example, 'rational animal' includes every human; 'social animal' might exclude a hermit; 'religious creature' might exclude atheists.
The definition must be comprehensive (jami').
4
Apply the mani' criterion
Check if the definition excludes non-humans. For instance, 'rational animal' excludes non-rational animals; 'social animal' could include some social insects; 'religious creature' excludes non-human animals that lack religion.
The definition must be exclusive (mani').
5
Identify genus and differentia
The best definition according to the author is 'rational animal' (hayawan natiq). Extract the proximate genus: 'animal' (hayawan) and the proximate differentia: 'rational' (natiq). Confirm that the differentia distinguishes humans from other animals.
In classical logic, 'natiq' implies intellect, not just speech. The passage emphasizes broader mental operations.

العالم، كونه يتناول الإنسان ويجسد حقيقة كينونته بصورة متفردة وقبل أن نسوق طائفة تلك الآيات، يجمل بنا أن نقف مع استعراض أحد الباحثين من لأبرز التعريفات للإنسان لدى مختلف المدارس، وذلك على النحو التالي: عرف فلاسفة اليونان القدماء الإنسان بأنه حيوان ناطق أو حيوان متكلم، أو حيوان مفكّر. وقد تابعهم على ذلك بعض فلاسفة المسلمين الأوائل كالفارابي وابن سينا وابن رشد وعرفه علماء الدين من فقهاء وغيرهم بأنه مخلوق متدين. وعرفه علماء الاجتماع والاقتصاد وذوو الاهتمام بنشأة وتطور الثقافات والحضارات بكونه حيواناً اجتماعياً. وعرّفه علماء اللغة بأنه حيوان رامز أو قادر على استخدام الرمز، و الرموز اللغوية بالذات. وذلك ما يميز الإنسان تمييزاً حقيقياً جوهرياً عن أي مخلوق آخر، فليس صحيحاً أن نقوم بعقد مقارنات سلوكية بينهما لمجرد وجود أوجه شبه محدودة بين الإنسان وبعض أنواع الحيوان. وعليه يتم إجراء تجارب اختبارية على الحيوان (المشابه) للخروج بنتائج يتم إسقاطها على سلوك الإنسان. إن وجود قدر من الشبه الخلقي بين الإنسان وحيوان (كالشمبانزي) -مثلاً- لا يؤذن بالقول: إنه بات بالإمكان ضبط السلوك الإنساني تبعاً للسلوك الخاص بالشمبانزي) ذلك أن سمة استخدام الرموز لدى الإنسان قبل أي سمة أخرى تقف عائقاً أمام هذه المقارنة التي تفتقدها (الشمبانزي) وعليه فالقدرة على استخدام الرموز ميزة إنسانية خالصة. أنه لا تعارض بين هذه التعريفات بل هي تكمل بعضها، ولكن لعل ومع أقربها إلى تحقيق التعريف الجامع المانع هو تعريف الفلاسفة للإنسان بأنه حيوان ناطق لكون هذا الوصف يستغرق جميع أفراد بني الإنسان، فهو جامع، ولا يدخل فيه أي شيء مما عداهم، فهو مانع. كما أن هذا التعريف يكتسب شمولاً تكونه من الجنس القريب بالنسبة إلى النوع الإنساني وهو الحيوانية، والفصل القريب وهو النطق، الذي يتجاوز معناه مجرّد القدرة على الكلام إلى القدرة على التفكير والقيام بكثير من العمليات العقلية العليا.
The world, as it deals with the human being and embodies the reality of his existence in a unique manner, and before we present a group of those verses, it is appropriate for us to pause with the review of one researcher of the most prominent definitions of the human being according to various schools, as follows: The ancient Greek philosophers defined the human being as a rational animal or a speaking animal, or a thinking animal. Some early Muslim philosophers like al-Farabi, Ibn Sina, and Ibn Rushd followed them. The religious scholars among jurists and others defined him as a religious creature. Sociologists and economists and those interested in the origin and development of cultures and civilizations defined him as a social animal. The linguists defined him as a symbolic animal or capable of using the symbol, and especially linguistic symbols. That is what distinguishes the human being genuinely and essentially from any other creature, so it is not correct to draw behavioral comparisons between them merely because of the existence of limited similarities between human beings and some types of animals. Accordingly, experimental tests are conducted on the (similar) animal to produce results that are then applied to human behavior. The existence of a degree of morphological similarity between humans and animals (like chimpanzees), for example, does not permit the claim that it has become possible to regulate human behavior according to the behavior specific to chimpanzees, because the characteristic of using symbols in humans, before any other characteristic, stands as an obstacle to this comparison which the chimpanzee lacks. Therefore, the ability to use symbols is a purely human trait. There is no contradiction among these definitions; rather, they complement each other, but perhaps the closest to achieving the comprehensive and exclusive definition (al-jami' al-mani') is the philosophers' definition of the human being as a rational animal, because this description encompasses all members of the human species, so it is comprehensive, and nothing other than them enters into it, so it is exclusive. Also, this definition acquires comprehensiveness consisting of the proximate genus relative to the human species, which is animality, and the proximate differentia, which is rationality, whose meaning goes beyond mere ability to speak to the ability to think and perform many higher mental operations.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage presents a survey of definitions of the human being (insan) from various intellectual traditions, and then evaluates them to determine which best satisfies the logical criteria of a proper definition (hadd or rasm) as used in Islamic logic. The author begins by noting the importance of the topic and then lists definitions: (1) Greek philosophers: 'human is a rational/speaking/thinking animal'; (2) Some early Muslim philosophers (al-Farabi, Ibn Sina, Ibn Rushd) follow the Greeks; (3) Religious scholars: 'human is a religious creature'; (4) Sociologists/economists: 'human is a social animal'; (5) Linguists: 'human is a symbolic animal'. The author then argues that the ability to use symbols is a distinctive human trait that prevents direct behavioral comparison with animals. He then asserts that these definitions are complementary, but the closest to a jami' mani' (comprehensive and exclusive) definition is the philosophical definition: 'rational animal'. This is because it includes all humans (comprehensive) and excludes all non-humans (exclusive). Moreover, this definition is constructed from the proximate genus (animality) and the proximate differentia (rationality), which extends beyond mere speech to higher cognitive functions. In the context of Ilm al-Mantiq, this mirrors the technical structure of hadd: genus (jins) + differentia (fasl).

حيوان ناطق
جامع مانع

The Universal Principle of Pairing
Author defines the concept of pairing (zawjiyya) as a universal principle across all realms of existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the universal instances of pairing (zawjiyya) in creation as described by the author and al-Ghazali, and recognize it as a broad ontological principle transcending biological sex.

Core Idea
Pairing is not just male and female; it is a universal principle across all levels of existence.

In this lesson, we explore the concept of 'mazhar al-zawjiyya' as presented in the passage. The author defines pairing as the existence of a pair in all creatures, material and spiritual, and illustrates it across domains: living, inanimate, ideas, emotions. Through Quranic verses and al-Ghazali's commentary, this principle is shown to be a fundamental ontological structure.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of pairing
Focus on the first sentence: 'مظهر الزوجية يعني وجود زوجين في الإنسان، كما هو الحال في جميع المخلوقات المادية والمعنوية.' Recognize that pair is universal and applies to both material and spiritual realms.
2
Identify the domains of pairing
List the examples: human/animal/plant (male-female), inanimate (positive-negative), ideas (right-wrong), emotions (pleasure-anger, joy-sorrow). Note that pairing includes both concrete and abstract categories.
3
Connect to Quranic verses
The author cites Surah Ya Seen 36 and Surah al-Dhariyat 49. Notice how the verses declare that Allah created all pairs, supporting the universal scope.
4
Analyze al-Ghazali's expansion
Al-Ghazali adds further dimensions: subtle/dense, composite/simple, and cosmic pairing of souls (giving) and elements (receiving). Understand this as a metaphysical deepening of the principle.
5
Synthesize the principle
Conclude that pairing is a fundamental ontological structure, not just a biological fact. It permeates all creation as a sign of divine wisdom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إنَّ مظهر الزوجية يعني وجود زوجين في الإنسان، كما هو الحال في جميع المخلوقات المادية والمعنوية. ففي عالم الإنسان والحيوان والنبات يعبر عن مظهر الزوجية بالذكر والأنثى، وفي الجماد بالموجب والسالب، وفي الأفكار بالصواب والخطأ، وفي المشاعر بالرضى والغضب والسرور والحزن، وهكذا.... وصدق الله القائل: {سُبْحانَ الَّذِي خَلَقَ الأَزْوَاجَ كُلَّها مِمَّا تُنبِتُ الْأَرْضُ وَمِنْ أَنفُسِهِمْ وَمِمَّا لا يَعْلَمُونَ} [يس: 36]. وقد عبر الإمام الغزالي (ت: 505هـ) عن هذه الظاهرة العامة فقال تعقيباً على قوله تعالى {وَمِنْ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ خَلَقْنَا زَوْجَيْنِ لَعَلَّكُمْ تَذَكَّرُونَ} [الذاريات: 49]: (فالمخلوقات كلّها مفطورة على الازدواج لطيفها وكثيفها، معقولها ومحسوسها. ففي المركبات ازدواج وفي البسائط ازدواج، وبين البسائط والمركبات ازدواج، والنفوس بواسطة الأفلاك معطية، والعناصر قابلة...).
The phenomenon of pairing means the existence of a pair in man, as is the case in all material and spiritual creatures. In the world of man, animal, and plant, the phenomenon of pairing is expressed by male and female; in the inanimate by positive and negative; in ideas by right and wrong; and in emotions by pleasure and anger, joy and sorrow, and so on. And Allah, the Exalted, speaks the truth: 'Exalted is He who created all pairs of what the earth grows and of themselves and of that which they do not know' [Ya Seen 36]. And Imam al-Ghazali (d. 505 AH) expressed this universal phenomenon, commenting on His statement, the Exalted, 'And of everything We have created pairs that you may remember' [al-Dhariyat 49]: 'All creatures are naturally disposed to pairing, their subtle and dense, their intelligible and sensible. In composites there is pairing, in simples there is pairing, and between simples and composites there is pairing; souls, through the spheres, are bestowing, and the elements are receiving...'
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage defines the concept of 'mazhar al-zawjiyya' (the phenomenon of pairing) as a universal principle permeating all levels of existence. The author begins by stating that pairing means the existence of a pair within the human being, and this holds true for all creatures, both material and spiritual. The explanation proceeds by enumerating domains: in living beings (human, animal, plant) it appears as male and female; in inanimate matter as positive and negative; in ideas as right and wrong; in emotions as pleasure/anger and joy/sorrow. The author then cites Quranic verse 36 from Surah Ya Seen, which declares that Allah created all pairs, and follows with a quotation from Imam al-Ghazali, who expands on the verse from Surah al-Dhariyat to assert that all creatures are innately dualistic—whether subtle or dense, intelligible or sensible. Ghazali further notes that pairing exists in composites, in simples, and even between simples and composites, and he describes a cosmic pairing where souls (through celestial spheres) are active/giving and the (earthly) elements are passive/receiving. The passage thus presents pairing not as a mere biological fact but as a fundamental ontological principle.

مظهر الزوجية
زوجين

Key Takeaway

Plato's Four Sources of Knowledge
Author enumerates Plato's four sources of knowledge with definitions and warns against reductionism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any given knowledge claim into one of Plato's four sources based on the definitions provided in the passage.

Core Idea
Knowledge has multiple sources; none alone suffices.

This lesson introduces Plato's fourfold classification of knowledge sources, which contrasts with both Sophist reliance on sensation and Socrates' sole reliance on reason. Understanding these categories helps you analyze how different types of knowledge claims originate and why a single-source approach leads to error. The passage also warns against reducing all knowledge to any one source.

Guided Path
1
Identify each source
Read the Arabic passage and locate the four named sources: الإحساس (sensation), الظن (opinion), الاستدلال (reasoning), التعقل (intellection). Note how each is introduced with a number or dash.
2
Extract the definition of each source
For each source, write down the key definitional phrase. Sensation: 'إدراك عوارض الأجسام أو أشباهها في اليقظة وصورها في المنام'. Opinion: 'الحكم على المحسوسات بما هي نسبية متغيرة لتعلقها بالمادة'. Reasoning: 'علم الماهيات الرياضية المتحققة في المحسوسات'. Intellection: 'إدراك الماهيات المجرّدة عن كل مادّة'.
Notice that reason and intellection are distinct in Plato's scheme.
3
Distinguish the sources hierarchically
Compare the four sources: sensation is lowest, opinion is judgment on changeable perceptibles, reasoning grasps abstract mathematical forms that still exist in matter, intellection grasps pure forms like 'bigness' apart from matter. This hierarchy implies different reliability.
Plato values intellection most.
4
Apply the warning against reductionism
The passage warns that taking any single source as the sole source leads to misuse. Reflect on how this warning applies to debates in Islamic theology (e.g., rejecting reason in favor of pure textualism, or vice versa).
This step connects to the 'where_this_tool_lives' application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ت: ٣٤٧ ق. م والذي يعده بعض الباحثين أول فيلسوف بحث مسألة المعرفة لذاتها، وخرج من الثنائية بين السوفسطائيين النازعين إلى اعتبار المعرفة صادرة عن الإحساس وأنها جزئية متغيّرة وبين سقراط (ت: ۳۹٫۹ ق.م) الذي يرجع المعرفة الحقة إلى العقل. ولكن أفلاطون استقصى مصادر المعرفة فوجدها أربعة هي:
۱ - الإحساس وهو إدراك عوارض الأجسام أو أشباهها في اليقظة وصورها في المنام.
٢ - الظن وهو الحكم على المحسوسات بما هي نسبية متغيرة لتعلقها بالمادة. وهذه الأحكام كذلك،
- الاستدلال وهو علم الماهيات الرياضية المتحققة في المحسوسات مثل الحساب والفلك والهندسة.
-
التعقل وهو إدراك الماهيات المجرّدة عن كل مادّة، وذلك حينما ينظر إلى الكبر أو الصغر كمعنيين مفارقين له نطبقهما عليه.
ونجد أن هناك من يؤمن بهذا التصنيف على اختلاف في بعض الألفاظ من غير تغيير حقيقي الجوهرها. ويشدد أحد الباحثين من خطورة اعتبار واحد من المصادر الأربعة مصدراً أوحد لها، إذ إن ذلك سيقود إلى كثير من سوء الاستعمال، ولهذا فيجب أن تتضافر جميعها للوصول إلى أهدافها.
Died 347 BC, and whom some researchers consider the first philosopher to investigate the question of knowledge for its own sake, and emerged from the duality between the Sophists who inclined to consider knowledge as emanating from sensation and as particular and changing, and between Socrates (died 399 BC) who traced true knowledge back to reason. But Plato investigated the sources of knowledge and found them to be four: 1- Sensation: it is the perception of accidents of bodies or their likenesses in wakefulness and their images in sleep. 2- Opinion: it is the judgment upon perceptibles as being relative and changing due to their attachment to matter. And these judgments likewise. 3- Reasoning: it is the knowledge of mathematical essences realized in perceptibles, such as arithmetic, astronomy, and geometry. 4- Intellection: it is the perception of essences abstracted from all matter, that is when one looks at bigness or smallness as two separate meanings that we apply to it. And we find that there are those who believe in this classification with a difference in some terms without a real change to its essence. And one researcher emphasizes the danger of considering any one of the four sources as the sole source for it, because that would lead to much misuse, and therefore all of them must cooperate to achieve their goals.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage presents the classification of knowledge sources according to Plato. It begins by contextualizing Plato's position between the Sophists, who reduced knowledge to sensory perception, and Socrates, who prioritized reason. The author then enumerates four sources: (1) Sensation (الإحساس), which perceives the accidental properties of bodies and their images in sleep. (2) Opinion (الظن), which judges sensory data as relative and changing due to material attachment. (3) Reasoning (الاستدلال), which grasps mathematical essences (e.g., arithmetic, astronomy, geometry) as realized in matter. (4) Intellection (التعقل), which apprehends pure essences like 'bigness' and 'smallness' as abstract forms. The author then notes that this classification is widely accepted with minor terminological variations. Finally, a warning is given about the danger of absolutizing any single source—all must work together. This passage is definitional, as it defines each source. In Islamic epistemology, similar distinctions are made between sense (hiss), reason ('aql), revelation (wahy), and intuition (ilham), but Plato's rationalist framework is distinct.

Key Terms
الإحساس
الظن
الاستدلال
التعقل

Key Takeaway
Plato identifies four distinct sources of knowledge—sensation, opinion, reasoning, and intellection—and warns that none alone is sufficient; they must work together.

Ibn Taymiyya's Fivefold Classification of Knowledge Sources
Presents Ibn Taymiyya's five sources of knowledge with educational implications and a critique of rigid classification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Ibn Taymiyya's five sources of knowledge and explain how each source corresponds to a specific domain of knowledge.

Core Idea
Ibn Taymiyya's five knowledge sources work integratively, with revelation as the ultimate authority.

In this passage, Ibn Taymiyya expands his earlier threefold classification into a fivefold one, detailing how reason, revelation, senses, inspiration, and teaching from the righteous all contribute to knowledge. He emphasizes that these sources are not in conflict but operate in different domains, and warns against dogmatically preferring one classification over another. This lesson will help you parse the five sources and their educational applications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five sources
List the five ways knowledge can be obtained according to Ibn Taymiyya: rational proof (reason), revelation (wahy), what God casts into the heart (senses/inner reflection), inspiration (ilham), and teaching of the Messenger and believers. Note that the fifth source is implicit in the text: 'تعليم الرسول والعلماء والمؤمنين'.
2
Map each source to its corresponding type of knowledge
The passage states that senses correspond to sensory knowledge, reason to rational, intuition/inspiration to emotional, and revelation to religious, moral, and unseen knowledge. The fifth source (teaching) is not explicitly mapped but can be inferred to cover transmitted knowledge.
3
Understand the integrative function
The passage says all sources work integratively in both visible and unseen worlds, with revelation as the absolute reference. Reflect on how this integration avoids reductionism and acknowledges the complexity of human knowledge.
4
Critique the rigid classification
The author warns that differences between classifications are merely verbal, not real. Identify the argument: classifications differ in conciseness and elaboration, not independence. Consider why this is important for avoiding dogmatic adherence to one taxonomy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثالث - مقدمة التصنيف الخماسي. ونجد هذا التصنيف مفصلاً عند ابن تيمية. فعلى حين سبق أن قرر ثلاثية المصادر والطرائق لكنه عنى بذلك المصادر والطرائق الأساسية للمعرفة فحسب. ويتضح هذا من خلال إيراده المصادر وطرائق أخرى. ففي معرض حديثه عن كون بعض أهل السنة قد احتجوا على أن المعرفة والإيمان يحصلان للعبد بفضل ورحمته وهدايته وتعريفه يؤكد ابن تيمية على وحدة تلك المصادر والطرائق جنباً إلى جنب من غير استحالة حصول المعرفة بالنظر العقلي (العقل) أو عـدم حصولها بتعليم الرسول والعلماء والمؤمنين ودعائهم وبيانهم واستدلالهم، بل يحصل ذلك تارة بالإشارة إلى الدليل العقلي (العقل)، وتارة بالإخبار بالحق (الوحي)، وتارة بما يقذفه الله في قلب المرء من النظر والاعتبار والاستدلال (الحس)، وتارة باضطراره إلى العلم من غير اكتساب منه (الإلهام). وقد تابع هذا التصنيف أحد الباحثين في ميدان التربية الإسلامية، كمـا مـال إلى الفصل بين المصادر والطرائق الأساسية وتلك المساعدة، كما مر آنفاً عند الحديث عن التصنيف الثنائي. ويبقى التأكيد على أن كل واحد من هذه الخمسة يعمل تربوياً في مجال معرفته. فالحس يتناسب والمعارف الحسية، والعقل يتناسب والمعارف العقلية والحدس والإلهام يتناسبان والمعارف الذوقية والعاطفية، والوحي يتناسب والمعارف الدينية والخلقية والغيبية بصورة عامة. وبصورة جامعة فإن جميع تلك المصادر والطرائق تؤدي وظائفها في ميدان المعرفة في عالم الشهادة، مثلما تؤديها في ميدان عالم الغيب على نحو تكاملي، وإن كانت المرجعية المطلقة فيه للوحي. ومما هو حري بالتنويه هنا أنّ من التعسف الجزم بصحة واحد من هذه التصنيفات ومصادرة البقية، لأن الاختلاف فيما بينها ليس حقيقياً، وإنما هو اختلاف ألفاظ، إذ مبناه قائم على الإجمال والتفصيل وليس على الاستقلال والتفرد كما هو واضح عند التحقيق.
The third chapter - Introduction: The fivefold classification. We find this classification detailed by Ibn Taymiyya. For although he had previously decided on a triad of sources and methods, he meant by that the basic sources and methods of knowledge only. This becomes clear through his mention of other sources and methods. For in the context of his discussion that some Ahl al-Sunna have argued that knowledge and faith are obtained by the servant through God's bounty, mercy, guidance, and definition, Ibn Taymiyya emphasizes the unity of those sources and methods side by side, without the impossibility of obtaining knowledge through rational reflection (reason) or its non-obtainment through the teaching of the Messenger, the scholars, and the believers, their supplication, explanation, and proofs. Rather, it is obtained sometimes by reference to rational proof (reason), sometimes by informing with the truth (revelation), sometimes by what God casts into the heart of a person of reflection, consideration, and inference (senses), and sometimes by his being compelled to knowledge without acquisition (inspiration). And this classification was followed by one researcher in the field of Islamic education, as he tended to separate between basic sources and methods and auxiliary ones, as mentioned earlier when discussing the twofold classification. And the emphasis remains that each of these five works educationally in its field of knowledge. For the senses correspond to sensory knowledge, reason corresponds to rational knowledge, intuition and inspiration correspond to tasteful and emotional knowledge, and revelation corresponds to religious, moral, and unseen knowledge in general. And comprehensively, all those sources and methods perform their functions in the field of knowledge in the visible world, just as they perform in the field of the unseen world in an integrative manner, although absolute reference in it is to revelation. And it is worth noting here that it is arbitrary to assert the correctness of one of these classifications and to dismiss the rest, because the difference between them is not real, but rather a difference of words, since its foundation is based on conciseness and elaboration, not on independence and uniqueness, as is clear upon investigation.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage presents the fivefold classification of sources and methods of knowledge as detailed by Ibn Taymiyya, along with its educational implications and a critique of rigid categorization. The author begins by noting that although Ibn Taymiyya previously established a triad of basic sources, he also mentions additional sources, indicating that the triad covers the fundamentals but not the entirety. In discussing how knowledge and faith are attained, Ibn Taymiyya lists four specific means: first, rational proof (reason); second, informing with truth (revelation); third, what God casts into the heart through reflection (senses); and fourth, being compelled to knowledge without acquisition (inspiration). These four, together with the teaching of the Messenger and believers mentioned earlier, form a fivefold classification. The passage then connects this to educational theory, explaining that each source corresponds to a type of knowledge: senses to sensory, reason to rational, intuition/inspiration to emotional, and revelation to religious, moral, and unseen knowledge. Importantly, all these sources function integratively in both the visible and unseen worlds, though revelation remains the ultimate authority. Finally, the author warns against dogmatically favoring one classification over others, arguing that differences between classifications are merely verbal—rooted in degree of detail—not substantive.

الوحي
الحس
الإلهام
التصنيف الخماسي

What Is Mantiq?
beginner

Threefold Classification of Knowledge from Quran 16:78
Adopts a threefold classification from Quran 16:78

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three primary sources of knowledge according to the classification derived from Quran 16:78 and explain how secondary sources are accommodated.

Core Idea
The Quran classifies knowledge into auditory, visual, and heart-based channels.

This lesson introduces a threefold classification of knowledge sources that the study adopts. It is grounded in Quran 16:78, which mentions hearing, sight, and hearts. The passage explains how these correspond to transmitted sciences, experimental sciences, and rational/spiritual knowledge, while also acknowledging secondary sources like inspiration and dreams.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three channels in the verse
Read Quran 16:78: 'And Allah brought you out from the wombs of your mothers while you knew nothing, and He made for you hearing, sight, and hearts that you might give thanks.' The three channels are al-sam' (hearing), al-absar (sight), and al-af'ida (hearts).
These are the primary faculties given by Allah for acquiring knowledge.
2
Map each channel to a type of knowledge
The passage maps hearing to auditory knowledge (transmitted sciences), sight to visual knowledge (experimental sciences), and hearts to heart knowledge (rational and spiritual knowledge). Note that transmitted sciences include religious sciences even if transmitted through writing.
This mapping extends the literal senses to broader epistemic categories.
3
Understand the role of secondary sources
The study does not exclude other sources like the senses (al-hiss), inspiration (ilham), and truthful dreams. These are considered secondary and operate within the framework of the three primary channels.
This classification is inclusive, not exclusive.
4
Recognize the shift from classical mantiq
In classical Islamic logic, sam' (auditory report) is not typically a source of certain knowledge; here it is elevated to a primary channel alongside reason and observation. This reflects an epistemological stance that values transmitted revelation.
This shift is significant for understanding the study's methodology.

الرأي في هذه الدراسة. أما ما تتبناه هذه الدراسة بصورة رئيسة فالتصنيف الثلاثي، المعتمد على الحس والعقل والخبر المعصوم أو الوحي، دون إقصاء لما عدا ذلك. فالحس والإلهام والرؤيا الصادقة مصادر ثانوية تأخذ دورها بحسبه في هذه الدراسة. ألطف الاستشهادات التي تساق في معرض ترجيح هذا التصنيف ما استنتجه أحد الباحثين من قول الله تعالى: ﴿وَاللهُ أَخْرَجَكُمْ مِنْ بُطُونِ أُمَّهَاتِكُمْ لا تَعْلَمُونَ شَيْئاً وَجَعَلَ لَكُمُ السَّمْعَ وَالأَبْصارَ وَالْأَفْئِدَةَ لَعَلَّكُمْ تَشْكُرُونَ﴾ [النحل: ۷۸/۱٦] . فقد استنتج أن منافذ المعرفة ثلاثة هي: 1 - المعرفة (السمعية) وتدخل فيها العلوم النقلية ومنها علوم الدين، وإن نقلت عن طريق القلم والكتاب. 2 - المعرفة (البصرية) وتدخل فيها العلوم التجريبية، لأنها تقوم على الملاحظة والتجربة والقياس وأساسها البصر والمشاهدة. 3 - المعرفة (الفؤادية) أو (القلبية) وتدخل فيها المعرفة العقلية الخالصة، عن طريق عمليات العقل العليا من تأمل ونظر وتفكير واعتبار ... إلخ، بل إن الآية قد يمتد معناها ليشمل المعرفة (الروحية) ويقصد بها المعارف التبعية من حدس وإلهام وسواهما. ويلاحظ هنا أنّ دخول العلوم النقلية في المعرفة (السمعية) وكذا التجريبية في (البصرية) لا يتعارض وذلك القول الذي تبناه أحد الباحثين من قبل، وذهب
The opinion in this study. As for what this study adopts principally, it is the threefold classification, based on the senses, reason, and the infallible report or revelation, without excluding what is beyond that. For the senses, inspiration, and truthful dreams are secondary sources that take their role accordingly in this study. The most elegant of the citations adduced in support of this classification is what one researcher concluded from the saying of God Most High: 'And Allah brought you out from the wombs of your mothers while you knew nothing, and He made for you hearing, sight, and hearts that you might give thanks' [Surah al-Nahl 16:78]. He concluded that the channels of knowledge are three: 1. Auditory knowledge, which includes transmitted sciences, including religious sciences, even if transmitted through pen and book. 2. Visual knowledge, which includes experimental sciences, because they are based on observation, experiment, and measurement, and their basis is sight and observation. 3. Heart knowledge or cardiac knowledge, which includes pure rational knowledge, through the higher mental processes of contemplation, reflection, thinking, consideration, etc. Rather, the verse may extend in meaning to include spiritual knowledge, by which is meant subordinate knowledge from intuition, inspiration, and others. And it is noted here that the inclusion of transmitted sciences in auditory knowledge, as well as experimental sciences in visual knowledge, does not contradict that statement which one researcher had previously adopted, and he went...
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage presents the methodological stance of the study regarding the classification of knowledge sources. The study primarily adopts a threefold classification: senses (al-hiss), reason (al-'aql), and infallible report or revelation (al-khabar al-ma'sum / al-wahy). However, it does not exclude other sources like inspiration (ilham) and truthful dreams, which are considered secondary. The author then provides a scriptural foundation for this threefold classification from Quran 16:78, which mentions hearing (al-sam'), sight (al-absar), and hearts (al-af'ida). A researcher interpreted these three as corresponding to three types of knowledge: auditory knowledge (al-ma'rifa al-sam'iyya) encompassing transmitted and religious sciences; visual knowledge (al-ma'rifa al-basariyya) encompassing experimental sciences based on observation and experiment; and heart knowledge (al-ma'rifa al-fu'adiyya or al-qalbiyya) encompassing pure rational knowledge through higher mental processes. The researcher further notes that the verse can also extend to spiritual knowledge (al-ma'rifa al-ruhiyya), which includes intuition, inspiration, etc. The passage concludes by noting that including transmitted sciences under auditory knowledge and experimental sciences under visual knowledge does not contradict earlier statements by another researcher, ensuring consistency in the study's framework.

What Is Mantiq?

The Linguistic and Technical Definition of Sensation
Author defines sensation linguistically, then technically.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the linguistic, lexicographical, and philosophical definitions of al-hiss.

Core Idea
Sensation in Islam is rooted in the Quran and expanded by scholars like al-Raghib.

Sensation (al-hiss) is a foundational concept in Islamic epistemology. The passage begins by tracing its linguistic root to a Quranic verse and then presents definitions from Ibn al-Athir and al-Raghib al-Isfahani, before moving to a philosophical definition. Understanding these layers helps you see how Islamic scholars refined terms for precise use in logic and theology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic root
Find the verse cited (Quran 21:102) and note the word 'hasis' (sensation). This shows the linguistic origin from a subtle sound.
2
Examine Ibn al-Athir's definition
He defines sensation as 'knowledge by the senses' and lists the five external senses. Note that he ties sensation directly to the perceptive faculties.
3
Analyze al-Raghib's definition
He defines al-hassa (the sense faculty) as 'the power by which sensory accidents are perceived.' This is more technical—focusing on the power, not just the act.
Al-Raghib distinguishes between the faculty and its operation.
4
Compare with the philosophical definition
The passage adds a philosophical definition: 'a natural power in the body by which man and animal perceive external things and changes.' Notice it includes animals and internal changes.
This broadens the scope beyond humans.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الأول الحس
تعريف الحس
الحس لغة: أصله من الصوت الخفي مأخوذ من قوله تعالى: ﴿لا يَسْمَعُونَ حَسِيسَها﴾ [الأنبياء: 102/21].
وقال ابن الأثير: الإحساس العلم بالحواس، وهي مشاعر الإنسان كالعين والأذن والأنف واللسان واليد وحواس الإنسان المشاعر الخمس وهي: الطعم والشم والبصر والسمع واللمس (1).
وعرّف الراغب الأصفهاني (ت: 502هـ) الحاسة بأنها: (القوة التي بها تدرك الأعراض الحسية، والحواس المشاعر الخمس، يقال حَسَسْتُ وحَسَّيْتُ وأحسست.... وأما أحسسته فحقيقته أدركته بحاستي، وأحسست مثله لكن حذفت إحدى السينين تخفيفاً نحو ظلت))(2).
وفي الدراسات الفلسفية تعرف الحاسة بأنها قوة طبيعية في الجسم وبها يدرك الإنسان والحيوان الأشياء الخارجة عنه، وما يطرأ على جسمه من تغيرات (3)
وقد نشأ عن الاعتماد على وسيلة الحس ما عرف بالمذهب الحسي (Sensationalism) وهو مذهب يرى أن الحواس هي المصدر الوحيد لجميع معارفنا، وهي وحدها التي تفصل في قيمة هذه المعارف. وهذا المذهب يرد المعقول إلى المحسوس، ومن أظهر القائلين به هوبز وكوندياك وهيوم... ويقابل العقلانية (Rationalism)(1).
و معنى رده المعقول إلى المحسوس رؤيته إلى المعرفة على أنها إما إحساسات أو راجعة إلى إحساسات (2).
ويُرجح أن دي جيراندو) هو الذي ابتدع اصطلاح المذهب الحسي(3).
الفرق بين الحس والتجريب
يرى بعض الباحثين أن المذهب الحسي ما هو إلا إحدى صور التجريبية (Empiricism) . إذ هو يقوم على أن الحس باب المعرفة الوحيد، وليس في العقل شيء لم يمر بالحس ابتداء.
ولهذا فإنهم ينكرون أن يولد العقل مزوداً بأفكار فطرية موروثة كما يرى العقليون. ووفق هذا المفهوم فإن التجريبيين يلتقون مع الحسيين، ولكنهم يختلفون عنهم في كون التجريبيين يرون أن فاعلية العقل تبدو في عملياته العقلية العليا كالتفكير فيما تنقله إليه الحواس من صور ذهنية، وتأليف أفكار من العناصر التي استمدها من التجربة، وهي أفكار لا وجود لها في العالم الخارجي (5)
Chapter One: Sensation
Definition of Sensation
Sensation linguistically: its origin is from subtle sound, taken from His saying the Exalted: 'They do not hear its sensation' [Al-Anbiya: 102/21].
Ibn al-Athir said: Sensation is knowledge by the senses, which are the perceptive faculties of man like the eye, ear, nose, tongue, and hand. The senses of man are the five perceptive faculties: taste, smell, sight, hearing, and touch (1).
Al-Raghib al-Isfahani (d. 502 AH) defined the sense faculty as: 'the power by which sensory accidents are perceived, and the senses are the five perceptive faculties; one says hasastu, hassaytu, and ahsastu... As for ahsastu, its true meaning is I perceived it with my sense faculty, and ahsastu is similar but one of the two sin's is omitted for ease, like zalta' (2).
In philosophical studies, the sense faculty is defined as a natural power in the body by which man and animal perceive external things and changes that occur to their body (3).
From reliance on the means of sensation arose what is known as Sensationalism, a doctrine that holds the senses are the sole source of all our knowledge, and they alone decide the value of this knowledge. This doctrine reduces the rational to the sensible, and its most prominent proponents are Hobbes, Condillac, and Hume... It is opposed to Rationalism (1).
And the meaning of its reducing the rational to the sensible is its view of knowledge as either sensations or reducible to sensations (2).
It is likely that de Gérando coined the term Sensationalism (3).
The Difference between Sensation and Empiricism
Some researchers hold that Sensationalism is nothing but a form of Empiricism. For it is based on the idea that sensation is the sole door of knowledge, and there is nothing in the mind that did not first pass through the senses.
Therefore, they deny that the mind is born equipped with innate inherited ideas as rationalists hold. According to this concept, empiricists agree with sensationalists, but they differ from them in that empiricists consider that the mind's activity appears in its higher mental processes such as thinking about the mental images transmitted to it by the senses, and composing ideas from elements derived from experience, ideas that have no existence in the external world (5).
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'sensation' (الحس) and discusses the philosophical school of sensationalism, contrasting it with empiricism. The author begins with a linguistic definition, tracing the root to a Quranic verse and citing Ibn al-Athir's definition that sensation is knowledge via the five senses. Then al-Raghib al-Isfahani's definition is given, emphasizing that the sense faculty perceives sensory accidents. The philosophical definition follows: a natural power in the body for perceiving external objects and bodily changes. Next, the author introduces sensationalism, a doctrine that considers the senses the sole source of knowledge and reduces rational concepts to sensible ones. Prominent advocates like Hobbes, Condillac, and Hume are mentioned. The author notes that the term was likely coined by de Gérando. Finally, the distinction between sensation (as a school) and empiricism is explained: both agree that all knowledge comes from the senses, but empiricism allows for higher mental processes (thinking, composing ideas) that go beyond raw sensations. This clarifies that sensationalism is a narrower, more radical form of empiricism. All examples in this explanation are epistemological, not from Islamic sciences, but the passage itself is philosophical in nature.

الحس
المذهب الحسي
التجريبية

Key Takeaway
The definition of sensation in Islamic thought moves from a Quranic referent to a technical philosophical term.

The Doctrine of Sensationalism
Author defines sensationalism and its core tenets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the core claims of sensationalism and contrast it with rationalism.

Core Idea
Sensationalism reduces all knowledge to sense perceptions, denying innate ideas.

The passage introduces sensationalism as a philosophical school that arose from reliance on sensation. It claims the senses are the sole source of knowledge and reduces rational concepts to sensations. Understanding this doctrine helps you locate the boundaries of sensory knowledge in Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core claim
Find the sentence: 'the senses are the sole source of all our knowledge.' This is the foundational premise of sensationalism.
2
Understand 'reducing the rational to the sensible'
The passage explains that sensationalism views knowledge as either sensations or reducible to sensations. This means no abstract concepts exist independently of sense experience.
3
Note the opposition to rationalism
Sensationalism is contrasted with rationalism, which holds that reason and innate ideas are sources of knowledge. The passage implies that sensationalists deny innate ideas.
4
Reflect on the implications for Islamic thought
If sensationalism were true, knowledge of the unseen (al-ghayb) or moral values would be impossible unless derived from senses. Islamic scholars affirm other sources like revelation and reason.
This is a modern Western doctrine, but it raises questions relevant to kalam.

Source Text
