تعريف الحس
الحس لغة: أصله من الصوت الخفي مأخوذ من قوله تعالى: ﴿لا يَسْمَعُونَ حَسِيسَها﴾ [الأنبياء: 102/21].
وقال ابن الأثير: الإحساس العلم بالحواس، وهي مشاعر الإنسان كالعين والأذن والأنف واللسان واليد وحواس الإنسان المشاعر الخمس وهي: الطعم والشم والبصر والسمع واللمس (1).
وعرّف الراغب الأصفهاني (ت: 502هـ) الحاسة بأنها: (القوة التي بها تدرك الأعراض الحسية، والحواس المشاعر الخمس، يقال حَسَسْتُ وحَسَّيْتُ وأحسست.... وأما أحسسته فحقيقته أدركته بحاستي، وأحسست مثله لكن حذفت إحدى السينين تخفيفاً نحو ظلت))(2).
وفي الدراسات الفلسفية تعرف الحاسة بأنها قوة طبيعية في الجسم وبها يدرك الإنسان والحيوان الأشياء الخارجة عنه، وما يطرأ على جسمه من تغيرات (3)
وقد نشأ عن الاعتماد على وسيلة الحس ما عرف بالمذهب الحسي (Sensationalism) وهو مذهب يرى أن الحواس هي المصدر الوحيد لجميع معارفنا، وهي وحدها التي تفصل في قيمة هذه المعارف. وهذا المذهب يرد المعقول إلى المحسوس، ومن أظهر القائلين به هوبز وكوندياك وهيوم... ويقابل العقلانية (Rationalism)(1).
و معنى رده المعقول إلى المحسوس رؤيته إلى المعرفة على أنها إما إحساسات أو راجعة إلى إحساسات (2).
ويُرجح أن دي جيراندو) هو الذي ابتدع اصطلاح المذهب الحسي(3).
الفرق بين الحس والتجريب
يرى بعض الباحثين أن المذهب الحسي ما هو إلا إحدى صور التجريبية (Empiricism) . إذ هو يقوم على أن الحس باب المعرفة الوحيد، وليس في العقل شيء لم يمر بالحس ابتداء.
ولهذا فإنهم ينكرون أن يولد العقل مزوداً بأفكار فطرية موروثة كما يرى العقليون. ووفق هذا المفهوم فإن التجريبيين يلتقون مع الحسيين، ولكنهم يختلفون عنهم في كون التجريبيين يرون أن فاعلية العقل تبدو في عملياته العقلية العليا كالتفكير فيما تنقله إليه الحواس من صور ذهنية، وتأليف أفكار من العناصر التي استمدها من التجربة، وهي أفكار لا وجود لها في العالم الخارجي (5)
Chapter One: Sensation
Definition of Sensation
Sensation linguistically: its origin is from subtle sound, taken from His saying the Exalted: 'They do not hear its sensation' [Al-Anbiya: 102/21].
Ibn al-Athir said: Sensation is knowledge by the senses, which are the perceptive faculties of man like the eye, ear, nose, tongue, and hand. The senses of man are the five perceptive faculties: taste, smell, sight, hearing, and touch (1).
Al-Raghib al-Isfahani (d. 502 AH) defined the sense faculty as: 'the power by which sensory accidents are perceived, and the senses are the five perceptive faculties; one says hasastu, hassaytu, and ahsastu... As for ahsastu, its true meaning is I perceived it with my sense faculty, and ahsastu is similar but one of the two sin's is omitted for ease, like zalta' (2).
In philosophical studies, the sense faculty is defined as a natural power in the body by which man and animal perceive external things and changes that occur to their body (3).
From reliance on the means of sensation arose what is known as Sensationalism, a doctrine that holds the senses are the sole source of all our knowledge, and they alone decide the value of this knowledge. This doctrine reduces the rational to the sensible, and its most prominent proponents are Hobbes, Condillac, and Hume... It is opposed to Rationalism (1).
And the meaning of its reducing the rational to the sensible is its view of knowledge as either sensations or reducible to sensations (2).
It is likely that de Gérando coined the term Sensationalism (3).
The Difference between Sensation and Empiricism
Some researchers hold that Sensationalism is nothing but a form of Empiricism. For it is based on the idea that sensation is the sole door of knowledge, and there is nothing in the mind that did not first pass through the senses.
Therefore, they deny that the mind is born equipped with innate inherited ideas as rationalists hold. According to this concept, empiricists agree with sensationalists, but they differ from them in that empiricists consider that the mind's activity appears in its higher mental processes such as thinking about the mental images transmitted to it by the senses, and composing ideas from elements derived from experience, ideas that have no existence in the external world (5).
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'sensation' (الحس) and discusses the philosophical school of sensationalism, contrasting it with empiricism. The author begins with a linguistic definition, tracing the root to a Quranic verse and citing Ibn al-Athir's definition that sensation is knowledge via the five senses. Then al-Raghib al-Isfahani's definition is given, emphasizing that the sense faculty perceives sensory accidents. The philosophical definition follows: a natural power in the body for perceiving external objects and bodily changes. Next, the author introduces sensationalism, a doctrine that considers the senses the sole source of knowledge and reduces rational concepts to sensible ones. Prominent advocates like Hobbes, Condillac, and Hume are mentioned. The author notes that the term was likely coined by de Gérando. Finally, the distinction between sensation (as a school) and empiricism is explained: both agree that all knowledge comes from the senses, but empiricism allows for higher mental processes (thinking, composing ideas) that go beyond raw sensations. This clarifies that sensationalism is a narrower, more radical form of empiricism. All examples in this explanation are epistemological, not from Islamic sciences, but the passage itself is philosophical in nature.

المذهب الحسي

D) Intuition is the primary source

Key Takeaway
Sensationalism is a radical empiricism that denies any a priori knowledge.

Distinguishing Sensationalism from Empiricism
Author distinguishes sensationalism from empiricism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to differentiate between sensationalism and empiricism based on the role of mental processes.

Core Idea
Empiricism allows for higher mental composition, while sensationalism stops at raw sensations.

The passage closes by distinguishing sensationalism from empiricism. Both agree that all knowledge comes from the senses, but empiricism recognizes that the mind actively processes sensory data to form new ideas. This distinction is crucial for evaluating theories of knowledge within Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Find the common ground
Both sensationalism and empiricism hold that all knowledge originates in the senses. The passage says 'there is nothing in the mind that did not first pass through the senses.'
2
Identify the difference
Empiricists believe the mind has higher mental processes (thinking, composing ideas) that go beyond raw sensations. Sensationalists reduce all knowledge to sensations or their combinations without mental construction.
3
Example from the passage
Empiricists allow ideas that 'have no existence in the external world' (e.g., abstract concepts) as mental constructs from experience. Sensationalism would reject such ideas as non-sensible.
4
Reflect on Islamic implication
In Islamic thought, concepts like 'justice' or 'the unseen' require mental composition beyond direct sensation. Empiricism can account for them; sensationalism cannot.

الفصل الأول الحس
تعريف الحس
الحس لغة: أصله من الصوت الخفي مأخوذ من قوله تعالى: ﴿لا يَسْمَعُونَ حَسِيسَها﴾ [الأنبياء: 102/21].
وقال ابن الأثير: الإحساس العلم بالحواس، وهي مشاعر الإنسان كالعين والأذن والأنف واللسان واليد وحواس الإنسان المشاعر الخمس وهي: الطعم والشم والبصر والسمع واللمس (1).
وعرّف الراغب الأصفهاني (ت: 502هـ) الحاسة بأنها: (القوة التي بها تدرك الأعراض الحسية، والحواس المشاعر الخمس، يقال حَسَسْتُ وحَسَّيْتُ وأحسست.... وأما أحسسته فحقيقته أدركته بحاستي، وأحسست مثله لكن حذفت إحدى السينين تخفيفاً نحو ظلت))(2).

Chapter One: Sensation
Definition of Sensation
Sensation linguistically: its origin is from subtle sound, taken from His saying the Exalted: 'They do not hear its sensation' [Al-Anbiya: 102/21].
Ibn al-Athir said: Sensation is knowledge by the senses, which are the perceptive faculties of man like the eye, ear, nose, tongue, and hand. The senses of man are the five perceptive faculties: taste, smell, sight, hearing, and touch (1).
Al-Raghib al-Isfahani (d. 502 AH) defined the sense faculty as: 'the power by which sensory accidents are perceived, and the senses are the five perceptive faculties; one says hasastu, hassaytu, and ahsastu... As for ahsastu, its true meaning is I perceived it with my sense faculty, and ahsastu is similar but one of the two sin's is omitted for ease, like zalta' (2).

This doctrine reduces the rational to the sensible, and its most prominent proponents are Hobbes, Condillac, and Hume... It is opposed to Rationalism (1).
And the meaning of its reducing the rational to the sensible is its view of knowledge as either sensations or reducible to sensations (2).
It is likely that de Gérando coined the term Sensationalism (3).

Some researchers hold that Sensationalism is nothing but a form of Empiricism. For it is based on the idea that sensation is the sole door of knowledge, and there is nothing in the mind that did not first pass through the senses.
Therefore, they deny that the mind is born equipped with innate inherited ideas as rationalists hold. According to this concept, empiricists agree with sensationalists, but they differ from them in that empiricists consider that the mind's activity appears in its higher mental processes such as thinking about the mental images transmitted to it by the senses, and composing ideas from elements derived from experience, ideas that have no existence in the external world (5).

The Five External Senses and Al-Baqillani's Sixth Sense
Author lists external senses and introduces al-Baqillani's sixth sense.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the five external senses according to the author and explain al-Baqillani's addition of a sixth sense and its nature.

Core Idea
Al-Baqillani's sixth sense is inner self-awareness, not new sensory input.

The author lists the five external senses—hearing, sight, touch, smell, taste—and notes near consensus, except for Imam al-Baqillani. Al-Baqillani added a sixth sense: an inner, self-evident perception that arises without reliance on the external senses, such as knowledge of one's own health, emotions, and volitions. This lesson helps you distinguish between external sensory knowledge and internal self-knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the standard five external senses
Read the opening sentence and list the five external senses mentioned: hearing, sight, touch, smell, taste. These are the classic five senses agreed upon by most scholars.
The author says 'no one opposed that - to my knowledge - except Imam al-Baqillani.'
2
Locate al-Baqillani's opinion
Find where the author mentions al-Baqillani's view. He counts six ways of knowledge: the five external senses plus a sixth sense. This sixth sense is described as 'a necessity that originates in the soul initially, without being present through some of these senses.'
3
Understand the nature of the sixth sense
Analyze the examples given: knowledge of oneself, health/sickness, pleasure/pain, distress/joy, ability/inability, will/aversion, perception/blindness. These are all internal states, not perceived through the five external senses. So the sixth sense is a faculty of inner awareness.
It is not a new sensory organ but an intuitive self-knowledge.
4
Recognize the minority status
Note that the author says this is the only opposition he knows. This highlights that the classification of five external senses is nearly universal. Al-Baqillani's view is a minority position.

الباب الثالث: الفصل الأول - الحس
أولاً : الحواس الظاهرة وهي خمسة أقسام : السمع والبصر واللمس والشم والطعم.
ولم يخالف في ذلك حسب معرفتي - سوى الإمام الباقلاني (ت: ٤٠٣هـ) حيث عد طرق العلم ستا: الحواس الخمس الظاهرة، وأضاف ما أسماه بالحاسة السادسة وهي عبارة عن ضرورة تخترع في النفس ابتداء، من غير أن تكون موجودة ببعض هذه الحواس، كعلم الإنسان بنفسه وما يجده فيها من الصحة والسقم واللذة والألم والغم والفرح والقدرة والعجز والإرادة والكراهية والإدراك والعمى، وغير ذلك مما يحدث في النفس، مما يدركه الحي إذا وجد به.
ثانياً: الحواس الباطنة، وقد تعدّدت عبارات الباحثين القدامى والمحدثين حيالها، فبعضهم يعبر عنها بالإحساس الباطني كاللذة والألم، والفرح والحزن، والقوة والغضب. أو الغضب والشهوة أو الإحساس بالعطش والجوع والتعب ونحوها.
وتوسع آخرون فعدوا الحواس الباطنة خمساً على النحو التالي:
۱ - الحس المشترك ويعني القوة النفسية العاكسة لجميع الصور المتسربة إليها عن طريق الحواس الخمس فتجتمع بالملموسات والمشمومات... إلخ فسميت بالحس المشترك، ومثالها رؤيتنا للشعلة التي تدار بسرعة دائرة مع أنها ليست كذلك في حقيقة الأمر.
٢- الخيال ويعني أن الصور التي ارتسمت بالحس المشترك إذا غابت فيمكن أن تتذكر بالرجوع إلى الخيال، ولذلك فالخيال خزانة الحس المشترك.
٣- الوهم: ويعني القوة المدركة للمعاني الجزئية كالعداوة تدركها الشاة من الذئب.
٤ - الحافظة: وتعني أن ذهاب صور المعاني الجزئية في الوهم يمكن تذكرها بالرجوع إلى الحافظة، ولذلك تسمى خزانة الوهم.
٥ - المتخيلة: وهي التي تنسب بعض الصور إلى بعض ومثاله: صاحب هذا اللون له طعم كذا.
وبالتأمل فيما سبق يتبدى لنا أن الخلاف في التقسيم من قبيل اختلاف الألفاظ لا الحقائق حيث يجمله بعضهم، ويفصله بعضهم الآخر، بما في ذلك تسمية الإمام الباقلاني للحاسة الباطنة بالحاسة السادسة من غير تقييد لها بحواس الباطن. بيد أن الخلاف الحقيقي هو في اعتبار العقل إحدى حواس العقل الباطنة، كما ذهبت إلى ذلك المدرسة الحسية الوضعية، وإن كان بعض الباحثين في إطار التربية الإسلامية وافق على ذلك باستناده إلى قول الله تعالى ﴿وَاللهُ أَخْرَجَكُمْ مِنْ بُطُونِ أُمَّهَاتِكُمْ لا تَعْلَمُونَ شَيْئاً وَجَعَلَ لَكُمُ السَّمْعَ وَالأَبْصَارَ وَالْأَفْئِدَةَ لَعَلَّكُمْ تَشْكُرُونَ﴾ [النحل: ٧٨/١٦). فعد الأفئدة المقرون بالسمع والبصر باعتبارها أبرز نعم الحواس خصت بالذكر دون سواها، فاستوجبت الشكر، وترتب عليها مسؤولية إنسانية أمام الخالق جل وعلا: ﴿إِنَّ السَّمْعَ وَالْبَصَرَ وَالْفُؤادَ كُلُّ أُولَئِكَ كَانَ عَنْهُ مَسْؤُولاً﴾ [الإسراء: ٢٣٦/١٧).
Chapter Three: Section One - Sense. First: The external senses, and they are five divisions: hearing, sight, touch, smell, and taste. And no one opposed that - to my knowledge - except Imam al-Baqillani (d. 403 AH), who counted the ways of knowledge as six: the five external senses, and he added what he called the sixth sense, which is a necessity that originates in the soul initially, without being present through some of these senses, such as a person's knowledge of himself and what he finds in himself of health and sickness, pleasure and pain, distress and joy, ability and inability, will and aversion, perception and blindness, and other things that occur in the soul, which a living being perceives when it experiences them. Second: The internal senses, and the expressions of ancient and modern researchers have varied regarding them. Some of them express them as internal sensation such as pleasure and pain, joy and sorrow, strength and anger; or anger and appetite; or the sensation of thirst, hunger, fatigue, and the like. And others expanded and counted the internal senses as five as follows: 1. Common sense (al-hiss al-mushtarak): it means the psychic power that reflects all the forms that permeate to it through the five senses, so they gather with tangible things, smells, etc., so it is called common sense. Its example is our vision of a flame that is rotated quickly in a circle even though it is not that in reality. 2. Imagination (al-khayal): it means that the forms that were imprinted in common sense, when they disappear, can be remembered by returning to imagination, therefore imagination is the storehouse of common sense. 3. Estimation (al-wahm): it means the power that perceives partial meanings, such as the enmity that the sheep perceives from the wolf. 4. Memory (al-hafiza): it means that the disappearance of the images of partial meanings in estimation can be remembered by returning to the memory, therefore it is called the storehouse of estimation. 5. The compositive imagination (al-mutakhayyila): it is that which relates some forms to others, and its example: the owner of this color has such a taste. And upon reflecting on the above, it appears to us that the disagreement in the division is a matter of differences in expressions, not realities, as some summarize it and others detail it, including the naming of Imam al-Baqillani for the internal sense as the sixth sense without restricting it to the internal senses. However, the real disagreement is regarding the consideration of the intellect as one of the internal senses, as the sensory-positivist school held, although some researchers within the framework of Islamic education agreed with that based on the saying of Allah Almighty: 'And Allah brought you out from the wombs of your mothers while you knew nothing, and He made for you hearing, sight, and hearts (af'ida) that you might be grateful' [Quran 16:78]. So he counted the hearts (af'ida) coupled with hearing and sight as the most prominent blessings of the senses, singled out for mention, thus necessitating gratitude, and resulting in human responsibility before the Creator: 'Indeed, the hearing, the sight, and the heart - all of those will be questioned' [Quran 17:236].
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage is a definitional exposition of the sensory faculties. The author begins by establishing the consensus on the five external senses (hearing, sight, touch, smell, taste) but notes one exception: Imam al-Baqillani, who counts a sixth sense. According to al-Baqillani, this sixth sense is an internal, self-evident awareness (ضَرورة تخترع في النفس) that arises without reliance on the external senses, such as knowledge of one's own health, emotions, and volitions. The author then transitions to the internal senses (الحواس الباطنة). He first observes that researchers have described internal sensations in different terms—some as pleasure/pain, others as anger/appetite, still others as thirst/hunger—indicating terminological variability. The main classification he adopts, however, enumerates five distinct internal powers: (1) Common sense (الحس المشترك), which synthesizes the forms arriving from the five external senses, exemplified by seeing a rotating flame as a circle when in reality it is a point moving rapidly. (2) Imagination (الخيال), which preserves forms after they disappear from common sense, serving as its storehouse. (3) Estimation (الوهم), which perceives particular, non-physical meanings like the sheep's perception of enmity from the wolf. (4) Memory (الحافظة), which retains the images of partial meanings after they leave estimation, acting as estimation's storehouse. (5) The compositive imagination (المتخيلة), which combines and relates images to one another, as in associating a color with a taste. Finally, the author reflects that most divisions are merely terminological differences, but a real dispute concerns whether intellect (العقل) should be counted among the internal senses. The sensory-positivist school affirms this, and some Islamic education researchers support it by citing Quran 16:78, which juxtaposes hearts (أفئدة) with hearing and sight as gifts from Allah, implying that the heart-as-intellect is a faculty of perception. The author mentions this view without fully endorsing it, presenting it as a genuine point of contention.

Key Terms
الحس
الحواس الظاهرة
الحاسة السادسة

Al-Baqillani's sixth sense is a faculty of immediate inner awareness, distinct from the five external senses.

What Is Mantiq?
intermediate
5 min
The Five Internal Senses and the Dispute over Intellect
Author enumerates five internal senses and discusses the real disagreement over intellect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to name the five internal senses according to the author, describe their functions, and identify the real disagreement over whether the intellect should be counted among them.

Core Idea
The five internal senses process and store sensory information; the real dispute is whether intellect is a sixth internal sense.

The author presents a detailed classification of internal senses: common sense, imagination, estimation, memory, and compositive imagination. He also addresses a terminological variation among scholars. Crucially, he identifies the genuine dispute: whether the intellect (al-'aql) should be considered one of the internal senses, a view supported by some using Quranic evidence about the heart (af'ida).

Guided Path
1
List the five internal senses
Read the enumeration starting from number 1 to 5. Write them down: common sense (al-hiss al-mushtarak), imagination (al-khayal), estimation (al-wahm), memory (al-hafiza), and compositive imagination (al-mutakhayyila).
The author says 'others expanded and counted the internal senses as five as follows.'
2
Understand the function of common sense
Common sense receives all forms from the external senses and unifies them. The example given is seeing a rotating flame as a circle, even though it is a point moving quickly. This shows how common sense synthesizes sensory input.
It is called 'common' because it collects inputs from all external senses.
3
Learn the role of imagination and memory as storehouses
Imagination preserves forms after they disappear from common sense; it is the storehouse of common sense. Memory retains the images of partial meanings from estimation; it is the storehouse of estimation. Note the parallel structure.
Imagination stores sensory images; memory stores abstract meanings perceived by estimation.
4
Examine estimation and compositive imagination
Estimation perceives partial meanings like enmity (e.g., a sheep perceiving a wolf as an enemy). Compositive imagination relates images to each other, e.g., associating a color with a taste.
These are higher cognitive processes beyond mere sensation.
5
Identify the real disagreement
The author states that the real disagreement is whether intellect (al-'aql) is an internal sense. The sensory-positivist school says yes, and some Islamic education researchers support this using Quran 16:78, where Allah mentions hearing, sight, and hearts (af'ida). They interpret 'hearts' as the intellect.
This is not merely terminological; it affects the understanding of human cognition and responsibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثالث: الفصل الأول - الحس
أولاً : الحواس الظاهرة وهي خمسة أقسام : السمع والبصر واللمس والشم والطعم.
ولم يخالف في ذلك حسب معرفتي - سوى الإمام الباقلاني (ت: ٤٠٣هـ) حيث عد طرق العلم ستا: الحواس الخمس الظاهرة، وأضاف ما أسماه بالحاسة السادسة وهي عبارة عن ضرورة تخترع في النفس ابتداء، من غير أن تكون موجودة ببعض هذه الحواس، كعلم الإنسان بنفسه وما يجده فيها من الصحة والسقم واللذة والألم والغم والفرح والقدرة والعجز والإرادة والكراهية والإدراك والعمى، وغير ذلك مما يحدث في النفس، مما يدركه الحي إذا وجد به.
ثانياً: الحواس الباطنة، وقد تعدّدت عبارات الباحثين القدامى والمحدثين حيالها، فبعضهم يعبر عنها بالإحساس الباطني كاللذة والألم، والفرح والحزن، والقوة والغضب. أو الغضب والشهوة أو الإحساس بالعطش والجوع والتعب ونحوها.
وتوسع آخرون فعدوا الحواس الباطنة خمساً على النحو التالي:
۱ - الحس المشترك ويعني القوة النفسية العاكسة لجميع الصور المتسربة إليها عن طريق الحواس الخمس فتجتمع بالملموسات والمشمومات... إلخ فسميت بالحس المشترك، ومثالها رؤيتنا للشعلة التي تدار بسرعة دائرة مع أنها ليست كذلك في حقيقة الأمر.
٢- الخيال ويعني أن الصور التي ارتسمت بالحس المشترك إذا غابت فيمكن أن تتذكر بالرجوع إلى الخيال، ولذلك فالخيال خزانة الحس المشترك.
٣- الوهم: ويعني القوة المدركة للمعاني الجزئية كالعداوة تدركها الشاة من الذئب.
٤ - الحافظة: وتعني أن ذهاب صور المعاني الجزئية في الوهم يمكن تذكرها بالرجوع إلى الحافظة، ولذلك تسمى خزانة الوهم.
٥ - المتخيلة: وهي التي تنسب بعض الصور إلى بعض ومثاله: صاحب هذا اللون له طعم كذا.
وبالتأمل فيما سبق يتبدى لنا أن الخلاف في التقسيم من قبيل اختلاف الألفاظ لا الحقائق حيث يجمله بعضهم، ويفصله بعضهم الآخر، بما في ذلك تسمية الإمام الباقلاني للحاسة الباطنة بالحاسة السادسة من غير تقييد لها بحواس الباطن. بيد أن الخلاف الحقيقي هو في اعتبار العقل إحدى حواس العقل الباطنة، كما ذهبت إلى ذلك المدرسة الحسية الوضعية، وإن كان بعض الباحثين في إطار التربية الإسلامية وافق على ذلك باستناده إلى قول الله تعالى ﴿وَاللهُ أَخْرَجَكُمْ مِنْ بُطُونِ أُمَّهَاتِكُمْ لا تَعْلَمُونَ شَيْئاً وَجَعَلَ لَكُمُ السَّمْعَ وَالأَبْصَارَ وَالْأَفْئِدَةَ لَعَلَّكُمْ تَشْكُرُونَ﴾ [النحل: ٧٨/١٦). فعد الأفئدة المقرون بالسمع والبصر باعتبارها أبرز نعم الحواس خصت بالذكر دون سواها، فاستوجبت الشكر، وترتب عليها مسؤولية إنسانية أمام الخالق جل وعلا: ﴿إِنَّ السَّمْعَ وَالْبَصَرَ وَالْفُؤادَ كُلُّ أُولَئِكَ كَانَ عَنْهُ مَسْؤُولاً﴾ [الإسراء: ٢٣٦/١٧).
Chapter Three: Section One - Sense. First: The external senses, and they are five divisions: hearing, sight, touch, smell, and taste. And no one opposed that - to my knowledge - except Imam al-Baqillani (d. 403 AH), who counted the ways of knowledge as six: the five external senses, and he added what he called the sixth sense, which is a necessity that originates in the soul initially, without being present through some of these senses, such as a person's knowledge of himself and what he finds in himself of health and sickness, pleasure and pain, distress and joy, ability and inability, will and aversion, perception and blindness, and other things that occur in the soul, which a living being perceives when it experiences them. Second: The internal senses, and the expressions of ancient and modern researchers have varied regarding them. Some of them express them as internal sensation such as pleasure and pain, joy and sorrow, strength and anger; or anger and appetite; or the sensation of thirst, hunger, fatigue, and the like. And others expanded and counted the internal senses as five as follows: 1. Common sense (al-hiss al-mushtarak): it means the psychic power that reflects all the forms that permeate to it through the five senses, so they gather with tangible things, smells, etc., so it is called common sense. Its example is our vision of a flame that is rotated quickly in a circle even though it is not that in reality. 2. Imagination (al-khayal): it means that the forms that were imprinted in common sense, when they disappear, can be remembered by returning to imagination, therefore imagination is the storehouse of common sense. 3. Estimation (al-wahm): it means the power that perceives partial meanings, such as the enmity that the sheep perceives from the wolf. 4. Memory (al-hafiza): it means that the disappearance of the images of partial meanings in estimation can be remembered by returning to the memory, therefore it is called the storehouse of estimation. 5. The compositive imagination (al-mutakhayyila): it is that which relates some forms to others, and its example: the owner of this color has such a taste. And upon reflecting on the above, it appears to us that the disagreement in the division is a matter of differences in expressions, not realities, as some summarize it and others detail it, including the naming of Imam al-Baqillani for the internal sense as the sixth sense without restricting it to the internal senses. However, the real disagreement is regarding the consideration of the intellect as one of the internal senses, as the sensory-positivist school held, although some researchers within the framework of Islamic education agreed with that based on the saying of Allah Almighty: 'And Allah brought you out from the wombs of your mothers while you knew nothing, and He made for you hearing, sight, and hearts (af'ida) that you might be grateful' [Quran 16:78]. So he counted the hearts (af'ida) coupled with hearing and sight as the most prominent blessings of the senses, singled out for mention, thus necessitating gratitude, and resulting in human responsibility before the Creator: 'Indeed, the hearing, the sight, and the heart - all of those will be questioned' [Quran 17:236].
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage is a definitional exposition of the sensory faculties. The author begins by establishing the consensus on the five external senses (hearing, sight, touch, smell, taste) but notes one exception: Imam al-Baqillani, who counts a sixth sense. According to al-Baqillani, this sixth sense is an internal, self-evident awareness (ضَرورة تخترع في النفس) that arises without reliance on the external senses, such as knowledge of one's own health, emotions, and volitions. The author then transitions to the internal senses (الحواس الباطنة). He first observes that researchers have described internal sensations in different terms—some as pleasure/pain, others as anger/appetite, still others as thirst/hunger—indicating terminological variability. The main classification he adopts, however, enumerates five distinct internal powers: (1) Common sense (الحس المشترك), which synthesizes the forms arriving from the five external senses, exemplified by seeing a rotating flame as a circle when in reality it is a point moving rapidly. (2) Imagination (الخيال), which preserves forms after they disappear from common sense, serving as its storehouse. (3) Estimation (الوهم), which perceives particular, non-physical meanings like the sheep's perception of enmity from the wolf. (4) Memory (الحافظة), which retains the images of partial meanings after they leave estimation, acting as estimation's storehouse. (5) The compositive imagination (المتخيلة), which combines and relates images to one another, as in associating a color with a taste. Finally, the author reflects that most divisions are merely terminological differences, but a real dispute concerns whether intellect (العقل) should be counted among the internal senses. The sensory-positivist school affirms this, and some Islamic education researchers support it by citing Quran 16:78, which juxtaposes hearts (أفئدة) with hearing and sight as gifts from Allah, implying that the heart-as-intellect is a faculty of perception. The author mentions this view without fully endorsing it, presenting it as a genuine point of contention.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

What Is Mantiq?

Desires, Values, and Sensory Blindness
Author explains how desires affect senses, then critiques empiricism as sole source of knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify how internal factors (desires, values) affect sensory perception according to the Qur'an and modern psychology.

Core Idea
Desires can blind the senses as surely as physical defects.

Before attacking empiricism head-on, the author establishes that sensory perception is not purely physical but is heavily influenced by psychological and spiritual factors. Using Qur'anic verses and modern psychoanalytic findings, he shows that desires and values can distort or even nullify what we perceive. Understanding this sets the stage for the deeper logical critique.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening claim
The author states that senses are limited by their created nature, and motives and values influence attention and perception. Underline the key terms: دوافع (motives) and قيم (values).
This is a foundational claim that perception is not neutral.
2
Identify the Quranic evidence
Locate the verses about disbelievers having hearts that do not understand, eyes that do not see, ears that do not hear. Note that these verses describe sensory failure despite physical organs being intact. The cause is spiritual: their whims (أهواء) and rejection of truth.
The verses demonstrate that internal states can override sensory function.
3
Connect to modern psychology
The author references modern experimental studies in psychoanalysis showing that people tend not to perceive things that disturb them. This aligns with the Quranic description: sensory perception is filtered by desires and fears.
This strengthens the argument by showing empirical confirmation.
4
Recognize the purpose
The author is not just describing a phenomenon; he is laying the groundwork for his critique of empiricism. If senses can be blocked by internal factors, then relying solely on sense as a source of knowledge is unreliable.
This step bridges to the next lesson's objections.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثالث: الفصل الأول - الحس. وإذا كانت الحواس محدودة من حيث طبيعتها التي خلقت عليها فإن دوافع الفرد وقيمه ذات تأثير في انتباهه وإدراكه الحسي. وهذا ما توصلت إليه نتائج الدراسات التجريبية الحديثة في مجال التحليل النفسي، حيث أوضحت أن الإنسان يميل إلى عدم إدراك الأشياء التي تزعجه وتقلقه والمتعارضة مع أهوائه ورغباته. وذلك ما يشير إليه القرآن عندما يعرض لحال الكافرين الذين لم يستفيدوا من حواسهم وعقولهم نتيجة الدوافع والقيم والأهواء التي تملكنهم: وَلَقَدْ ذَرَأْنَا لِجَهَنَّمَ كَثِيراً مِنَ الْجِنِّ وَالإِنْسِ لَهُمْ قُلُوبٌ لا يَفْقَهُونَ بِها وَلَهُمْ أَعْيُنٌ لا يُبْصِرُونَ بِها وَلَهُمْ آذَانٌ لا يَسْمَعُونَ بِهَا أُولَئِكَ كَالأَنْعَامِ بَلْ هُمْ أَضَلُّ أُولَئِكَ هُمُ الْغَافِلُونَ ﴾ [الأعراف: ۱۷۹/۷]. ... قُلْ هُوَ لِلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا هُدَى وَشِفَاءٌ وَالَّذِينَ لَا يُؤْمِنُونَ فِي آذَانِهِمْ وَقَرٌ وَهُوَ عَلَيْهِمْ عَمَى أُولَئِكَ يُنادَوْنَ مِنْ مَكان بَعِيد [فصلت: ٤٤/٤١]. أُولَئِكَ الَّذِينَ لَعَنَهُمُ اللهُ فَأَصَمَّهُمْ وَأَعْمَى أَبْصَارَهُمْ [عمده: ٢٣/٤٧]. أفَأَنتَ تُسْمِعُ الصُّمَّ أَوْ تَهْدِي الْعُمْيَ وَمَنْ كَانَ فِي ضَلالٍ مُبِينٍ (الزخرف: ١٤٠/٤٣). وإذا كان هناك عمى حسي ناتج عن الخلقة ابتداءً فإن هناك عمى طارئاً يولّده الهوى أو الحب، ولذلك فإن العاشق أو صاحب الهوى محجوب عن أشياء كثيرة لا يراها في حين يراها غيره إذ هو مصاب بعمى جزئي طارئ بسبب عشقه أو هواه، فلا يرى إلا البعد الذي يزيده هوى أو عشقاً. ولذلك جاء في قوم نوح: فَكَذَّبُوهُ فَأَنجَيْنَاهُ وَالَّذِينَ مَعَهُ فِي الْفُلْكِ وَأَغْرَقْنَا الَّذِينَ كَذَّبُوا بِآيَاتِنا إِنَّهُمْ كَانُوا قَوْماً عَمِينَ﴾ [الأعراف: ٦٤/٧]. وعن المنافقين: مَثَلُهُمْ كَمَثَلِ الَّذِي اسْتَوْقَدَ نَاراً فَلَمّا أَضَاءَتْ مَا حَوْلَهُ ذَهَبَ اللَّهُ بِنُورِهِمْ وَتَرَكَهُمْ فِي ظُلُماتِ لا يُبْصِرُونَ، صُمٌّ بُكْمٌ عُمْيٌ فَهُمْ لا يَرْجِعُونَ [البقرة: ۱۷/۲-۱۸]. وعن الكافرين عموماً: ﴿وَمَثَلُ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا كَمَثَلِ الَّذِي يَنْعِقُ بِما لَا يَسْمَعُ إِلَّا دُعاء وَنِدَاءً صُمٌ بُكْمٌ عُمْيٌ فَهُمْ لا يَعْقِلُونَ) [البقرة: ١٧٩/٢]. هنا يتضح أن الاقتصار على الحس طريقاً وحيداً للمعرفة يعرض القائلين به لمزالق ومآخذ كثيرة أبرزها: ۱ - في هذا القول تحديد لطاقة الفكر البشري، وإنقاص لفعالية العقل بوصفه طريقاً للمعرفة. حيث إن تقرير طريقة الحس إنما أتت بناءً على حكم العقل، وإن لم يعلن الحسيّون ذلك صراحة. ذلك أنهم يدركون أن الحس لا يمكن أن يكون هو الذي قرّر قاعدتهم تلك، لأن الشيء لا يكون دليلاً على صدق نفسه. ٢- لو اعتمدنا على الحس طريقاً وحيداً للمعرفة لما استطعنا الحكم باستحالة شيء مطلقاً، لأن الاستحالة التي تعني عدم إمكان وجود الشيء ليس مما يدخل في نطاق التجربة، ولا يمكن للحواس أن تكشف عنه. وكون الحسيين يزعمون أنه لا موجود إلا المحسوس بصيغة الحصر فإنهم يكونون قد تجاوزوا حدود اختصاصهم، وانتقلوا من الحكم باستحالة تصور شيء أو إحساسه إلى الحكم.
Chapter Three: Section One - The Sense. And if the senses are limited by their nature on which they were created, then the individual's motives and values have an influence on his attention and sensory perception. This is what the results of modern experimental studies in the field of psychoanalysis have reached, where they clarified that man tends not to perceive things that disturb and worry him and that contradict his whims and desires. And that is what the Qur'an indicates when it presents the condition of the disbelievers who did not benefit from their senses and minds as a result of motives, values, and whims that possessed them: 'And We have certainly created for Hell many of the jinn and mankind. They have hearts with which they do not understand, they have eyes with which they do not see, and they have ears with which they do not hear. Those are like livestock; rather, they are more astray. Those are the heedless.' [Al-A'raf 7:179]. ... 'Say, it is for those who believe a guidance and healing. And those who do not believe - in their ears is deafness, and it is upon them blindness. Those are being called from a distant place.' [Fussilat 41:44]. 'Those are the ones whom Allah has cursed, so He made them deaf and blinded their vision.' [Muhammad 47:23]. 'So can you make the deaf hear or guide the blind or he who is in clear error?' [Az-Zukhruf 43:40]. And if there is sensory blindness resulting from creation initially, then there is an accidental blindness generated by whim or love, and therefore the lover or the one with a whim is veiled from many things that he does not see while others see them, for he is afflicted with a partial accidental blindness due to his love or whim, so he sees only the dimension that increases his whim or love. And so it came regarding the people of Noah: 'But they denied him, so We saved him and those with him in the ship, and We drowned those who denied Our signs. Indeed, they were a blind people.' [Al-A'raf 7:64]. And about the hypocrites: 'Their example is like that of one who kindled a fire, but when it illuminated what was around him, Allah took away their light and left them in darkness [so] they could not see. Deaf, dumb, and blind, so they will not return.' [Al-Baqarah 2:17-18]. And about the disbelievers generally: 'And the example of those who disbelieve is like that of one who shouts at that which hears nothing but calls and cries. Deaf, dumb, and blind, so they do not reason.' [Al-Baqarah 2:171]. Here it becomes clear that restricting [knowledge] to sense as the sole path of knowledge exposes its proponents to many pitfalls and objections, the most prominent of which are: 1 - In this statement there is a limitation of the capacity of human thought and a reduction of the effectiveness of the intellect as a path of knowledge. For the determination of the sensory method came based on the judgment of the intellect, even if the empiricists do not declare that explicitly. That is because they realize that sense cannot be the one that established that rule, because a thing cannot be evidence of its own truth. 2 - If we relied on sense as the sole path of knowledge, we would not be able to judge the impossibility of anything absolutely, because impossibility, which means the non-possibility of the existence of a thing, does not fall within the scope of experience, and senses cannot reveal it. And the fact that the empiricists claim that nothing exists except the sensible in a restrictive form, they would have exceeded the limits of their specialization, and moved from judging the impossibility of conceiving or sensing something to judging [its impossibility of existence].
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage critiques the doctrine of empiricism (al-hissiyya) by first establishing the inherent limitations of sensory perception due to internal factors like desires and values, then exposing logical flaws in the claim that sense is the sole source of knowledge. The author begins by acknowledging that senses are limited by their created nature, but emphasizes that motives and values further distort attention and perception, citing modern psychoanalytic findings that confirm the Qur'anic descriptions of disbelievers who fail to use their senses and reason due to their whims. Qur'anic verses are presented to show that even when senses are intact, they can be rendered ineffective by spiritual blindness (e.g., deafness, blindness, and muteness as metaphors for rejection of truth). Examples include the people of Noah (blindness), hypocrites (deaf, dumb, blind), and a general analogy of those who disbelieve being like animals that cannot reason. From this, the author draws a critical conclusion: restricting knowledge to sense alone leads to serious problems. The first problem is that this doctrine implicitly relies on a judgment of the intellect (to decide that sense is the criterion), yet empiricists do not acknowledge this—a thing cannot be evidence of its own truth. The second problem is that empirical observation cannot establish absolute impossibility because impossibility is not within the scope of sensory experience; thus, when empiricists claim that only the sensible exists, they overstep their boundaries and illicitly infer from 'we cannot conceive/sense it' to 'it cannot exist.' The argument is epistemological and critical, using Islamic scripture as evidence for the limitation of senses.

Two Logical Objections to Empiricism
Author explains how desires affect senses, then critiques empiricism as sole source of knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct and evaluate the two objections the author raises against the claim that sense is the sole source of knowledge.

Core Idea
Empiricism refutes itself: it must rely on reason to deny reason.

Having shown that sensory perception is influenced by desires, the author now delivers two powerful logical blows against empiricism. The first objection reveals that empiricism is self-refuting because it depends on a prior judgment of reason. The second shows that empiricism oversteps its bounds by claiming to know absolute impossibility, which lies outside sensory experience. These objections are classic in Islamic epistemology and are still debated today.

Guided Path
1
Locate the two objections
In the Arabic text, find the numbered points 1 and 2 after the Qur'anic verses. These are the author's explicit objections. Mark them clearly.
They are labeled with Arabic numerals: ۱ and ٢.
2
Analyze the first objection: self-refutation
Objection 1: The empiricist rule 'sense is the sole source of knowledge' was itself arrived at by an act of reason. Yet empiricists claim to deny reason's authority. This is self-refuting because the rule cannot be sensibly proven; it requires a rational judgment.
The key phrase: 'الشيء لا يكون دليلاً على صدق نفسه' (a thing cannot be evidence of its own truth).
3
Analyze the second objection: impossibility exceeds sense
Objection 2: Empiricists claim that nothing exists except the sensible. But to assert that something is impossible (cannot exist) is not something that can be experienced. Impossibility is a modal judgment beyond sensory reach. So empiricists illicitly infer from 'we cannot sense X' to 'X cannot exist'.
The author calls this 'exceeding the limits of specialization' (جاوزوا حدود اختصاصهم).
4
Evaluate the strength of the objections
Consider whether these objections hold logically. The first shows an inconsistency in the empiricist position. The second points out an overextension. Both are valid critiques if empiricism claims exclusivity. Think about how an empiricist might respond.
This step deepens understanding of the debate.

صاحب الهوى محجوب عن أشياء كثيرة لا يراها في حين يراها غيره إذ هو مصاب بعمى جزئي طارئ بسبب عشقه أو هواه، فلا يرى إلا البعد الذي يزيده هوى أو عشقاً. ولذلك جاء في قوم نوح: فَكَذَّبُوهُ فَأَنجَيْنَاهُ وَالَّذِينَ مَعَهُ فِي الْفُلْكِ وَأَغْرَقْنَا الَّذِينَ كَذَّبُوا بِآيَاتِنا إِنَّهُمْ كَانُوا قَوْماً عَمِينَ﴾ [الأعراف: ٦٤/٧]. وعن المنافقين: مَثَلُهُمْ كَمَثَلِ الَّذِي اسْتَوْقَدَ نَاراً فَلَمّا كَفَرُوا كَمَثَلِ الَّذِي يَنْعِقُ بِما لَا يَسْمَعُ إِلَّا دُعاء وَنِدَاءً صُمٌ بُكْمٌ عُمْيٌ فَهُمْ لا يَعْقِلُونَ) [البقرة: ١٧٩/٢]. هنا يتضح أن الاقتصار على الحس طريقاً وحيداً للمعرفة يعرض القائلين به لمزالق ومآخذ كثيرة أبرزها: ۱ - في هذا القول تحديد لطاقة الفكر البشري، وإنقاص لفعالية العقل بوصفه طريقاً للمعرفة. حيث إن تقرير طريقة الحس إنما أتت بناءً على حكم العقل، وإن لم يعلن الحسيّون ذلك صراحة. ذلك أنهم يدركون أن الحس لا يمكن أن يكون هو الذي قرّر قاعدتهم تلك، لأن الشيء لا يكون دليلاً على صدق نفسه. ٢- لو اعتمدنا على الحس طريقاً وحيداً للمعرفة لما استطعنا الحكم باستحالة شيء مطلقاً، لأن الاستحالة التي تعني عدم إمكان وجود الشيء ليس مما يدخل في نطاق التجربة، ولا يمكن للحواس أن تكشف عنه. وكون الحسيين يزعمون أنه لا موجود إلا المحسوس بصيغة الحصر فإنهم يكونون قد تجاوزوا حدود اختصاصهم، وانتقلوا من الحكم باستحالة تصور شيء أو إحساسه إلى الحكم.
Chapter Three: Section One - The Sense. And if the senses are limited by their nature on which they were created, then the individual's motives and values have an influence on his attention and sensory perception. This is what the results of modern experimental studies in the field of psychoanalysis have reached, where they clarified that man tends not to perceive things that disturb and worry him and that contradict his whims and desires. And that is what the Qur'an indicates when it presents the condition of the disbelievers who did not benefit from their senses and minds as a result of motives, values, and whims that possessed them: 'And We have certainly created for Hell many of the jinn and mankind. They have hearts with which they do not understand, they have eyes with which they do not see, and they have ears with which they do not hear. Those are like livestock; rather, they are more astray. Those are the heedless.' [Al-A'raf 7:179]. ... 'Say, it is for those who believe a guidance and healing. And those who do not believe - in their ears is deafness, and it is upon them blindness. Those are being called from a distant place.' [Fussilat 41:44]. 'Those are the ones whom Allah has cursed, so He made them deaf and blinded their vision.' [Muhammad 47:23]. 'So can you make the deaf hear or guide the blind or he who is in clear error?' [Az-Zukhruf 43:40]. And if there is sensory blindness resulting from creation initially, then there is an accidental blindness generated by whim or love, and therefore the lover or the one with a whim is veiled from many things that he does not see while others see them, for he is afflicted with a partial accidental blindness due to his love or whim, so he sees only the dimension that increases his whim or love. And so it came regarding the people of Noah: 'But they denied him, so We saved him and those with him in the ship, and We drowned those who denied Our signs. Indeed, they were a blind people.' [Al-A'raf 7:64]. And about the hypocrites: 'Their example is like that of one who kindled a fire, but when it illuminated what was around him, Allah took away their light and left them in darkness [so] they could not see. Deaf, dumb, and blind, so they will not return.' [Al-Baqarah 2:17-18]. And about the disbelievers generally: 'And the example of those who disbelieve is like that of one who shouts at that which hears nothing but calls and cries. Deaf, dumb, and blind, so they do not reason.' [Al-Baqarah 2:171]. Here it becomes clear that restricting [knowledge] to sense as the sole path of knowledge exposes its proponents to many pitfalls and objections, the most prominent of which are: 1 - In this statement there is a limitation of the capacity of human thought and a reduction of the effectiveness of the intellect as a path of knowledge. For the determination of the sensory method came based on the judgment of the intellect, even if the empiricists do not declare that explicitly. That is because they realize that sense cannot be the one that established that rule, because a thing cannot be evidence of its own truth. 2 - If we relied on sense as the sole path of knowledge, we would not be able to judge the impossibility of anything absolutely, because impossibility, which means the non-possibility of the existence of a thing, does not fall within the scope of experience, and senses cannot reveal it. And the fact that the empiricists claim that nothing exists except the sensible in a restrictive form, they would have exceeded the limits of their specialization, and moved from judging the impossibility of conceiving or sensing something to judging [its impossibility of existence].
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage critiques the doctrine of empiricism (al-hissiyya) by first establishing the inherent limitations of sensory perception due to internal factors like desires and values, then exposing logical flaws in the claim that sense is the sole source of knowledge. The author begins by acknowledging that senses are limited by their created nature, but emphasizes that motives and values further distort attention and perception, citing modern psychoanalytic findings that confirm the Qur'anic descriptions of disbelievers who fail to use their senses and reason due to their whims. Qur'anic verses are presented to show that even when senses are intact, they can be rendered ineffective by spiritual blindness (e.g., deafness, blindness, and muteness as metaphors for rejection of truth). Examples include the people of Noah (blindness), hypocrites (deaf, dumb, blind), and a general analogy of those who disbelieve being like animals that cannot reason. From this, the author draws a critical conclusion: restricting knowledge to sense alone leads to serious problems. The first problem is that this doctrine implicitly relies on a judgment of the intellect (to decide that sense is the criterion), yet empiricists do not acknowledge this—a thing cannot be evidence of its own truth. The second problem is that empirical observation cannot establish absolute impossibility because impossibility is not within the scope of sensory experience; thus, when empiricists claim that only the sensible exists, they overstep their boundaries and illicitly infer from 'we cannot conceive/sense it' to 'it cannot exist.' The argument is epistemological and critical, using Islamic scripture as evidence for the limitation of senses.

Linguistic Definition of 'Aql (Intellect)
Author presents rationalist critique and linguistic definition of 'aql.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define 'aql linguistically and explain its etymological connection to restraint.

Core Idea
'Aql linguistically means 'to restrain' – it is the faculty that prevents falling into error.

In this passage, the author sets up a debate between rationalists and empiricists about the reliability of sense perception. To ground the discussion, he turns to the linguistic definition of 'aql, revealing its deep connection to inhibition and comprehension. Let's unpack this definition step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rationalist critique of sense
Find the claims made against sense perception: the senses are deceptive, lying, erroneous; they only capture one state of a thing, not all; some rationalists deny that anything external reaches the soul.
This sets the context for why defining 'aql is important.
2
Extract the linguistic meaning of 'aql
Look for the phrase 'al-'aql lughatan: al-hajr wa al-nahy' (prevention and prohibition, opposite of folly). Note that it is a verbal noun (masdar).
The plural is 'uqool.
3
Understand Sibawayh's grammatical note
Sibawayh considers 'aql an adjective because the pattern maf'ool is not typical for masdars. This shows attention to Arabic morphology.
This is a linguistic nuance, not a logical one.
4
Connect the linguistic meaning to the function
The author explains: 'aql restrains its possessor from falling into perils (ya'qilu 'an al-tawarrut) and allows grasping realities (ya'qilu bihi haqa'iq al-ashya').
The dual function: ethical inhibition and cognitive apprehension.
5
Formulate your own definition
Combine the linguistic and functional aspects: 'aql is the faculty that prevents errors and enables understanding of true realities.
This prepares for technical definitions used in mantiq.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثاني العقل
إذا كان الحس مصدراً من مصادر المعرفة و طريقة من طرائقها حسبما سبق - فإن أصحاب المذهب العقلي لا يوافقون على ذلك، بل يعدون الحواس خداعة كذابة مخطئه. إذ لو كانت معارفنا قائمه بالفعل على الحس لكانت المعرفة مستحيلة، ذلك أن الإدراك و التجربة يخبراننا عن التعلق بحال واحدة من أحوال الشيء، دون تناول جميع أحواله وإن الحواس أقرب إلى عدو المعرفة منها إلى خادمها. بل لقد غلا بعضهم في معارضة الحسيين إلى الحد الذي ادعى فيه أنه لا يصل شيء إلى النفس من الخارج، كما لا يمكن للنفس أن تبتكر شيئاً إذا لم يكن الأصل فيها العقل(۱).
·
ولتحرير النزاع حول هذا الأمر يحسن بنا أن نتناوله ابتداء من التعريف.

Chapter Two: The Intellect
If sense is a source of knowledge and a method among its methods as previously - then the proponents of the rationalist school do not agree with that, rather they consider the senses to be deceptive, lying, and erroneous. For if our knowledge were actually based on sense, knowledge would be impossible, because perception and experience inform us about attachment to one state among the states of a thing, without covering all its states, and the senses are closer to being an enemy of knowledge than its servant. Rather, some of them went so far in opposing the sensualists to the extent that they claimed that nothing reaches the soul from the outside, and also that the soul cannot invent anything if the original principle in it is not the intellect.
·
To settle the dispute about this matter, it is good for us to approach it starting from the definition.
Definition of the Intellect
'Alaq' linguistically means: prevention and prohibition, opposite of folly, plural 'uqool. It is a verbal noun (masdar), although Sibawayh considers it an adjective, because the verbal noun absolutely does not come on the pattern of maf'ool. And it was called 'aql because it restrains its possessor from falling into perils, i.e., it prevents him. Or because through it one grasps the realities of things.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage presents a definition of the intellect ('aql) from linguistic and semantic perspectives, preceded by a summary of the rationalist critique of sense perception. The author first states that rationalists consider the senses deceptive and unreliable; if knowledge were based solely on sense, it would be impossible because sense perception only captures one aspect of a thing, not all its states. Some rationalists even deny that anything external reaches the soul, asserting the intellect as the origin of knowledge. To resolve the dispute, the author begins with a definition. Linguistically, 'aql means prevention (al-hajr) and prohibition (al-nahy), the opposite of folly. It is a verbal noun (masdar), though Sibawayh treats it as an adjective because the pattern maf'ool is atypical for masdars. It is called 'aql because it restrains ('aqala) its possessor from falling into perils, or because through it one comprehends ('aqala) the realities of things. The definition emphasizes 'aql as a restraining faculty, linking it to Islamic legal responsibility (taklif) and intellectual grasp.

Key Terms
العقل (al-'aql): Linguistically: prevention and prohibition, opposite of folly. Terminologically: the faculty that restrains from perils or grasps realities. [Note: In classical mantiq, 'aql is often the faculty of reasoning; here the focus is linguistic and also related to ethical restraint.]
الحس (al-hiss): Sense perception, considered by rationalists as deceptive and providing only partial knowledge. [Note: In earlier works, hiss is a valid source of knowledge but limited; here it is critiqued.]
المذهب العقلي (al-madhhab al-'aqli): The rationalist school that prioritizes intellect over senses as a source of knowledge. [Note: This is a modern classification; classical Islamic philosophy distinguishes between rationalists (e.g., Mu'tazila) and others, but not exactly as here.]
سيبویه (Sibawayh): The famous grammarian (d. 180 AH/796 CE) cited for his view that 'aql is an adjective because of its pattern. [Note: Sibawayh is a grammarian, not a logician; his grammatical analysis is used here to clarify the word's form.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the linguistic meaning of the word 'aql?
A) Intelligence and wisdom.
B) Prevention and prohibition.
C) Reflection and contemplation.
D) Understanding and comprehension.

Key Takeaway
The linguistic definition of 'aql reveals that it is fundamentally a restraining faculty, which informs its technical use in Islamic logic and law.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Convert it into a categorical syllogism using Islamic examples: e.g., 'Every sense perception is partial. Partial perception cannot give complete knowledge. Therefore, sense perception cannot give complete knowledge.' Check the validity.

Defining the Intellect ('Aql): Linguistic and Philosophical Perspectives
Author presents various definitions of 'aql (intellect).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the linguistic and philosophical definitions of 'aql (intellect) and identify its three main philosophical meanings.

Core Idea
The intellect is both a faculty and the knowledge it produces; philosophers define it in multiple ways.

In this passage, the author presents a comprehensive overview of how 'aql (intellect) is defined both linguistically and philosophically. Understanding these definitions is crucial because 'aql is the foundational tool for all logical reasoning in the Islamic tradition. Let's unpack the different layers of meaning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic linguistic definition
The passage begins by defining 'aql as the power prepared to receive knowledge and also as the knowledge acquired through that power. Note the dual usage: it refers both to the faculty and to its product.
This dual meaning is important in Islamic logic where 'aql sometimes means the innate faculty and sometimes acquired knowledge.
2
List the three philosophical definitions
The author gives three general philosophical meanings: (1) tool for distinguishing truth from falsehood, right from wrong; (2) highest form of mental operations, especially demonstration and inference; (3) certain principles upon which all rational people agree.
These definitions are not mutually exclusive but highlight different functions of the intellect.
3
Examine the three aspects according to most philosophers
The majority of philosophers view 'aql in three aspects: (a) a praiseworthy state manifested in speech, choice, movements, and stillness; (b) combined meanings in the mind that form premises from which goals and benefits are deduced; (c) a power that perceives the qualities of things—their beauty/ugliness or perfection/deficiency.
These aspects focus on the intellect as an ethical and practical faculty, not just a cognitive one.
4
Connect to Western rationalism
The author concludes by noting that these meanings gave rise to Western rationalism (intellectualism). Reflect on how the Islamic conception of 'aql differs from the Cartesian or Hegelian version.
In the Islamic tradition, 'aql is always linked to revelation (wahy) and cannot be an independent source of truth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثالث: الفصل الثاني - العقل
والعقل هو القوه المتهيئة لقبول العلم، ويطلق على العلم الذي يستفيده الإنسان عن طريق العقل.
وفي الاصطلاح الفلسفي: ورد تعريف العقل لدى الفلاسفة بمعنى من المعاني التالية:
١ - أداة التمييز بين الحق و الباطل و الصواب والخطأ.
٢- أسمى صور العمليات الذهنية بعامة والبرهنة والاستدلال بوجه خاص.
٣- المبادئ اليقينية التي يلتقي عندها العقلاء جميعاً.
وجمهور الفلاسفة يطلق العقل على ثلاثة أوجه هي:
(۱) هيئة محمودة للإنسان في كلامه واختياره، وحركاته وسكناته. (۲) معان مجتمعة في الذهن تكون مقدمات فتستنبط بها الأغراض والمصالح.
(۳) قوة تدرك صفات الأشياء من حسنها وقبحها، أو كمالها و نقصانها.
إن هذه المعاني هي التي أفرزت ما عُرف لدى الغرب بالمذهب العقلي (Intellectualisme) أو العقليين (Rationalists)، وهو عبارة عن القول بأن كل ما هو موجود فهو مردود إلى مبادئ عقلية. وهو مذهب ديكارت واسبينوزا، وليبنز، وفولف وهيجل...
Chapter Three: Section Two - The Intellect. The intellect is the power prepared to receive knowledge, and it is applied to the knowledge that a person acquires through the intellect. In the philosophical terminology: the definition of the intellect came from the philosophers in one of the following meanings: 1- The tool of distinction between truth and falsehood, and right and wrong. 2- The highest form of mental operations in general, and demonstration and inference in particular. 3- The certain principles upon which all rational people agree. The majority of philosophers apply the intellect in three aspects: (1) A praiseworthy state for a person in his speech, choice, movements, and stillness. (2) Combined meanings in the mind that form premises from which goals and benefits are deduced. (3) A power that perceives the qualities of things: their beauty and ugliness, or their perfection and deficiency. These meanings are what gave rise to what is known in the West as intellectualism (Intellectualisme) or rationalists (Rationalists), which is the statement that everything that exists is reducible to rational principles. It is the doctrine of Descartes, Spinoza, Leibniz, Wolff, and Hegel...
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage provides a comprehensive overview of the various definitions of 'aql (intellect) from both linguistic and philosophical perspectives. The author begins with a basic definition: the intellect is the faculty prepared to receive knowledge, and also refers to the knowledge acquired through this faculty. Then, three philosophical definitions are listed: (1) as a tool for distinguishing truth from falsehood, (2) as the highest form of mental operations, especially demonstration and inference, and (3) as the certain principles that are universally agreed upon by rational people. Next, the majority of philosophers view the intellect in three aspects: (a) as a praiseworthy state manifest in a person's speech and actions, (b) as combined mental premises used to deduce goals and benefits, and (c) as a power perceiving the good and bad qualities of things. The passage concludes by linking these meanings to the Western intellectual movement of rationalism, noting its key proponents. Throughout, the emphasis is on the intellect as a cognitive faculty and a source of knowledge.

Key Terms
العقل
المذهب العقلي

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) A tool for distinguishing truth from falsehood

Key Takeaway
The intellect (al-'aql) is understood both as a faculty and as acquired knowledge, with multiple philosophical layers that inform its role in logic and rational inquiry.

Al-Ghazali's Homonymous Analysis of 'Aql
Author enumerates al-Ghazali's homonymous meanings of 'aql.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the four (or five) distinct meanings of the term 'aql according to al-Ghazali and identify which meaning is being used in a given context from Islamic kalam.

Core Idea
'Aql is not one thing—it is five distinct but related concepts.

Al-Ghazali, one of the great systematizers of Islamic thought, noticed that the term 'aql (intellect/reason) is used in multiple ways in the Islamic tradition. To avoid confusion, he distinguished four primary meanings and added a fifth. This lesson will guide you through each meaning and show you how this tool helps clarify discussions in kalam, usul al-fiqh, and philosophy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first meaning: knowledge of realities
Look for the definition: 'aql as the attribute of knowledge located in the physical heart. Understand that this is the content, not the faculty.
2
Identify the second meaning: the perceiver of sciences
Here 'aql is the subtle substance (the physical spirit) that perceives. It is the instrument of perception.
3
Identify the third meaning: the rational soul's attribute
This is the attribute of the rational soul that controls the appetitive soul. It is a moral-intellectual faculty.
4
Identify the fourth meaning: the locus of perception
This is the place or subject that perceives, i.e., the mind or heart as a container.
5
Identify the added fifth meaning: the knowing subtle substance
This is the human subtle substance that knows and perceives; all four previous expressions can be applied to it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعنده – أي الغزالي- أن العقل اسم يطلق بالاشتراك لمعان أربعة مختلفة هي: المعنى الأول: قد يطلق ويراد به العلم بحقائق الأمور فيكون عبارة عن صفة العلم الذي محله (القلب الجسماني). المعنى الثاني: قد يطلق ويراد به المدرك للعلوم، فيكون هو لطيفة القلب (الروح الجسماني). المعنى الثالث قد يطلق ويراد به صفة العالم النفس الشهوانية). المعنى الرابع: قد يطلق ويراد به محل الإدراك أي المدرك (العلوم). وقد يضاف معنى خامس وهو اللطيفة العالمة المدركة من الإنسان والألفاظ الأربعة بجملتها تتوارد عليها (٢).
And according to him – al-Ghazali – that 'aql is a term used homonymously for four different meanings: The first meaning: it is used to mean knowledge of the realities of things, thus it is an expression for the attribute of knowledge whose locus is the physical heart. The second meaning: it is used to mean the perceiver of sciences, thus it is the subtle substance of the heart (the physical spirit). The third meaning: it is used to mean the attribute of the rational soul that controls the appetitive soul. The fourth meaning: it is used to mean the locus of perception, i.e., the perceiver of sciences. And a fifth meaning may be added, which is the knowing, perceiving subtle substance in man, and the four expressions as a whole are applicable to it.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage presents al-Ghazali's analysis of the term 'aql (intellect/rationality). The author notes that 'aql is a polysemous term used homonymously for four distinct meanings. First, it can refer to the knowledge of realities itself, an attribute located in the physical heart. Second, it can refer to the perceiver of sciences, which is the subtle spiritual substance of the heart (ruh jismani). Third, it can refer to the attribute of the rational soul that controls the appetitive soul. Fourth, it can refer to the locus of perception itself. A fifth meaning is added: the knowing, perceiving subtle substance in man, which all four expressions can denote. This shows that Ghazali distinguishes between the faculty, its attribute, and its locus, a nuanced epistemological analysis rooted in his spiritual psychology.

Key Terms
العقل
القلب الجسماني
الروح الجسماني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Three
B) Four
C) Five
D) Six

Key Takeaway
Al-Ghazali's homonymous analysis of 'aql reveals that a single term can have multiple distinct technical meanings, each with its own locus and function.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Quranic Definition and Division of 'Aql
Quranic definition and division of 'aql

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Quranic definition of 'aql and distinguish between its two types: innate and acquired.

Core Idea
The intellect is both an innate potential and an acquired reality; one empowers the other.

This passage concludes the discussion on the definition of 'aql in a Quranic theory of logic text. The author provides a concise Quranic definition and then presents a key classification of 'aql into two types found among scholars. Understanding this division is essential for grasping how Islamic epistemology views the relationship between innate capacity and acquired knowledge, a distinction that underlies many debates in Kalam and Usul al-Fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Find the Quranic definition of 'aql
Locate where the author defines 'aql as a perceiving power that distinguishes humans and makes them responsible. Note the key functions: perception and distinction between truth/falsehood, good/evil, beautiful/ugly.
This definition establishes the genus (power) and differentia (distinguishing humans).
2
Identify the Quranic terms for the instrument of 'aql
The author lists four terms used in the Quran: qalb (heart), fu'ad (inner heart), lubb (core), and nuha (understanding). Understand that these are not synonyms for 'aql itself but the tool through which 'aql functions, connecting causes and results.
These terms appear in many Quranic verses about reasoning.
3
Extract the two types of 'aql
Read the division: some scholars hold that 'aql is of two types. The first is innate (ghareezi): a potential power ready to receive sciences, likened to a palm tree in a seed. The second is acquired (mustafad): it strengthens the innate power.
The analogy emphasizes that the innate 'aql is not yet actual knowledge.
4
Understand the relationship between the two types
The acquired 'aql does not replace the innate; rather, it strengthens it. The innate is the foundation, and the acquired builds upon it through learning and experience.
This relationship is crucial for theories of knowledge acquisition.
5
Connect to the Quranic verse
The acquired 'aql is identified with the 'heard' 'aql in the verse from Surah Ankabut (43): 'And none comprehend it except the knowledgeable.' This shows that true comprehension requires both innate capacity and acquired learning.
The verse supports the necessity of effort in attaining understanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجماع القول في نهاية الحديث عن تعريف العقل - أن العقل في اللغة وفي القرآن الكريم قوة مدركه في الإنسان، تميزه عن سواه من الكائنات، و تجعل منه مخلوقاً مسؤولاً عن أعماله على أساس قدرته على الإدراك و التمييز بين الحق والباطل، والخير والشر، والحسن والقبيح. وأنّ القرآن يطلق ألفاظ القلب أو الفؤاد أو اللب أو النهى على الأداة أو الآلة التي تقوم بوظيفة العقل، أو الربط وإيجاد العلاقة بين الأسباب و النتائج (1) . أقسام العقل. يرى بعض العلماء أن العقل قسمان: الأول غريزي: وهو قوة متهيئة لقبول العلوم، ووجوده في الطفل كوجود النخلة في النواة، والسنبلة في الحبة. الثاني مستفاد: وهو الذي تتقوى به تلك القوه الغريزية في القسم الأول(۲). ونسب إلى علي - رضي الله عنه - قوله: العقل عقلان: [؟] مطبوع و[؟] كما لا ينفع ضوء الشمس وضوء العين ممنوع(۳). والعقل المسموع هو المكتسب للمعرفة، وهو المشار إليه في قوله تعالى: ﴿وَما يَعْقِلُها إلا العالِمُونَ ﴾ [العنكبوت: ٤٣/٢٩].
And the sum of the statement at the end of the discussion on the definition of 'aql is that 'aql in language and in the Noble Quran is a perceiving power in man, distinguishing him from other creatures, and making him a responsible being for his actions based on his ability to perceive and distinguish between truth and falsehood, good and evil, and the beautiful and ugly. And that the Quran uses the terms heart (qalb), inner heart (fu'ad), core (lubb), or understanding (nuha) for the instrument or tool that performs the function of 'aql, or the connection and establishing the relationship between causes and results (1). The divisions of 'aql: Some scholars hold that 'aql is of two types: first, innate: it is a power prepared to receive sciences, and its existence in the child is like the existence of the palm tree in the seed, and the ear of grain in the grain. Second, acquired: it is that by which that innate power in the first type is strengthened (2). And it is attributed to 'Ali - may Allah be pleased with him - his saying: 'Aql is two 'aqls: [؟] innate and [؟] just as the light of the sun and the light of the eye are of no benefit when the eye is prevented (3). And the heard 'aql is the one acquired for knowledge, and it is referred to in His saying: 'And none comprehend it except the knowledgeable' [Ankabut 43].
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage concludes the discussion on the definition of 'aql and introduces its division. The author first summarizes the Quranic view: 'aql is a perceiving power that distinguishes humans and makes them morally responsible. The Quran uses terms like qalb, fu'ad, lubb, and nuha interchangeably for the instrument of 'aql, which connects causes and effects. Then the author presents a classification of 'aql into two types found among scholars. The first is innate (ghareezi): a potential power ready to receive knowledge, likened to a palm tree in a seed or an ear in a grain. The second is acquired (mustafad): it strengthens the innate power through learning. A saying attributed to 'Ali reinforces this duality, though the OCR is corrupted. The acquired 'aql corresponds to the 'heard' 'aql mentioned in the Quranic verse 'none comprehend it except the knowledgeable,' indicating that true understanding requires both innate capacity and acquired learning.

العقل المستفاد (al-'aql al-mustafad)
القلب (al-qalb)

Key Takeaway
The Quran defines 'aql as a perceiving power that makes humans responsible, and scholars divide it into innate potential and acquired knowledge that strengthens it.

Quranic Definition of 'Ulu al-Albab: The Possessors of Sound Intellect
Author defines 'ulu al-albab' as possessors of intellect who understand the Quran and wisdom.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key characteristics of 'ulu al-albab as described in the Quran and explain their significance for Islamic epistemology.

Core Idea
Quranic 'ulu al-albab are those with sound intellects who comprehend revelation, wisdom, and follow the best sayings.

The Quran frequently praises a group called 'ulu al-albab. But who are they? In this passage, the author draws from multiple Quranic verses to construct a profile of these intellectually preeminent individuals. Understanding this profile is crucial because it defines the ideal epistemic agent in Islam—one who combines intellect with faith and follows the best of arguments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic verses cited
List the five verses the author uses (3:7, 2:269, 13:19, 14:52, 39:18). For each, note what attribute of 'ulu al-albab is highlighted.
2
Extract the common attributes
From each verse, extract one key characteristic: comprehension of Quranic meanings, receiving wisdom, distinguishing truth from falsehood, knowing the purpose of revelation, and following the best of sayings.
3
Synthesise the definition
Combine all attributes into a single coherent description of 'ulu al-albab: possessors of sound intellect who understand the Quran and wisdom, distinguish truth, know revelation's purpose, and follow the best guidance.
4
Apply the definition to an example
Consider a scholar of usul al-fiqh who uses rational reasoning to derive rulings while adhering to the Quran and Sunnah. Would they qualify as 'ulu al-albab? Justify using the attributes.
This connects the definition to a real Islamic science.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثالث: الفصل الثاني - العقل
برجاحة العقل، ولذلك فقد أثنى القرآن الكريم على العقلاء بصيغة أولا الألباب في غير موضع، وفي ذلك حث ضمني على بلوغ مرتبة الرجاحة العقلية تلك:
فالعقلاء (أولو العقول الراجحات) هم الذين يدركون معاني القرآن وحقائق العلم:
هُوَ الَّذِي أَنْزَلَ عَلَيْكَ الْكِتابَ مِنْهُ آيَاتٌ مُحْكَمَاتٌ هُنَّ أُمُّ الْكِتَابِ وَأَخَرُ مُتَشابهات فَأَمَّا الَّذِينَ فِي قُلُوبهمْ زَيْغٌ فَيَبعُونَ مَا تَشابَهَ مِنْهُ ابْتِغَاءَ الْفِتْنَةِ وَابْتِغاءَ تَأْوِيلِهِ وَمَا يَعْلَمُ تَأْوِيلَهُ إِلَّا اللهُ وَالرّاسِخُونَ فِي الْعِلْمِ يَقُولُونَ آمَنَا بِهِ كُلٌّ مِنْ عِندِ رَبَّنَا وَمَا يَذَّكَّرُ إِلا أُولُو الأَلْباب [آل عمران: ٢٧/٣].
ولا يعرف الحكمة وحقيقتها ويدرك أهميتها إلا أولو الألباب: يُؤْتِي الْحِكْمَةَ مَنْ يَشَاءُ وَمَنْ يُؤْتَ الْحِكْمَةَ فَقَدْ أُوتِيَ خَيْراً كَثِيراً وَمَا يَذكرُ إِلا أُولُو الألباب) (البقرة: ٢٦٩/٢].
وأولو الألباب هم وحدهم الذين يعون حقيقة الفرق بين العلم والجهل، أو النور والظلام: أَفَمَنْ يَعْلَمُ أَنَّما أُنْزِلَ إِلَيْكَ مِنْ رَبِّكَ الْحَقُّ كَمَنْ هُوَ أَعْمَى إِنَّمَا يَتَذَكَّرُ أُولُو الألباب كم [الرعد: ۱۹/۱۳].
وأولو الألباب هم الذين يعلمون غاية الوحي ومقاصده: هَذا بَلاغ لِلنَّاسِ وَلِيُنْذَرُوا بِهِ وَلِيَعْلَمُوا أَنَّما هُوَ إِلَهٌ وَاحِدٌ وَلِيَذَّكَّرَ أُولُو الألباب [إبراهيم: ٥٢/١٤].
ويتميز أولو الألباب كذلك بالربط بين معارفهم النظرية وإيمانهم عن طريق اتباع أرشد الأقوال وأحسنها انبثاقاً من حسهم الجمالي الذي يتمتعون بتذوقه: الَّذِينَ يَسْتَمِعُونَ الْقَوْلَ فَيَتَّبِعُونَ أَحْسَنَهُ أُولَئِكَ الَّذِينَ هَدَاهُمُ اللهُ وَأُولَئِكَ هُمْ أُولُو الأَلْباب ﴾ [الزمر: ١٨/٣٩].
وهذا يدلّ بالتأكيد على أن من المفترض أن تتوجّه السياسات التعليمية المنبثقة عن التربية الإسلامية إلى تكريم ذوي التفوق العقلي من المتعلمين، وأن تولي المناهج التعليمية اهتماماً أكبر بجوانب التربية العقلية، كما ينبغي أن تتاح فرص لتقديم الأنشطة ذات الطابع العقلي من ثقافية وفكرية وسواهما، وأن تُقدّم الحوافز الدافعة لدعم ذلك التفاعل، وتلك الأنشطة.
Chapter Three, Section Two - The Intellect. Due to the preponderance of the intellect, the Noble Quran has praised the intelligent using the phrase 'ulu al-albab' in more than one place, and in that is an implicit encouragement to reach that level of intellectual preponderance. So the intelligent (those with preponderant intellects) are the ones who comprehend the meanings of the Quran and the realities of knowledge: 'It is He who has sent down to you the Book; in it are verses definitive...' [3:7]. And no one knows wisdom and its reality and grasps its importance except ulu al-albab: 'He gives wisdom to whom He wills, and whoever is given wisdom has been given much good...' [2:269]. And ulu al-albab are the only ones who comprehend the reality of the difference between knowledge and ignorance, or light and darkness: 'Is he who knows that what is revealed to you from your Lord is truth like him who is blind? Only those with understanding will remember' [13:19]. And ulu al-albab are the ones who know the purpose and objectives of revelation: 'This is a message for mankind, that they may be warned thereby and know that He is but one God, and that those of understanding may take heed' [14:52]. And ulu al-albab are also distinguished by linking their theoretical knowledge with their faith through following the most guided and best of sayings, emanating from their aesthetic sense that they enjoy: 'Those who listen to the word and follow the best of it; those are the ones Allah has guided, and those are the people of understanding' [39:18]. This surely indicates that educational policies emanating from Islamic education should be directed toward honoring those with intellectual excellence among learners, and that curricula should pay greater attention to aspects of intellectual education, and that opportunities should be provided for intellectual activities, cultural and intellectual and otherwise, and that motivating incentives should be given to support that interaction and those activities.
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the Quranic concept of 'aql (intellect) and its possessors, termed 'ulu al-albab' (possessors of intellects). The author begins by stating that the Quran praises the intelligent using the phrase 'ulu al-albab' in multiple verses, implying an encouragement to attain intellectual excellence. The term 'ulu al-albab' is then defined as those who possess preponderant intellects and comprehend the meanings of the Quran and the realities of knowledge. The author cites five Quranic verses to illustrate the characteristics and virtues of ulu al-albab. First, from Surah Al-Imran (3:7), they are the ones who understand the definitive and ambiguous verses and affirm faith in all of them. Second, from Surah Al-Baqarah (2:269), they are the ones who receive wisdom, which is a great good. Third, from Surah Ar-Ra'd (13:19), they distinguish between knowledge and ignorance, truth and falsehood. Fourth, from Surah Ibrahim (14:52), they comprehend the purpose of revelation. Fifth, from Surah Az-Zumar (39:18), they listen to sayings and follow the best, linking knowledge and faith through an aesthetic sense. The passage concludes by drawing a practical implication: Islamic educational policies should honor intellectually outstanding students, emphasize intellectual education in curricula, and provide incentives for intellectual activities.

Key Terms
العقل
أولو الألباب
الحكمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which quality is attributed to 'ulu al-albab in Surah Az-Zumar (39:18)?
A) They know the interpretation of ambiguous verses.
B) They listen to the word and follow the best of it.
C) They receive wisdom from Allah.
D) They perceive the difference between light and darkness.

Key Takeaway
The Quran defines 'ulu al-albab as those with sound intellects who comprehend revelation, wisdom, distinguish truth, and follow the best guidance, making them the ideal epistemic agents in Islam.
